Overview
For a general overview of the Dayforce Implementation Guide, see the following topics:
About the Dayforce Implementation Guide
Dayforce Implementation - Overview of the Key Tasks
About the Dayforce Implementation Guide
The Dayforce Implementation Guide provides an overview of the process for implementing and
configuring Dayforce. This guide contains general information about workforce performance
management. It also covers the various concepts, rules, codes, and other elements required for
Dayforce to function, as well as the detailed steps that implementation consultants and other
administrators need to know and perform to configure Dayforce.
This guide assumes that you have access to an instance of Dayforce, and that your role has
access to the features, access authorizations, and elements in the user interface (UI) described in
this guide. Note that some topics describe procedures, or user interface elements, that are only
visible to users with a Support or Service level user role, which is reserved for Dayforce service
and support personnel. These topics and UI elements are clearly marked, and you can contact
your Dayforce representative for more information.
The audience for this guide includes:
Dayforce Implementation Consultants
Dayforce Implementation Partners
Dayforce Resellers
Client System Administrators or other technical staff
Note: Some of the new or updated features in this release might not yet be localized for French or
for the other languages supported in Dayforce. Translation efforts for this content are ongoing.
Also, because Dayforce is highly customizable, some of the features and options discussed in this
guide might not be visible when you access Dayforce. To confirm your access, contact your
organization’s Dayforce administrator.
Dayforce Implementation - Overview of the Key Tasks

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 106 of 0

Dayforce Implementation Guide

Application Configuration
This section describes how to define important application-wide settings that are applied to a
Dayforce site. If you are administering more than one site, each site (or client) can have its own
settings.
Note: For your privacy and security, Dayforce terminates your session and logs you out if your
session is idle or inactive for 30 minutes.
Site Setup
In the Site Setup feature in Dayforce, you can view and set up organization-specific information,
client (customer) details, culture settings, and image files for logos used by the organization, on
checks and earning statements, as well as signatures used on checks.
Before You Begin: Some of the fields or features described in this topic might be available only to
users with Support or Service roles. For more information, contact your implementation consultant.
Depending on how your organization is configured, the Site Setup can have the following
subfeatures:
Client: Contains identifying information about the organization, name, namespace, and
reference code. See Site Setup > Client.
Clock Devices: Lists any clocks or clock types associated with the organization. See Clock
Device Setup.
Clock Config Groups: Lists any clock configuration groups associated with the organization.
See Create Clock Configuration Groups.
Clock Configuration: Contains configuration XML information and other related information
about clocks associated with the organization. See Update Custom Clock Configurations.
Clock Surveys: Contains subfeatures that control how and when surveys appear on
Dayforce clocks in specific scenarios. For example, when configured, clocks might prompt
employees with a survey where they must select a predefined response before the clock
can approve or reject their action, such as time entry. See Clock Survey Configuration. The
following subfeatures are available under Clock Surveys:
Survey Question Setup: Contains the questions and answers that can be associated
with clock surveys in Clock Surveys > Survey Setup. This subfeature contains system-
generated questions and answers that can be associated with clock surveys.
Additionally, this subfeature also supports customized questions and answers.
Survey Setup: This subfeature is used to configure clock surveys and also contains all
available clock surveys.
Clock Survey Groups: Contains options to configure clock survey groups which can be
used to associate surveys with specific clock devices. See Create Clock Survey Groups.

-- 107 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 108 of 0
Clock Update Info: Contains information about software version, update repository, and log
files storage locations for any clocks associated with the organization.
LMS Configuration: Contains options for the Learning Management module configuration.
See Settings Tab in LMS Configuration.
Site Setup > Client
In Site Setup > Client, you can define organization properties such as the name and description of
your organization, as well as view information about Dayforce properties. There are three tabs for
client site information in Site Setup > Client: Properties, Cultures, and Images.
See the following topics:
Set Client Site Properties
Choose a Help Collection
Client Cultures
Add a Logo or Signature
Brand the Application
Set Client Site Properties
Client Site Properties as shown in below table
To define client settings:
1. Go to Site Setup > Client.
2. In the Properties tab, modify the client site properties by entering values in the various fields
(as shown in the table below).
3. Click Save.
Client site properties
Property 	Purpose
Identity
Name 	The name of your organization’s client site. There is a 64-character limit.
Description 	The description for your organization’s client site.
Help Collection 	Drop-down list with options for online help for your client site.

-- 108 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 109 of 0
Reference Code Used in imports and exports. See Cross-Reference Codes.
Namespace Dayforce assigned designation that uniquely identifies your organization’s
client site.
First Day of
Week
First day for the week for your organization. This day is displayed in
calendars.
Business
Day Start Time of day at which your organization’s business day starts.
Trade Name 	General name for your organization used instead of the legal name.
Software
This section contains information about your Dayforce clock’s log files and
software version, if available.
Note: When the Start Day of Week parameter in Org Setup > Organization > General hasn’t been
specified in the org setup for a user's primary location, Dayforce uses the configuration specified
in the First Day of Week parameter. If Start Day of Week and First Day of Week have been
specified, Dayforce uses Start Day of Week. If both the Start Day of Week and First Day of Week
aren't specified, Dayforce uses Sunday as the first day of the week.
Choose a Help Collection
You can select which Help Collection Dayforce opens when users click the Help buttons (?)
throughout Dayforce. Help is available in two formats: standard help, and the interactive MyPath
training platform.
Note: MyPath training is included in most Dayforce implementations. Before January 2018, you
had to have bought MyPath for it to be part of your implementation.
To change which help collection Dayforce uses, in the Properties tab of Site Setup > Client, select
one of the following options from the Help Collection drop-down list. Select the option that most
closely resembles your organization's Dayforce configuration:
Standard Help
MyPath Standard
MyPath Standard Canada
MyPath PowerPay

Release notes
Add a Logo or Signature
You can upload logos and signature images that are shown on benefit summaries, earning
statements, and US checks in Site Setup > Client, in the Images tab.
When you add a logo or signature image, you can select one of the following Image Type choices
for the image:
Benefit Summary Logo
Check Signature US : This option is available for the United States only. This option is used
for normal and additional checks, as well as onsite checks that don’t use pre-printed check
stock. This option also allows you to add an image of a signature to be used when you print
onsite checks using pre-printed onsite check stock. See Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity
and Client Properties - Payroll.
Client Branding Logo: This option shows as the branded logo in the toolbar if Dayforce is
configured to show it. See Brand the Application.
Compensation Logo
ESS Earning Statement Canada
ESS Earning Statement Legal Entity: This option allows you to assign a logo that can
override any logo assigned to a country in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity,
where logo names are set up in images and available for selection.
ESS Earning Statement US
Login Screen Logo
Performance Logo
Printed Earning Statement Logo US: This option also shows as the employer logo on printed
checks.
Recruiting Logo
Each image type is subject to specific criteria:
Check Signature US images and Printed Earning Statement US logo images must be in
JPG or PNG format.
Dimensions for Check Signature US images and Printed Earning Statement US logo images
must be 600 x 225 pixels with a resolution of 300 DPI (dots per inch).
Note: For best results, you should upload black and white images for printed earning statement
logos, check signatures, and check logos.
To add logos or signatures:
1. Go to Site Setup > Client and click the Images tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description of the logo.

-- 115 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 116 of 0
4. In the Image Type drop-down list, select the image type according to the document in which
the image will appear.
5. Enter a start date and, optionally, an end date to have Dayforce use the selected image
type for a specific period of time.
6. (Optional) Enter a comment.
7. In the Edit Image drop-down list, click Upload.
8. In the File Upload dialog box, select the file type and image file and then click Open.
Dayforce uploads the selected image file and shows a preview of it in the Image section.
9. Note: You can upload only JPG and PNG files.
9. Click Save.
Brand the Application
You can further customize Dayforce by displaying your organization's logo in the toolbar, to the
right of the menu icon. The branding property is enabled by default. When you log in to Dayforce,
the application shows your company logo on the login screen and the main toolbar by default.
To upload a branding logo:
1. Go to Site Setup > Client and click the Images tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description of the logo.
4. In the Image Type drop-down list, click Client Branding Logo.
5. Enter a start date and, optionally, an end date to have Dayforce use the selected image for
a specific period of time.
6. (Optional) Enter a comment.
7. In the Edit Image drop-down list, click Upload.
8. Select the file type and the appropriate image file and click Open. Dayforce uploads the
selected image file and shows a preview of it in the Image section.
9. Note: You can upload only JPG and PNG files.
9. Click Save.
Important: When users accessing Dayforce with a Hub-enabled role click the logo, it navigates to
Hub or Home, depending on what is configured. The logo is either your company logo, if you
uploaded one, or the Dayforce logo.

Enter Contact Information
In System Admin > Client Properties, in the Contacts tab, you can set various contacts for your
organization. For example, the contacts that receive the delivery packages generated by
Dayforce, Inc.. Delivery packages can be sent to multiple contacts in the organization and can
contain reports, direct deposit pay stubs, or physical checks to be distributed. You can also set
other contact types here, including ROE Contacts and ROE Issuers (for Canadian payroll).
To enter contacts for an organization:
1. Go to System Admin > Client Properties.
2. In the Contacts tab, click Add.
3. In the Contact Type drop-down list, select the type of contact you're configuring.
4. Enter the contact details using the available fields and drop-down lists.
5. In the Communication Type drop-down list, select the contact's communication type.
Select Customer Support/Year End to receive emails from the Support team regarding
year end activities.
No other types are used at this time.
6. Click Save.
Add an ROE Issuer or ROE Contact
Canadian ROE forms require you to enter the name and contact information of the person in your
organization who can provide more information about the ROE form, if needed. According to
Service Canada, an ROE contact should be able to provide information about the reason for
issuing the ROE, and an ROE issuer should be able to answer questions about the information on
the ROE.
You need to add people and their contact details in Dayforce so that this information appears on
the generated ROE forms.
To add a person as an ROE issuer or an ROE contact for the organization:
1. Add the ROE contact assignment role feature to the user role that is used to configure the
ROE contacts and issuers.
a. Go to System Admin > Roles and select a role in the list.
b. Click the Features tab.
c. Under Payroll Setup, select the ROE Contact Assignment checkbox.
d. Click Save.

-- 118 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 119 of 0
2. Go to System Admin > Client Properties and click the Contacts tab.
3. Click Add.
4. In the Contact Type drop-down list, select ROE Issuer or ROE Contact.
5. Add the contact name, phone, country, and language details in their respective fields.
6. In the Communication Type drop-down list, select All to receive emails from the Dayforce
support team about product updates.
7. Click Save.
8. To make this person the default ROE issuer or contact for the organization (if you previously
added a default issuer or contact and do not want to change this setup, you can skip this
step):
a. Go to Payroll Setup > ROE Contact Assignment.
b. Expand ROE Contacts or ROE Issuers and select the contact that you just added.
Under Assignment, select the Default checkbox.
c. Click Save.
You can also assign ROE issuers and contacts to specific pay groups so that ROE forms list
specific contact information for different pay groups. See Configure Multiple ROE Contact
Assignments.
Configure Multiple ROE Contact Assignments
An organization can have more than one person who issues ROE forms or who is designated as
the ROE contact. In Dayforce, you can assign multiple pay groups to one person, assign specific
pay groups to specific people, or delegate a default ROE contact and ROE issuer for all pay
groups. A default ROE contact and issuer ensures pay groups without an assigned contact or
issuer will not be overlooked. See Add an ROE Issuer or ROE Contact.
For example, if your organization has four pay groups (A, B, C, and D):
You can assign person X to be the ROE contact and issuer for pay groups A and B.
Person Y isn’t only assigned as the default contact and issuer for the organization, they are
also the contact and issuer for the pay group C.
Pay group D does not have a contact or issuer assigned to it. Because person Y is the
default ROE contact and issuer for the organization, this means person Y will be listed as a
contact and issuer for pay group D.
For more information on working with ROEs in Payroll, see Record of Employment (ROE) in the
Payroll Administrator Guide.
You can configure either the ROE contact or ROE issuer in the ROE Contact Assignment screen
by clicking Payroll Setup > ROE Contact Assignment.
To configure a specific ROE contact or issuer to one or more pay groups:

-- 119 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 120 of 0
1. Add the ROE contact assignment role feature to the user role that is used to configure the
ROE contacts and issuers:
a. Go to System Admin > Roles and select a role in the list.
b. Click the Features tab.
c. Under Payroll Setup, select the ROE Contact Assignment checkbox.
d. Click Save.
2. Add the contact details in System Admin > Client Properties in the Contacts tab. See Add
an ROE Issuer or ROE Contact.
3. Go to Payroll Setup > ROE Contact Assignment.
4. Assign one or more pay groups to an ROE contact:
a. Expand ROE Contacts and select the assignee.
b. Under Assignment, in Pay Groups, select one or more pay groups.
5. Assign one or more pay groups to an ROE issuer:
a. Expand ROE Issuers and select the assignee.
b. Under Assignment, in Pay Groups, select one or more pay groups.
6. Click Save.

The Display rounding informational message checkbox is selected.
The Display Time Decimal Precision client property is set to either 1 (##.#), 2 (##.##), or 3
(##.###).

Enable HR Event on HR Import
Select this checkbox for HR imports to be able to trigger the New Hire/Rehire and Assignment
Changed HR events. This checkbox is cleared by default.
See Events Triggered by HR Import.
HR Import Event Threshold in Days
Enter a value to place a boundary on how far back an update in the import can go to trigger the
above HR events. This is evaluated as follows:
For new hires and rehires, Dayforce looks at the Hire Date field in the import file.
For work assignment changes Dayforce looks at the date that the primary work assignment
record changed.
This client property is set to 0 by default so that updates only trigger an HR event if they are on
the date that the import is run or future dated.
For example, you leave this field set to zero and run an HR import on February 17, 2020. The
import includes employees with the following hire dates:
Steve, hired on February 16, 2020
Erin, hired on February 17, 2020
Kyle, hired on February 18, 2020
As a result, the HR event is only triggered for Erin and Kyle, and not for Steve, whose hire date
falls outside of the threshold.
Continuing this example, if you enter 7 in this field, all three employees are included. In this case,
hires, rehires, and assignment changes in the file that occurred on February 10, 2020 and onward
can have an event triggered for them.
Note: The HR Import Event Threshold in Days field accepts negative values, but entering a
negative value sets the system to only generate events for items with an effective date in the
future.
See Events Triggered by HR Import.
Company Code
Specifies the code used to identify the company in some exports. The Company Code client
property is only used for integrating with specific products and can be left blank.

-- 124 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 125 of 0
End Dates Required on Secondary HR Records
Controls whether users need to provide an effective end date when adding secondary records in
the Work > Work Assignments screen in People. When selected, users can’t save secondary
records in People without specifying a date in the Effective To field. When cleared, Dayforce
doesn’t enforce this requirement.
HR Import Auto Generates Config Data
Note: If your organization uses Position Management this client property isn’t applicable to
position assignments, because position work assignments have preconfigured locations.
Controls whether the HR Import interface automatically generates missing configuration data if it’s
being assigned by the import. This data can be jobs, departments, job assignments, employment
statuses, employment status reasons, and pay classes. If an import file contains entries for any of
this data that are missing in Dayforce, the items are automatically created and then assigned to
the employee. For example, in the HR Import, several employees are being assigned the Head
Cashier job, but this job hasn’t yet been created in Dayforce. With the new configuration enabled,
Dayforce creates the Head Cashier job and then assigns it to the employees specified in the HR
Import.
When selected, Dayforce creates the configuration data listed above if it’s specified in the import
file but missing in Dayforce. When cleared, the import doesn't create new data. Instead, records
that attempt to assign items that don’t exist in Dayforce fail.
Client Operating Locations
Configures Dayforce to show labels based on where the organization is located. For example, if all
locations are in the United States, Dayforce can show State and SSN labels, while if all locations
are in Canada, Dayforce can show Province and SIN labels in the associated fields.
The selection controls address labels in People, the New Hire form, and in workflow forms with
address information. It also affects references to Social Security information in the Personal
> Confidential Information screen in People, the New Hire form, and in corresponding workflow
forms.
The drop-down list contains the following options:
Canada: Locations operate only in Canada. Labels reference “Provinces” and “Postal
Codes” in address fields and “SIN” in personal details. When users specify addresses in
People or in workflow forms, Dayforce populates the Province drop-down list with only the
provinces of Canada.
United States: Locations operate only in the United States of America. Labels reference
“States” and “ZIP Codes” in address fields and “SSN” in personal details. When users

-- 125 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 126 of 0
specify addresses in People or on workflow forms, Dayforce populates the State drop-down
list only with the states of the US.
North America: Locations operate in both the United States and Canada. Labels reference
“State/Province” and “Zip / Postal Code” in address fields and “SSN / SIN” in personal
details. When users specify addresses in People or in workflow forms, Dayforce populates
the State/Province drop-down list with Canadian provinces and states of the US.
International: Locations operate worldwide. Dayforce labels reference “State/Province” and
“Zip / Postal Code” in address fields and “National ID Number” in personal details. When
users specify addresses in People or in workflow forms, Dayforce populates the
State/Province drop-down list with Canadian provinces, states of the US, the UK, Germany,
Mexico, Netherlands, Italy, Czech Republic, Japan, China, India, Poland, and Korea.
Respect Client Operating Locations for Non-Primary Contact Information
Controls whether Dayforce allows international address and contact information for employees'
non-primary records. By default, the checkbox is selected and Dayforce restricts address and
contact information to the locations selected in the Client Operating Locations drop-down list.
Clear the checkbox and Dayforce shows additional options in the State/Province and Country
drop-down lists in address and contact records.
Hide displayed zero values
Controls whether Dayforce suppresses the display of zero dollar figures. If a field, report, row, or
column would show $0, Dayforce can be configured to substitute the value with a special
character or simply a blank. When selected, Dayforce shows the characters specified in the Text
to replace hidden zero values with field. If you leave the field blank, the $0 is replaced with a
blank.
Text to replace hidden zero values with
Controls what characters are shown instead of zero dollar figures; only used if the Hide displayed
zero values property is selected. If left blank and the Hide displayed zero values property is
selected, $0 is replaced with a blank.
Default Job Assignment Display
Controls the default setting of the Display Job Assignment As drop-down list in the view options of
Timesheets and the Grid View of Schedules. Select Job Name to hide the department names on
shift labels by default; select Department Name Job Name to show the full department and job
name by default.

Suppress from HR Export changes made by HR Import
Controls whether Dayforce exports delta changes made to employee records through the

Limit Work Assignments by Budget
Controls whether Dayforce limits work assignments based on the number entered in the Budget

When the limit is reached for a location, the job assignment isn’t available to assign to the
employee in the following areas:
Custom and system XML forms that have the Location and Job Assignment fields.
The Work > Work Assignments screen in the People feature.
For example, if a job assignment’s limit is reached for the location that you select in the Location
and Job Assignment section of the New Hire form, that job assignment isn’t available to select.
Restrict Job Assignment - Location Assignment To Physical Locations
Controls whether job assignments can be assigned to any organizational unit in the hierarchy, or if
job assignments are restricted to locations that are configured with the Physical Location
checkbox selected in the General subtab of the Organization tab in Org Setup > Organization.
Select the checkbox, and job assignments can only be assigned to physical locations. Clear the
checkbox, and job assignments can be assigned to any location in the organizational hierarchy.
Preferred Time Zone
Select the time zone that Dayforce uses for scheduling background jobs. With a time zone
selected, when system administrators schedule background jobs for specific times, Dayforce
schedules the job to run at the specified time in the time zone selected in this setting, regardless
of the time zone of the user’s computer or the server. For example, select Pacific Standard Time
and when a system administrator schedules a background job to run at 4:00 PM, Dayforce runs
the job at 4:00 PM Pacific Standard Time, even if the system administrator schedules the job from
a computer in a different time zone.

TAFW auto select shifts
Controls whether Dayforce automatically unfills or deletes shifts in Approvals that overlap with an
employee’s approved time away from work request. When selected, Dayforce automatically
removes the shift from the employee’s schedule (either by deleting or unfilling it, depending on
how Dayforce is configured) when managers approve a request. If the TAFW auto select shifts
checkbox isn’t selected, managers need to manually select the shifts they want to delete or unfill
in the Edit Schedule dialog box.
TAFW Search Result Limit
The number of time away from work requests that Dayforce loads in Approvals.
Note: When you search using the Employee Name field in the Filter & Sort panel, Dayforce
respects the Employee Search Result Limit field (also configured in the General section of the
Properties tab in System Admin > Client Properties) instead of the TAFW Search Result Limit field.
For example, with the Employee Search Result Limit field set to 15, and the TAFW Search Result
Limit field to set 100, Dayforce only returns results if you select 15 or fewer employees.
TAFW Alert/Reports Show By
Controls how Dayforce shows time in the Pending Time Off Request Alert and the Employee TAFW
Report. The following options are available:
Elapsed: Dayforce shows elapsed time in the alert and report. For example, an employee
has a shift rotation of Monday to Friday, with Saturday and Sunday off. The employee
schedules time off starting on a Friday, and ending on a Monday. With this option selected,
the alert and report show a duration of four days
Scheduled: Dayforce shows scheduled time in the alert and report. Continuing the example
above, the alert and report show a duration of two days.
Approvals Max Employees Search Limit
Specifies the limit for employee search results in Approvals. For example, if you enter 100 in this
field and then perform a search that yields more than 100 employees, a message is shown to

indicate that the search can't be completed because it exceeds the search limit. To complete the

Run Pay Engine on Punch Import
Selected by default. Dayforce runs the pay rule engine on every out clock entry and injected meal
during the import. To reduce the import time for files that contain a large number of clock entries,
administrators can clear this checkbox to prevent the engine from running.
Run Pay Engine on Pay Adjustment Import
By default, this checkbox is selected and Dayforce runs the pay rule engine after the Employee
Pay Adjustment Import runs. Dayforce also runs the Pay Summary Recalc background job for all
of the records in the import file.
By default, the Pay Summary Recalc background job processes the records one at a time. If the
File size (no. of records) threshold client property is configured with a value and the import file has
more records than this value, then its records are processed all at once. Otherwise, the records
are processed one at a time.
Clear this checkbox and the pay rule engine doesn’t run after the Employee Pay Adjustment
Import runs. The Pay Summary Recalc background job also doesn’t run. This reduces the import
time for files with a large number of pay adjustments.
If your organization has a large number of employees, it’s recommended that you clear this client
property to reduce the import time. For example, if your import file contains more than 500 pay
adjustments, this client property—if enabled—can impact Dayforce performance when running
the import. You could also ask Dayforce Support to set an appropriate value in the File size (no. of
records) threshold client property to improve the processing time for large import files.
File size (no. of records) threshold
Before You Begin: You need to contact Dayforce Support to ask for this field to be updated.
Specify the number of records there should be in an import file for Dayforce to run the Pay
Summary Recalc background job for all of the records in an import file instead of one record at a
time. By default, this field is set to 0.
When the Run Pay Engine on Pay Adjustment Import client property is selected and a value is
configured in this field, the Pay Summary Recalc background job processes all the records in an
import file at once when there are more records in the file than the value configured in this field. If

-- 130 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 131 of 0
the number of records in an import file are less than the value configured in this field, the
Pay Summary Recalc background job processes each record one at a time.

Show Affiliate Promotions
When selected, Dayforce shows an Intuit TurboTax promotional offer when US employees view
their W-2 forms in Earnings > Year End Forms. This feature is designed as an opportunity for
customers to offer their employees a way to potentially save money on their taxes. By default, this

disable this, clear the Show Affiliate Promotions checkbox, click Save, and then click Refresh.
Basic Business Day Calculation
This checkbox is selected by default, and Dayforce uses the basic calculation method to
determine business day alignment time (BDA). The basic method applies the BDA settings
configured at the pay group level first, and if the employee’s pay group doesn't have a BDA

-- 132 of 472 --

configured, then it applies the organization-level BDA settings. If there is no BDA specified at the

1. Shift rotation
2. Pay group

Default Value for User Property “Display24HourTime” via HR Import
Controls which time display format employees receive when they are created using the HR Import:
24-hour time or 12-hour time. The options are as follows:
True: Applies the 24-hour time format to new employees imported by the HR Import.
False: Applies the 12-hour time format to new employees imported by the HR Import.
By default, this property has no option selected and new imported employees receive the 24-hour
time format. However, if you select False for this property, the HR Import applies the 12-hour time
format to the new employees it imports. If you later want to go back to the 24-hour time format,
you can select True.

Days to load SL without prompt
Silverlight loads in Dayforce for the following three reasons:
When a role uses Silverlight features.
When a role is associated with workflows or forms that use Silverlight.
When Dayforce detects in the back end that a user’s activity requires Silverlight.
This property addresses the last point above. When Dayforce detects that a user’s activity
requires Silverlight, an entry is made in the database in the backend and Silverlight loads in
Dayforce. By default, the expiration for a user session is 30 days and administrators can reduce or
increase the value based on the user’s needs. If the value is reduced, and there are days
remaining for the user’s session, the expiration for the user’s session is updated the next time the
user logs in. If the value is reduced, and there are no days remaining for the user’s session,
Silverlight won't load.
End date non-primary work assignments upon termination on HR Import
Select this checkbox to end-date existing active non-primary work assignments as of employee
termination dates when terminating employees via the HR Import. Non-primary work assignments
that start after the termination date are deleted.

Delegation Duration Maximum (in Days)
Enter a number in this field to limit the number of days for which a delegation can be configured.
Enter a value between 1 and 999999999 to restrict the delegation access duration. Dayforce
treats the value 0 in the same way as there being no value entered, and delegations will have no
duration restriction. The default value in the field is 0.
Important: You can enter and save values between -999999999 and 999999999. It’s important that
you only enter values between 0 and 999999999 in this field because Dayforce only validates that
a value within this range has been entered when you’re configuring delegation access elsewhere
in Dayforce.

Assign employee to all matching departments on HR Import when org assignment is above site

When you select this checkbox, and the OrgUnitXrefCode in the HR import file is above store
level, then the import looks at the child org units under the OrgUnitXrefCode to find a

assigned to the org unit that matches the department.
When you select this checkbox, and the OrgUnitXrefCode in the HR Import is at or below store
level, then the import finds the matching department at the onsite department level and assigns
the employee to that department.

Enter the amount that compensation can be increased in the Job Assignment and Compensation
form before a validation is triggered. By default, this value is 10,000,000.
Generate Base Rate Transactions
This setting controls whether Dayforce can detect and commit base rate transactions after you run
the Base Rate Recalc background job.
Select this checkbox to include base rate transactions in base rate recalculations. This includes
both system-generated base rate updates and manual base rate updates made in the Work
> Base Rate Progression screen of People.
Clear this checkbox and Dayforce ignores both system-generated and manual transactions
during base rate recalculation. This checkbox is cleared by default. It’s recommended that you
don’t enable this client property if your organization doesn't use the Dayforce base rate
progression features, because it might affect the performance of the background job engine.

Select this checkbox to show the Indicate Shared Employees checkbox in the Options panel in
Schedules and Timesheets. When the Indicate Shared Employees checkbox is selected, Dayforce
shows the shared employee icon ( ) next to employees who work at the selected location on a
secondary work assignment.
Enable activity based costing
When you select this checkbox, you can assign the system-generated Activity labor metric to time
entry policies and default labor records in the Labor Metrics tab of Pay Setup > Time Entry Policy
and in the Work > Default Labor screen of People. When this checkbox is cleared, Dayforce hides
the Activity labor metric in these locations and makes it unavailable for time entry policy and
default labor configuration.
Disable auto update of Most Recent Hire date
When an employee’s employment status transitions from Terminated to Active, Dayforce
automatically updates the Most Recent Hire Date field to match the start date of the new Active
status. Employment status transitions can be triggered by HR Import, forms, or when you make

Hide comments from Complex (Non-XML based) forms
Select this checkbox to hide the Comment field from complex (non-XML based) forms anywhere
that a form is shown. For example, users won't see it when they fill out the Direct Deposit form,
during any approval stage, or in the form submission history. This functionality can be used to limit
free-text communication between employees in Dayforce to prevent the sharing of sensitive data.
Comments that are in submitted forms before this checkbox is selected are retained in the
database but hidden from all areas in Dayforce.
Notes:
A complex form is a Dayforce form that has predefined content and no XML code to review
or edit. Examples include the Direct Deposit form and tax forms. In the Form Builder screen
of Workflow Administration, these forms have the IsComplexForm checkbox of the
Properties tab selected, and the XML and Preview tabs grayed-out.
In non-complex forms (forms where the XML code is editable), you can manually remove
the Comment field from the form code so that it's not available to users.

Release (ESR) version 52 browsers. Because Dayforce shows the banner by default, if you want
to hide the banner, click No. Changes take effect after the next login.
Exclude One Time Payment Bonus Form
Select this checkbox to ensure that approval requests for a custom version of the Bonus Payment
Form are only shown in Message Center.
When users submit the system version of the Bonus Payment Form that comes with Dayforce,
approvals are only shown in Message Center and not in other areas such as the Actions tab of
Home. This is because of a processing requirement for this form. However, when users submit a
custom version of this form, approvals aren't just restricted to Message Center by default, and
processing issues can occur if users approve it in other areas.
To ensure that approval requests for a custom version of a Bonus Payment Form only appear in
Message Center:
Select the Exclude One Time Payment Bonus Form checkbox.

Controls you can import a primary work assignment that has the same job, location, and

Minimum worksheets to set budget by guidelines using a background job
Enter the minimum number of compensation worksheets required to trigger a background job for
setting budgets.
If the number of worksheets exceeds this value and one or more guidelines are set based on
budgets, the Compensation Set Budget From Guidelines Job runs to set the budgets. Otherwise,
budgets are set without using the background job.
The background job also supports setting budgets by percentage or fixed amount when these
options are used together with guidelines.
By default, this field is set to a high integer.
Minimum employees to auto-allocate rewards using a background job
Enter the minimum number of employees required in compensation worksheets to enable auto-
allocation of the budget using a background job. If the number of employees exceeds this limit,
the Compensation Auto Allocation Job allocates the budget and automatically saves the
worksheet. Otherwise, when you click Auto-Allocate in compensation worksheets, Dayforce
allocates the budget without using a background job.
By default, this field is set to a high integer to allow automatic budget allocation. If you experience
issues with auto-allocation, reduce the value (the recommended setting is 500).

reward letters for multiple employees. The default value is 50. This value indicates that each ZIP
file contains 50 reward letters for a mass download. If you encounter performance issues when
downloading reward letters in bulk, enter a lower value for this client property.

Employee
The settings in the Employee section of the Properties tab in System Admin > Client Properties
deal with employee information in Dayforce.
Enable SSN Validation
Controls whether Dayforce validates the Social Security numbers (SSN) or Social Insurance
numbers (SIN) supplied for each employee in People and any new hires onboarded using the
onboarding wizard in People, or the workflow New Hire form.
The SSN validation checks whether the number is in a valid format and isn’t a duplicate of a
number already entered for an employee in Dayforce.
When the Enable SSN Validation checkbox is cleared, Dayforce doesn't validate SSNs and the
field doesn't need a valid number when onboarding employees with the onboarding wizard.
Note: The Enable SSN Validation client property must be enabled if you’re using payroll because
the Payroll functionality requires that all employees have valid SSNs.
Allow Applied for SSN
Controls whether Dayforce allows duplicate SSN values of 000-00-0000 to be entered for
employees in People, imported through the HR Imports, or saved on workflow forms, for
employees that have applied for a Social Security number but haven’t received one yet.
Note: This functionality only affects employees with a primary residence in the United States.
Allow Hiring With No SSN/SIN
When this checkbox is selected, the SSN/SIN field (or the National ID Number field in some
locations) in the Personal Details section of the Candidate Hire form isn’t required. Select this
checkbox if you’ll onboard employees before entering their SSN/SIN.
Blank SSN for Contractors
Controls whether you can onboard contractors without entering their SSN or SIN.
Enable SSN Warning Or Error Messages
Controls whether Dayforce shows an error or warning message when employees are onboarded
without a valid Social Security number (SSN) and Dayforce is configured with the Enable
SSN Validation client property selected or when employees enter dependent information without a

-- 145 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 146 of 0
valid Social Security number (SSN) and Dayforce is configured with the Enable Dependent SSN
Required at age (In Months) client property selected.
When Dayforce is configured to show error messages, the form can't be submitted with an invalid
SSN or SIN. When Dayforce is configured to show warning messages, the form can be submitted
or approved, if the warning message is approved.
Note: The Enable SSN Warning or Error Messages client property is only active if the Enable
SSN Validation checkbox is also selected.
Enable Dependent SSN Required at age (In Months)
Controls whether Dayforce validates the SSN or SIN of employees' dependents saved in Dayforce
Benefits. Specify the age, in months, at which Dayforce begins validating the SSN or SIN for
dependents. For example, enter 6 and Dayforce validates the value for any dependents older
than six months, and doesn't validate SSNs or SINs for dependents younger than six months.
If left blank, Dayforce doesn't validate SSN or SIN values for employees' dependents regardless
of age.
When you select the Enable SSN Validation checkbox and leave the Enable Dependent SSN
Required at age (In Months) field blank, Dayforce doesn’t validate the SSN field for US
dependents, or the SIN and SIN Expiry Date fields for Canadian dependents during mobile and
web enrollments.
If you select the Enable SSN Validation checkbox and enter zero in the Enable Dependent SSN
Required at age (In Months) field, Dayforce doesn't validate the SIN or SIN Expiry Date fields for
Canadian dependents. However, Dayforce continues to validate the SSN field for US dependents
during mobile and web enrollments.
Generate granular Work Assignment records via Cover Your Tracks
Controls how Dayforce generates Cover Your Tracks (CYT) work assignments. Select the
checkbox and Dayforce generates multiple individual work assignments to cover the periods
taken into consideration by CYT. Clear the checkbox and Dayforce generates only one work
assignment record to cover the periods taken into consideration by CYT. For more information
about CYT, see Cover Your Tracks Work Assignments in the HR Administration Guide.
Allow Duplicate Australian Tax File Number (TFN)
Controls whether employee profiles can have duplicate tax file numbers (TFNs). This option
provides support for cases where employees work under more than one award classification with
different pay frequencies. An employee's pay frequency in Dayforce is based on the pay group
assigned to their employment status record, and an employee can have only one active status
record at a given time. To pay these types of employees correctly, they must have a separate
employee record configured for each pay frequency. Each employee record must have the same

-- 146 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 147 of 0
TFN record on file for payroll processing, and as such, you must configure Dayforce to allow
duplicate TFNs.
When you select this checkbox, and an identification record with the TFN type is added or
updated, Dayforce doesn't need the identification number to be unique compared to other
identification records with the TFN type already in Dayforce. This functionality is in place when you
add or update records through the Identification section of the Personal > Confidential Information
screen in People, and through HR forms or the HR Import.
If you leave the Allow Duplicate Australian Tax File Number (TFN) checkbox cleared, Dayforce
continues to validate that TFN records added to Dayforce are unique. Regardless of whether the
Allow Duplicate Australian Tax File Number (TFN) checkbox is selected, Dayforce always
performs the standard TFN validation for format and length as set out by the Australian Taxation
Office.
Allow Duplicate New Zealand IRD Number
Controls whether employee profiles can have duplicate IRD numbers. This option adds support
for cases where employees work under more than one award classification with different pay
frequencies. An employee's pay frequency in Dayforce is based on the pay group assigned to
their employment status record, and an employee can only have one active status record at a
given time. To pay these types of employees correctly, they must have a separate employee
record configured for each pay frequency. Each employee record must have the same
IRD number record on file for payroll processing, and as such, you must configure Dayforce to
allow duplicate IRD numbers.
When you select this checkbox, and an identification record with the IRD Number type is added or
updated, Dayforce doesn't need the number to be unique compared to other identification
records with the IRD Number type already in Dayforce. This functionality is in place when you add
or update records through the Identification section of the Personal > Confidential Information
screen of People, and through HR forms or the HR Import.
If you leave the Allow Duplicate New Zealand IRD Number checkbox cleared, Dayforce continues
to validate that IRD number records added to Dayforce are unique. Regardless of whether the
Allow Duplicate New Zealand IRD Number checkbox is selected, Dayforce always performs the
standard IRD number validation for format and length as set out by the Inland Revenue
Department.

To help ensure the proper display of employee names, Dayforce makes the following automatic
updates to all name display formats:
Multiple spaces are compressed to a single space.
Spaces immediately before a comma are removed.
If a comma is the first character, it’s removed.
Spaces at the beginning or the end of the name after all other changes have been made
are removed to ensure that there is no whitespace.

Defines whether employee numbers are shown alongside employee names throughout Dayforce.
Select the checkbox and Dayforce appends the employee number to the end of the employee's

Number Algorithm
The algorithm used for generating new employee numbers. Set it to AUTO_UNIQUE to generate
employee numbers for employees onboarded through the HR Import or People. Set it to
USER_UNIQUE to allow users to specify their own employee numbers for new hires.
Note: The Number Algorithm field must be set to 'AUTO_UNIQUE' to use the Generate New
Employee Number functionality in the Work > Work Assignments screen of People, or
'USER_UNIQUE' for users to edit and specify employee numbers. See Generate New Employee
Numbers in the HR Administration Guide.
Reuse Rehire Previous Employee Number
Determines whether terminated employees can be reassigned their most recently assigned
employee number when they’re rehired with the same SSN or SIN as was saved previously. Select
the checkbox, and when an employee is rehired, Dayforce reassigns the employee's existing
employee number. Clear the checkbox, and the employee is assigned a new employee number
on rehire.
Important: To use this functionality, Dayforce must be configured with the Enable SSN Validation
client property selected, and the Number Algorithm set to AUTO_UNIQUE.
Allow Multiple Employees To Share The Same Employee Number
Determines whether duplicate employee numbers are permitted in the RESTful API, HR Import,
Rehire form, and user interface.
Options are:
Legacy: Preserves the default functionality where you can create duplicate numbers
through the user interface but not through HR Import. In addition, patching employees
allows duplicate employee numbers but posting employees doesn’t. This is the default
option.
On: Duplicate employee numbers are allowed in PATCH, POST, HR Import, Rehire form, and
the user interface.
Off: Duplicate employee numbers aren’t allowed in PATCH, POST, HR Import, forms, or the
user interface, including inactive employee numbers.
Important: If you select the Allow Multiple Employees To Share The Same Employee Number client
property to allow duplicate employee numbers, don’t select the Set Employee Badge to Employee
Number for New Hire client property.

-- 150 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 151 of 0
Login Algorithm
The algorithm used for generating new employee user names.
Important: These options generate user names only for employees hired through a new hire
workflow, and not for employees added to Dayforce using the HR Import.
The login algorithm options are:
Custom Format: Dayforce generates a login based on the format defined in the Login
Algorithm Custom Format client property of System Admin > Client Properties.
Note: You must configure the Login Algorithm Custom Format client property to use this
option.
Employee number: Dayforce generates a login that is the employee number of the new hire.
F.LAST: Dayforce generates a login that is the first initial of the new hire's first name and
their full last name, separated by a period. For example, the login Dayforce generates for
Margaret Parr is M.Parr.
FIRST.LAST: Dayforce generates a login that is the new hire's first name and last name,
separated by a period. For example, the login Dayforce generates for Margaret Parr is
Margaret.Parr.
LAST.FIRST: Dayforce generates a login that is the new hire's last name and first name,
separated by a period. For example, the login Dayforce generates for Margaret Parr is
Parr.Margaret.
User defined: Users specify a login ID themselves when onboarding new employees and
Dayforce validates that the user name is unique. Users can only specify a login ID if their
user role is configured with at least one user role in the New Hire Role Assignments tab in
System Admin > Roles. See Define New Hire Role Assignment Access.
Employees reporting to multiple managers
Controls whether employees can report to multiple managers in Dayforce. When selected,
multiple assigned managers can schedule the employee, add or edit worked shifts or pay
adjustments on the timesheet, record or approve time away from work requests for the employee,
or receive notification of decisions from a workflow routing node.
Note: If your organization uses Position Management, this client property isn’t applicable because
employees can’t report to multiple managers.

Prevent gaps between Employment Status and Work Assignment dates
Controls whether Dayforce shows an error when you save an employee work assignment record

Use predictive analytics for flight risk
Controls whether Dayforce uses the Predictive Analytics feature to calculate flight risk for
employees. By default, the Use predictive analytics for flight risk checkbox is selected, and
Dayforce uses Predictive Analytics to calculate each employee’s flight risk. When the Use
predictive analytics for flight risk checkbox is cleared, you can manually enter a flight risk rating
for each employee when completing their talent reviews in Home or People. See Flight Risk in the
HR Administration Guide.
Minimum age for new hires
Use the Minimum age for new hires field to override the default validation for the minimum age that
is entered for employees in Dayforce. Minimum age validation helps to prevent mistakes such as
entering the current date as the employee's date of birth.
By default, if you enter a date of birth in areas such as the New Hire form that is within three years
of the current date, Dayforce shows a warning message asking you to verify the entered date.
With warning messages, you can still save the record.
You can use the Minimum age for new hires field to set a custom minimum age that is enforced by
an error message rather than a warning message. For example, if you enter 14 and a user enters
a date of birth in the New Hire form that places the employee below 14 years of age, an error
message is generated and you can't save the record.
Minimum age validation is enforced in the following areas:
Candidate Hire form
New Hire form
Rehire form
HR Import
The Birth Date field in the General section of the Personal > Confidential Information screen
in People.

Allow Base Rate Entries Below Minimum Wage for RESTful
Select this checkbox to allow users to enter base rate values that fall below the accepted

submitting POST or PATCH updates to an employee’s BaseRate value using the RESTful API.
Prevent Employee Termination if Future Timesheet Entries Exist
Controls whether you can terminate or inactivate employees who have future-dated timesheet
entries. The options are:

-- 154 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 155 of 0
Off: The property is not enabled. You can terminate or inactivate employees even if they
have timesheet entries or worked time logged for a future date. This option is selected by
default.
All entries: You can’t terminate or inactivate employees if they have either future time entries
or future worked time saved. Dayforce returns an error message and prevents you from
completing the termination or inactivation process.
Worked time only: You can’t terminate or inactivate employees if they have future worked
time saved. However, if they have future time entries that haven’t been worked, you can
terminate or inactivate them. Dayforce returns an error message and prevents you from
completing the termination or inactivation process only if the employee has future worked
time logged.
To use this client property on custom employee termination or leave of absence forms, you must
add the following rules to the form:
Termination forms: <ValidationRule
Type="EmployeeTerminationFutureWorksheetsValidationRule"
Event="OnSubmit" />
Leave of absence forms: <ValidationRule
Type="EmployeeLeaveOfAbsenceFutureWorksheetsValidationRule"
Event="OnSubmit" />
See Use a Named Rule in the XML Forms Guide.
Enable String Sanitizing for Employee Name and Addresses
Select one of the following options to configure Dayforce to check employee names and
addresses for invalid characters in RESTful API requests and HR Import jobs:
Off: This is the default setting. No validation is done on requests or HR Import for invalid
characters.
Warning: Shows a warning message when a request or HR Import job contains invalid
characters, but continues processing the request or job.
Error: Shows an error message when a request or HR Import job contains invalid characters
and stops the request or import from proceeding.
These messages are shown in the HR Import background job log or in the response to the
RESTful request.

Use strict manager effective dating
Controls whether managers can modify timesheets before their effective start date as manager at
the location or for an employee. Select the checkbox and managers can’t edit timesheets for a

For example, an employee is assigned a new manager, effective August 30. The employee
creates three shifts for their location: August 25, August 29, and August 31. The new manager
reviews the time for the employee for the week of August 25. With Use strict manager effective
dating cleared, the new manager can authorize all three shifts. With Use strict manager effective
dating selected, the new manager can only authorize the shift for August 31.

Consolidate employee pay transactions to new pay group effective start
By default, Dayforce doesn’t consolidate employee pay summaries when employees are assigned
a new pay group mid-pay period. When this field contains a date, Dayforce consolidates
employee pay summaries for pay periods that start on or after the date entered, provided that
both pay groups are configured with the same frequency and have the same pay calendars.
For example, Pay Group A and Pay Group B both have a biweekly frequency and have the same
pay calendars, while Pay Group C is configured with a semi-monthly frequency. If an employee is
moved from Pay Group A to Pay Group B mid-pay period, Dayforce consolidates the employee’s
pay summaries. Conversely, if the employee is moved from Pay Group A to Pay Group C,
Dayforce doesn’t consolidate the pay summaries, because the pay groups don’t share the same
frequency.

By default, Dayforce loads all of the dockets an employee has access to, which can take longer
than expected for customers with a large number of dockets configured. With the Use auto
complete for dockets checkbox selected, Dayforce shows a docket control that doesn’t auto-load
all dockets. Instead, it shows an empty docket drop-down list, and prompts users to start typing.
As the user types, Dayforce shows up to ten dockets that match what they have entered.
Round Timesheet Calculations
When this field contains a date, Dayforce rounds timesheet calculations to two decimal places
starting on or after the date entered. Rounding the calculations ensures that the values shown on
the timesheet match the values shown in the pay summary. To avoid retros, any calculations made
prior to the specified date aren’t affected by the client property.
Use auto complete for projects
By default, Dayforce loads all of the projects an employee has access to, which can take longer
than expected for customers with a large number of projects configured. With the Use auto
complete for projects checkbox selected, Dayforce shows a project control that doesn’t auto-load
all projects. Instead, it shows an empty project drop-down list, and prompts users to start typing.
As the user types, Dayforce shows up to ten projects that match what they entered.
Note: Unlike full-text searches, this control uses prefix-matching, which means that the search text
must exactly match the start of the project name. This means that if you type dev, Dayforce
searches only for projects that start with “dev.” It wouldn’t find projects with “dev” in the middle of
the project name.

PSR Org Parallel Processing Mode
Select how Dayforce processes pay summary data when running the Pay Summary Recalc
background job. Depending on how Dayforce is configured, using an alternative calculation
process might improve the job’s performance when calculating affected sites and pay groups.
Important: This client property is effective only if you’ve configured the Pay Summary Recalc
background job to run as a multi-threaded task. This requires admin access and an advanced
understanding of the Dayforce database.
The following calculation methods are available:
Pre-Allocate: This option represents the existing calculation process and is selected by
default. The job assigns org units to a thread at the start of the job calculation. This
calculation process is also referred to as range partitioning.
Load Balance: The job processes and assigns org units to the next available thread. This
calculation process is also referred to as chunk partitioning.

section control how Dayforce processes time and attendance.

Controls whether the site uses tardy rule processing. When selected, tardy rules are enabled and

Cost Time Entries Against
Controls how Dayforce accounts for an employee’s wages and worked hours, including when
employees clock in at different locations from where they were scheduled. Select an option in the
Cost Time Entries Against drop-down list to determine where Dayforce charges an employee’s
worked time (that is, where the cost is allocated). The Cost Time Entries Against drop-down list
has the following options:
Scheduled or primary location: Cost is tied to the location where the employee was
scheduled, regardless of where they clocked in. This is the default setting.

-- 165 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 166 of 0
Clock location: Cost is tied to the location where the employee clocked in, regardless of
where they were scheduled. There’s no link to the schedule.
Clock location; Always link to schedule: Cost is tied to the location where the employee
clocked in and a link to the clock entry is added to the schedule.
Enable support for split pay by business day start time
You can use this client property to configure Dayforce to split pay by the business day start time.
When selected, Dayforce can be configured to split the pay for shifts that cross between two
business days for employees, based on their pay policy. For example, if the business day starts at
midnight, and an employee works from 10:00 PM on Monday to 5:00 AM on Tuesday, Dayforce
splits the pay for the shift so that the employee is paid for two hours on Monday and then five
hours on Tuesday.
When selected, Dayforce shows the Split Pay at Day Start Time checkbox in Pay Setup > Pay
Policy. When the Split Pay at Day Start Time checkbox is selected for a specific pay policy, the
pay for employees who are assigned the policy is split when it crosses two business days.
Enable support for job rate worked
Enables the Respect job rate worked and Allow lower job rate to override base rate checkboxes in
Pay Setup > Pay Policy.
By default, Dayforce pays employees at the higher of either their base rate in People, or the rate
for their primary work assignment. For example, if an employee’s base rate is $10, and the rate for
their primary work assignment is $9, Dayforce would pay the employee at their $10 rate. In cases
where an employee works a non-primary work assignment, they are paid at the higher of either
their usual rate or the rate for the work assignment they actually worked. Continuing the example
above, if the employee works a shift for a non-primary work assignment with a rate of $12,
Dayforce would pay them their $12 rate.
When the Allow lower job rate to override base rate checkbox is selected in Pay Setup > Pay
Policy, Dayforce ignores the employee’s base rate and pays the employee the higher of either the
rate for their primary work assignment or the rate for the work assignment they actually worked.
Continuing the example above, the employee would be paid their $9 rate by default, except for
time worked at their non-primary work assignment with the $12 rate.
When the Respect job rate worked checkbox is selected in Pay Setup > Pay Policy, Dayforce
ignores the employee’s primary work assignment rate and pays them at the higher of either their
base rate for the rate for the work assignment they actually worked. Continuing the example
above, the employee would be paid their $10 base rate for time worked at their primary work
assignment, and their $12 rate for their non-primary work assignment.
When both of these checkboxes are selected, Dayforce always pays the employee at the rate for
the work assignment they actually worked, regardless of their base rate or the rate for their

-- 166 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 167 of 0
primary work assignment.
Unpaired Threshold
Defines the maximum duration, in hours, an “in” clock entry can occur from the next “out” clock
entry and still be paired by Dayforce and considered a single shift. For example, enter 14 and
employees can clock in and out within 14 hours and Dayforce pairs the clock entries together as a
single worked shift. An employee could clock in at 8:00 AM and clock out any time before 10:00
PM (14 hours later) and Dayforce considers the time a single, worked shift.
This client property also defines when Dayforce marks recorded shifts on the timesheet with a
missing clock entry problem. After the unpaired threshold has passed from when an employee
clocks in, Dayforce marks the shift with the problem icon and states that the shift is missing an out
clock entry. The employee’s manager would then need to correct the problem by providing an end
time to the worked shift. Continuing the example, if the employee hadn’t clocked out by 10:00 PM,
beyond the unpaired clock entry threshold, Dayforce considers the shift to have no out clock entry
and marks it as a problem on the timesheet. The employee can’t record an out clock entry against
this shift.
This also defines the number of hours that must elapse before an employee can clock in again
after an unpaired in clock entry. Continuing the example above, if the employee clocked in again
within the 14 hour threshold set by this setting, Dayforce marks the second in clock entry as a
problem as well.
The Unpaired Threshold field should be set to a significantly large duration to cover any scenario
that might arise where employees work late.
It also defines the number of hours that a shift override lasts. A shift override is a supervisor
function that’s performed on a Dayforce clock. For example, this functionality allows supervisors to
override a rejected clock entry if an employee is early or late when clocking in (that is, if Dayforce
is configured to reject clock entries outside of grace periods).
Note: When Dayforce makes comparisons for the unpaired threshold, it considers the in clock
entry after any rounding rules have been applied and the raw clock entry time of the out clock
entry.
Ignore Employee Rate for Unpaid Hours in Reports
Select this checkbox and Dayforce includes hours worked with a pay rate of zero when
generating reports. Clear the checkbox and Dayforce includes hours with a pay rate of zero in
reports only if the Include Unpaid Hours in Total checkbox is selected in the report options.
Auto delete balance transactions after employee termination
Sometimes administrators need to backdate an employee termination. For example, if there’s a lag
between the time when an employee is terminated and the recording of the termination in

-- 167 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 168 of 0
Dayforce, and the lag spans several days or weeks, it’s possible that the employee could accrue
entitlements during that time. When this checkbox is selected, Dayforce automatically deletes any
balance transactions after an employee is terminated in the system. When cleared, Dayforce
doesn’t delete any balance transactions after an employee’s termination. This property is disabled
by default.
The following list details which entitlements are deleted and which aren’t:
Balance transactions that belong to transmitted, closed, approved, or locked pay periods
aren’t deleted.
Transactions managed through Dayforce payroll via pay entries, awarded through payroll
processing on pay out, or committed in payroll aren’t deleted.
In open periods, only timesheet transactions after the last pay date are deleted when the
Last Pay Date is specified in the employee’s HR record. Timesheet transactions before the
last pay date aren’t deleted.
Transactions manually added in the employee’s HR record aren’t deleted.
When this client property is enabled, the balance period is deleted only if:
There are no balance transactions within the period.
The balance period start date occurs on or after the termination date (that is, the balance
period start date is greater than or equal to the termination date).
Note: This functionality has no effect on time away from work transactions, which are still removed
automatically by Dayforce after employee termination regardless of the configuration of the Auto
delete balance transactions after employee termination property.
Attendance Management Default Period Range (Months)
Enter the default period range that’s populated, by default, in the Period of fields of the Load
panel in Attendance Management. By default, this field is set to 3 and Dayforce populates the
Period of fields with a range of three months prior to the current date.
Important: Increasing the default value from 3 to a higher number might cause performance
issues in Attendance Management.
Attendance Management Period Limit (Months)
Enter the maximum number of months in the past that users can load in Attendance Management.
By default, this field is set to 18. For example, consider a user who is loading attendance data on
3/28/2022. With this default period limit configuration, the user can’t load attendance data for
dates before 9/28/2020 because they exceed the 18-month period limit.
Important: Increasing the default value from 18 to a higher number might cause performance
issues in Attendance Management.

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 169 of 0
Restart Attendance Points on
Select one or both options in this drop-down list to configure Dayforce to reset an employee’s
number of accrued attendance incident points in some situations. You can configure Dayforce to
reset incident point totals after employees are rehired or given a new attendance policy
assignment. The options are: Attendance Policy Change and Rehire.
Use transactional data for attendance
By default, Dayforce examines employees’ pay summaries only when calculating absences. For
example, if an instance of the Assign Pay Code Rule updates the pay code associated with an
absence to a pay code that wasn’t an exception (that is, the Is Exception checkbox wasn't
selected in the pay code’s configuration), Dayforce doesn’t count the time associated with this pay
code as an absence.
Conversely, with this checkbox selected, Dayforce examines an employee’s clock entries, pay
adjustments, and transfers to calculate their absences. This means that the time in the example
above would still be counted as an absence, even though it had been reassigned to a non-
exception pay code.
Retry for X more times, if database result is a deadlock
Controls the number of times that Dayforce should retry saving a timesheet when the process fails
due to a deadlock. For example, if you enter 3, Dayforce retries the save three more times. If the
save still fails, Dayforce shows an error message indicating that the user should click Save again.
Enable period authorization
Controls the ability to use period authorization policies to automatically authorize all days in a pay
period, while using an Unauthorization Rule to identify exceptions and unauthorize records based
on a configured set of settings. See Period Authorization Policies.
Important: If this client property is enabled, Dayforce doesn’t show the Time Review section in the
Workforce Insights feature, even for users with the appropriate role access. To review and
authorize time entries and pay adjustments in the Time Review section, you must clear this
checkbox. See Your Workforce in the Manager Guide.
Enable real time calculations (HTML Timesheets)
Controls whether Dayforce shows the Enable real time calculations checkbox in the Options panel
of Employee Timesheet and Timesheets. When you select the Enable real time calculations
checkbox in these features, Dayforce automatically recalculates the shown data when you make

Engine past-dated calculation limit (months)
Defines the maximum number of prior months that Dayforce includes when it calculates changes
using the attendance, base rate, entitlement, job step rate, and payroll engines. This client
property also works in tandem with the WFM GDPR Compliance Check site-level background job,
which tracks calculations and database requests made by WFM engines to ensure Dayforce
meets data minimization settings configured for compliance with General Data Protection
Regulation (GDPR) legislation. The default value is 999.
For example, if you enter 14 and initiate a pay summary recalculation for 24 months in the past,
the recalculation won’t be performed for the period outside of the calculation limit (in this case, the
first 10 months are excluded).
Important: If you configure the Engine past-dated calculation limit (months) client property with a
value equal to or greater than 120 (or, 10 years), the background job fails to run and the job log
contains an error message.
Additionally, when this client property is configured, Dayforce shows a warning notification in
Employee Timesheet, Manager Timesheet, Time Review, and Timesheets when you load time and
attendance records that fall outside of your configured past-dated calculation limit. For example, if
you enter 2 and load a timesheet from three months in the past, Dayforce shows the following
warning notification:

Scheduling
In System Admin > Client Properties in the Properties tab, the settings in the Scheduling section
control how Dayforce schedules employees and shows information in Schedules. Additional
properties control whether Dayforce shows certain types of information, such as unfilled shifts, job
assignments, and pay codes.
Publishes Schedule
Controls if Dayforce tracks whether a schedule was published before it’s printed.
When selected and users print a schedule before it’s published, it’s labeled as a “Draft.”
When cleared, even if the schedule isn’t published, it isn’t labeled as a draft when printed.

Controls if Schedules shows employee job assignments. When cleared, users can’t see which job
assignment is scheduled to a shift and can’t change which job assignment employees are
working during their shifts.

updates, unfills, or deletes shifts that were scheduled under the employee’s previous assignment.

Update Future weeks shifts when work assignment changes (Range 1-52 weeks)
If you select Update in the Update/Unfill/Delete Shifts for work assignment changes drop-down
list, enter the number of weeks into the future that Dayforce begins updating shifts when an
employee’s work assignment changes. For example, if you enter 2, Dayforce begins updating

Use loose activity matching in shift
Controls how Schedules determines which activities can be added to a shift.
When selected, employees can be scheduled for activities they’re qualified to perform
based on each job assignment they’re qualified to work, rather than the job assignment
they’re scheduled to work. For example, if an employee is qualified to work three jobs, and
each job has two distinct activities linked to it, six activities can be scheduled in the shift.
Activities are linked to job assignments in Schedule Setup. See Configure Job Assignment
Activities.
When cleared, employees can be scheduled for activities they’re qualified to perform based
on the job assignment they’re scheduled to work.
Display Pay Codes
Controls whether Schedules shows pay code information. When cleared, users can’t schedule
employees to a specific pay code in the Schedules Grid View.
Auto load
Controls whether the upcoming schedule is loaded in Schedules instead of waiting for users to
select a week and click Load.
Zone in activity overwrites
Controls how Dayforce accounts for the labor spent during scheduled activities. When cleared, all
of the labor from a shift counts toward its zone. This is determined by the job assignment the
employee was scheduled to work during the shift and the activities scheduled to a shift don’t
impact this allocation. When selected, the labor from a shift can count toward an activity’s zone. If
an activity has been linked to a specific zone in Schedule Setup > Activities, then the portion of a
shift covered by that activity counts its labor toward the activity’s zone.
See Configure Activities.

View mode
Controls whether Schedules opens in the Bar View, Grid View, or Split View. See Schedule Options

Reallocate meals/breaks
Controls if Dayforce reallocates meals and breaks when users edit the schedule. When selected,
Dayforce adds, removes, or reschedules any meal or break on a scheduled shift when the shift's
duration is edited. When or if the meal or break is rescheduled depends on the meal and break
allocation rules that are already configured. These rules dictate how many meals and breaks shifts
receive automatically, and they’re based on the shift’s scheduled duration. For example, the rules
might state that a four-hour shift receives one 15-minute break. When a user changes a three-hour
shift, which wasn’t scheduled for a break, to last five hours, Dayforce automatically schedules the
15-minute break.
You configure meal and break allocations in time entry policies in Pay Setup > Time Entry Policy.
See Meal and Break Allocations.

can also unselected it.

icon ( ) next to employees’ names in the Grid View if the Indicate Minor Status checkbox in the
Options panel is selected. By default, this client property is set to 18 and you can update it as
required.

Controls whether Dayforce automatically selects and schedules an employee to their job

activity assigned to it in Schedule Setup > Job Assignment Activities. If the job assignment has
more than one activity assigned to it, Dayforce assigns the activity that’s at the top of the list.

Primary sort, Secondary sort, and Third sort
These three drop-down lists define the order in which schedules are shown by default. The
Primary sort drop-down list defines how schedules are sorted first, and the Secondary sort and
Third sort lists used for successive sorts. The schedule can be sorted by department name,
employee job rank, employee name, job rank, pay class rank, seniority date, or zone.
Note: Any sort order defined in Schedules supersedes a default sort order that’s configured using
these client properties. To ensure that these client properties are respected, remove the
configured sort order (if available) in Schedules by clicking Sort and removing any sorting options
in the Selected column.
Job ranks are assigned to the jobs configured in Dayforce. See Jobs and Job Assignments
Configuration. If the schedule is sorted by job ranks, shifts with the job that has the highest job
rank are shown at the top of the schedule.
Similarly, pay class ranks reference each pay class’s sort order. See Create Pay Classes in the
HR Administration Guide.
Dayforce sorts zones based on each zone’s sort index. See Create Zones.

Controls how Dayforce examines employee availability. When selected, Dayforce considers
