Day of week when next week shown
Defines when Dayforce loads the next schedule period:
0 loads the next schedule period.
7 loads the current schedule period.
1 to 6 determines which schedule loads, based on the current day’s number in the days of
the week. For example, say an organization’s week starts on Monday and a user goes to
Schedules on Wednesday, which is the third day of the week. If you enter 2, Dayforce loads
the next week’s schedule. If you enter 4, it loads the current week.

Scheduling Interval Size
Defines the minimum increment that users can specify or change scheduled times by when
adding or editing shifts. You can select the following increments:
1 Minute: Shifts can be scheduled to the desired minute. For example, you can schedule a
shift to start at 8:58 AM and end at 3:28 PM.
Note: Selecting this option disables the Schedules Bar View and Split View. However,
Dayforce still shows coverage totals.
5 Minutes: Shifts can be scheduled on the hour, or at five minute intervals past the hour.
15 Minutes: Shifts can be scheduled on the hour, or 15, 30, or 45 minutes past the hour.
When you select 1 Minute, Dayforce also supports 1-minute schedule increments for the following:
Shift rotations
Activities
Schedule templates
Schedule auditing
Schedule compliance rules (for example, Core Hours Rule, Daily Hours Rule, Minimum Rest
In Period Rule, and others)
Printed Schedule Report
Schedule Audit Report
Note: The Daily Coverage Report and Manager Coverage Report don’t support 1-minute
schedule increments. These reports are unavailable to users when 1-minute increments are
enabled.

Time entry policies
The Scheduling Interval Size client property also governs the behavior of the Min Duration
(minutes) field in activities. Dayforce rounds the value specified in Min Duration (minutes) up to the
nearest interval size specified in the Scheduling Interval Size client property. For example, if the
interval specified is 15 minutes, and the Min Duration (minutes) is 16 minutes, then the minimum
activity length applied for scheduling is rounded to 30 minutes. However, continuing that example,
if the Scheduling Interval Size property is set to 5 minutes, then the minimum activity length
applied for scheduling is 20 minutes.
Autofill will allow work to start/end/change
Defines the default points in the hour that shifts can start or end when you create shifts using
autofill. You can configure shifts to start every 15 minutes, on the 30 and 60 minute marks, or only
on the 60-minute mark. Every 15 minutes is selected by default. When users create a schedule
using autofill, the option that you select is selected by default in the Options dialog box. If
necessary, the user can select another option to change when shifts start, end, or change for the
schedule that they’re creating.
Prompt to clear
Defines if Dayforce shows a prompt when users click the Clear button in Schedules. Select Always
and Dayforce shows a prompt. Select Never and Dayforce doesn’t show a prompt. Clearing a
loaded schedule deletes every scheduled shift, based on the user’s access and any applied
filters. By prompting users to confirm, Dayforce helps ensure that this action is performed only
when appropriate.
Number of Editable Scheduled Days in the Past
Defines the number of rolling 24 hour periods into the past (if any) that Dayforce permits users to
edit schedules, either through Schedules or the schedule import. For example, enter 14 and users
with access can go back a maximum of 14 rolling 24 hour periods from the present time and still
edit schedules. You can also enter a negative number to restrict edits to future schedules. For
example, to prevent users from editing shifts that are within the next three rolling 24 hour periods,
enter -3. This prevents users from editing any shifts that occur from now (for example, 3:00 AM
Monday) until three rolling 24 hour periods in the future (that is, 3:00 AM Thursday). Also, because
the number isn’t positive, this prevents users from editing any schedules prior to that time in the
past. By default, the value is 0.

-- 182 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 183 of 0
The ability to allow past edits to schedules is intended for situations where an employee’s
schedule has changed, but the schedule wasn’t modified in time to reflect the new hours that the
employee will be working. For example, if a manager calls an employee in to cover an
unexpected absence, then the employee works the shift, and records the time. Dayforce shows
this as an unscheduled, worked shift in Timesheets, even though the employee’s manager asked
them to come in to work on short notice or there was an agreement to work another shift. With this
functionality, the employee’s manager can update the schedule afterwards, even though it’s in the
past, to reflect what the employee was asked to work.
This functionality is controlled by this client property and the Edit Past Schedules access
authorization.
To allow past schedule edits or prevent future edits:
In the Number of Editable Scheduled Days in the Past client property, specify the number of
days into the past that users with access can edit schedules.
In System Admin > Roles, in the Authorizations tab, locate the Edit Past Schedules access
authorization and assign all permissions. See Configure User Role Authorizations.
Note: When you edit a past schedule, Dayforce runs the rule engine to recalculate employees’
pay and changes to pay can occur, depending on the configuration of the pay rules and
qualifiers. For added security and to prevent Dayforce from creating inadvertent retros, it isn’t
possible to edit schedules in retro pay periods (that is, on transmitted pay periods). However,
users with access can still edit schedules in past, non-retro periods.

Enables Dayforce to use workflows for schedule approval. When this client property is enabled

KPI for Schedule Efficiency Score
Links a KPI to the Recalculate Schedule Efficiency background job, which is used to store
schedule efficiency scores in the database. You can use the selected KPI to track daily and
weekly schedule efficiency scores for locations and their zones in Plan and Operation View, and to
create reports on schedule efficiency in Reporting and Analytics. It can be used to track scores of
individual stores or the average score of stores under an above store location (for example, to
provide a district-wide schedule efficiency score).
First, you need to create a KPI for schedule efficiency. Because schedule efficiency is a
percentage value, the KPI must use a percentage.

-- 183 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 184 of 0
Then, select the KPI in the KPI for Schedule Efficiency Score drop-down list to link the KPI to the
Recalculate Schedule Efficiency background job. The drop-down list shows only KPIs that use a
percentage value. When a schedule efficiency KPI is defined, run the Recalculate Schedule
Efficiency background job to store schedule efficiency scores in the database. For more
information on configuring KPIs for use in Dayforce, see the following sections:
To configure KPIs for use in Plan, see KPIs and KPI Metadata.
To configure KPIs for use in Operation View, see Operation Dashboards Configuration.
To create ad hoc reports, see Ad Hoc Report Administration.
Skip the one-step look-ahead for base coverage in autofill
With one-step look-ahead, Dayforce checks to see if making a schedule change will detrimentally
impact the next step in the autofill. This property controls whether the Skip base coverage
checking checkbox in the Autofill dialog box is selected by default. When you select this
checkbox, autofill doesn’t check for detrimental impacts to base coverage when filling the
schedule.

minimum staffing coverage.

by default. When you select this checkbox, autofill tries to add/modify activities within shifts at the
end of the process to see it can improve schedule efficiency.
Skip appending activities to shifts improvement method
Controls whether the Skip append activity improvement checkbox in the Autofill dialog box is
selected by default. This option is enabled by default because it should generally be skipped
unless being used for configuration purposes. When enabled, this option attempts to cover a shift
entirely with activities which can have some undesirable side effects outside of configuration
scenarios.

Match Employee Transfer based on

-- 185 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 186 of 0
Specifies how Dayforce determines which employees you can reassign shifts to. When you select
Job Assignments, Dayforce restricts shift reassignment based on job assignment. For example, a
Supervisor shift can be reassigned only to another employee with a work assignment for the
Supervisor job assignment. When you select Activities, Dayforce ignores shifts’ job assignments
and users can reassign it based on the activity. So, if the Markdowns activity is associated with a
shift, Dayforce allows you to reassign the shift to any employee who can perform that activity,
regardless of their job assignment.
Note the following when using the Match Employee Transfer based on client property:
When this client property is set to Activities but no activities are assigned to the selected
shift, Dayforce reverts back to Job Assignments.
When an employee has more than one job assignment that they can work at an activity,
Dayforce defaults to their primary job assignment. If they can work only that activity in non-
primary job assignments, Dayforce uses the first non-primary job assignment it finds.
Dayforce respects this client property regardless of whether users reassign the shift using
the Find Candidate dialog box, by selecting a new employee in the drop-down list when
editing the shift, or by dragging and dropping the shift into a new cell in Grid View.

> Assignment Policy in the Weekly Order tab when determining which shifts to add to the
schedule first. If this checkbox is cleared, Dayforce doesn’t use your customized weekly order
and adds the shifts to the schedule randomly.

Controls whether Dayforce runs the Pay Summary Recalc job every time you save their schedule,
or only when the Pay Summary Recalc nightly job runs. When selected, the Pay Summary Recalc
job runs automatically along with the Reconcile Schedule Data background job, every time you
save a schedule. When cleared, the Reconcile Schedule Data background job runs without
running the Pay Summary Recalc job. Only the Tardy and Time Entry Problem Recalc job engines
run. Saved schedules aren’t recalculated via the Pay Summary Recalc job until the Pay Summary
Recalc nightly job runs.

The dialog boxes and panels where managers add and edit shifts.
The Cost panel in the Daily tab.

Use auto complete for dockets
By default, Dayforce loads all of the dockets that an employee has access to, which can take
longer for customers with a large number of dockets. Select this checkbox and Dayforce shows a
dialog box where you can search for dockets to load.
Use auto complete for projects
By default, Dayforce loads all of the projects that an employee has access to, which can take
longer for customers with a large number of projects. Select this checkbox and Dayforce shows a
dialog box where you can search for projects to load.
Note: Unlike full-text searches, this control uses prefix-matching, which means that the search text
must exactly match the start of the project name.
Use auto complete for labor metric codes
By default, Dayforce loads all of the labor metrics that an employee has access to, which can take
longer for customers with a large number of metrics. Select this checkbox and Dayforce shows a
dialog box where you can search for labor metrics to load.

Mobile Calendar Inbox Future Date Range
Controls the date-range threshold for the Schedule Acceptance – Schedule Offer Sent notification.
If a manager creates a new schedule offer for an employee that falls outside of this future date

by default.
Consider an example where this client property is set to 14. If a manager updates a shift that’s 22
days in the future, Dayforce doesn’t send a schedule acceptance offer to the affected employee
because the shift is outside of the 14-day threshold.

Primary Location: Employees are restricted to being scheduled to their primary location but

Primary Job Assignment: Employees are restricted to being scheduled to their primary

be scheduled only to their primary work assignment. This is the most restrictive option.
Maximum Number of Weeks in the Past to Allow Edits in Plan
Role feature access: Plan > Edit
The maximum number of weeks in the past that users can modify plans in Plan. For example, this
field can be thought of as the earliest week relative to the current week that you can edit in Plan.
By default, the value in the field is 0 and users can only edit the values in the Manager Adjust
column for the current and future weeks. This field accepts integer values including zero and
negative numbers. Consider the following examples of this field’s configuration:
Enter 1 and users can edit future weeks, the current week, and up to one week in the past.
Enter 0 and users can edit the current week and the future weeks, but not previous weeks.
Enter -1 and users can edit only future weeks, but not the current or previous weeks.
If left empty, all weeks are editable if the Plan > Edit role feature is enabled in System Admin >
Roles in the Features tab.

Shift Marketplace
Controls access to Shift Marketplace functionality in Dayforce. In the mobile Shift Marketplace
feature, employees can pick up shifts at eligible, non-primary locations. When the Shift
Marketplace client property is enabled, Dayforce shows information about Shift Marketplace shifts
in several features.
This client property also enables access to:
The Shift Marketplace checkbox in People in the Work > Work Assignments screen. When
employees pick up shifts in Shift Marketplace at eligible locations for the first time, Dayforce
automatically creates a Shift Marketplace work assignment for the employe. Optionally, you
can also manually enable Shift Marketplace functionality for employees by creating a new
secondary work assignment for them and selecting this checkbox. This checkbox is
available only for secondary work assignments.
The Display Shift Marketplace Employees checkbox in the Options panels in Schedules and
Multi-Week Calendar.
The Display Scheduled Shift Marketplace Employees checkbox in the Options panel in
Timesheets.
When these display checkboxes are selected in the scheduling and timesheet features, Dayforce
shows Shift Marketplace shifts and employees in schedules and timesheets. Note that in
Timesheets, Dayforce shows some Shift Marketplace information by default, regardless if the
Display Scheduled Shift Marketplace Employees checkbox is selected or cleared. See Shift
Marketplace Shift Display in Timesheets in the Manager Guide.
When you enable the Shift Marketplace client property, Dayforce also marks affected shifts with
the Shift Marketplace icon ( ) in the following timesheet features, by default:
Employee Timesheet
Manager Timesheet
Work > Timesheet
Features where you can load duration timesheets (Pay Admin Checklist, Pay Approve
Checklist, Period Review, Time Review, Work > Calendar)
Important: You shouldn’t enable and disable the Shift Marketplace client property periodically. If
the Shift Marketplace client property is enabled and then you disable it, Dayforce converts
existing Shift Marketplace shifts and pay adjustments to shifts with a secondary work assignment
in timesheet features. This behavior can impact your data in the following ways:
Shift Marketplace shifts aren’t editable, but when they’re converted to a shift under an
employee’s secondary work assignment, the employee might be able to adjust the shift’s
details.

-- 194 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 195 of 0
After Dayforce converts Shift Marketplace work assignments to secondary work
assignments, employees might be able to:
Add shifts using these secondary work assignments.
Add these secondary work assignments to favorite sets in some timesheet features,
and create shifts using these favorite sets.
If you re-enable the Shift Marketplace client property, these shifts are reconverted and
inaccurately shown as Shift Marketplace shifts in timesheet features. This behavior occurs
even if the shifts aren’t linked to a schedule and weren’t picked up in the mobile Shift
Marketplace feature.
See Shift Marketplace.

This topic contains an overview of the client payroll properties that you can set in the Payroll
section of the Properties tab in System Admin > Client Properties. This topic addresses each of
the fields and options available to you in the Payroll section and how they work together.
For basic instructions on how to configure client payroll properties, see Configure Client Payroll
Properties.
Allow Canada Customer Banking
Note: This property shows only for users who log in to Dayforce using a Service role. For more
information, contact Dayforce Support. After this setting is turned on, it can’t be turned off or
cleared.
Enables Canadian organizations to configure a bank account to fund payroll. This bank account
can be configured to pay employees directly via direct deposits.
Allow GL duplication of premium split hours
Note: This property shows only for users who log in to Dayforce using a Service role. For more
information, contact Dayforce Support.
When you select the client property, Dayforce duplicates entries during a payroll GL export of
premium earnings with split hours. By default, the client property is not selected and premium
earning entries are not duplicated.
Allow Provincial Health Tax Deferral
Select to enable the Enable Tax Payment Deferral setting for specific Canadian provincial taxes in
the Tax Authorities tab in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity. Dayforce supports the tax
deferral programs for the following provincial taxes:
Ontario Employer Health Tax (EHT)
Allow Reduction of Canada Income Tax Deductions at Source for Cross Province Employment
Select to enable Dayforce to calculate taxes for Quebec employees who reside in a province
other than Quebec and want to reduce their income tax deductions at source. Each employee
must complete a T1213 form. To finish configuring this feature, you must also select the Apply
Income Tax Reduction for Cross Province Employment checkbox in the Payroll > Tax Definitions
screen in People.

(ABN) but a different branch number in Org Set-up > Org Payroll Set-up > Legal Entity in the
Federal/Business ID number field, and in the STP Parameters sub-tab in the Branch ID field,
respectively.
Allow duplicate BN (Canada Only - Restricted)
Allows Canadian organizations to configure more than one legal entity record with the same
business number. This feature is used to support a legal entity that has more than one employer
health tax (EHT) or Revenu Quebec "RS" identification number.
Before you turn on this setting, the legal entities must meet the following requirements:
The legal entities that share the same business number must have different names in
Dayforce.
Each legal entity can have the same or different account IDs for employer health taxes or
RS identification numbers.
To ensure accurate reporting, each legal entity must use different funding accounts to pay
their employees. See Customer Funding Identifiers for Canadian Legal Entities.
Allow imports to add terminated employee to the pay run
Select to allow the import process to automatically add prior period terminated employees to the
pay run when you run a Quick Entry Import or a Pay Entry Import. As well, a warning message is
displayed in the Problems panel to let you know that a terminated employee was automatically
added when you recalculate payroll after the import.
Enable option to use Benefit Eligibility date for Expression-based Payroll elections
When selected, Dayforce uses the actual benefit eligibility dates to determine the payroll election
effective dates. See Payroll Election Effective Dates.
Allow pay date to fall on holiday/weekend for off-cycle runs (North America)
Enables employers in the United States and Canada to create an off-cycle pay run with a pay
date on Saturday, Sunday, or a public holiday.

Changes how Block 12 Final Pay Period Ending Date is filled in the ROE forms in Dayforce.
When the client property is turned on, the end date shown in Block 12 belongs to the pay period

period, earnings in later pay periods aren’t automatically included in Block 15C.
Tax Locator Behavior
Before You Begin: The Tax Locator Behavior client property is available only to users with the
System role.
Select an option to determine how the tax locator calculates updates to employee locations when
they’re made using HR Import or the Employee API:
Default: The tax locator processes changes caused by HR imports or Employee API
updates immediately.
Defer (HR Import 2 and RESTful API Only): The tax locator processes changes caused by
HR imports or Employee API updates after they are completed.
Disable: The tax locator doesn’t process any changes caused by HR imports or Employee
API updates.

Disable Canada Garnishment Arrears Calculation
(Canada only) By default, Dayforce is set to calculate arrears, so this checkbox is cleared. To turn

This setting also impacts the Garnishments History Report. If this checkbox is cleared, the
Garnishment History Report includes the message "Disable Arrears Calculation" with the indicator
"N", and arrears amounts are included in the report output. If the checkbox is selected, the
Garnishment History Report includes the message "Disable Arrears Calculation" with the indicator
"Y", and arrears amounts are excluded from the report output.
Important: After you commit a pay run for a Canadian pay group, you cannot change this option
back to calculate arrears.

Use Verification Services APIs instead of Equifax Payroll Export File
Service role users only. This client payroll property controls whether employment and income data

GET Employee Verification of Employment (VOE)
GET Employee Verification of Income (VOI)
Information about these APIs is available on the Dayforce Developers Network,
https://developers.dayforce.com, in the API Explorer under Payroll > Employee Verification.
Select this checkbox to configure the client instance to return employment and income data for
US employees as an API response to a call that a vendor makes.
Data isn’t sent to a vendor using both methods for the same namespace. For a namespace with
US employees, data is only be sent to Equifax using the export file by Dayforce Link, or as a result
of an API call. This property determines which method is used. If the checkbox is:
Cleared (not selected), any API calls made for US employees in this namespace fail and
display an error that API isn’t available.
Selected, any export files that configured aren’t generated. Dayforce includes a warning
message in the payroll data export background job to indicate that the export didn’t
generate because the client is configured for API calls instead.

Benefits
This topic contains information on the client properties that you must configure in the Benefits
section of the Properties tab in System Admin > Client Properties.
Benefits Cutover Date
Determines the date at which eligibility is calculated for events generated in the past. When an
event is processed based on the workflow form or the forms included in the benefits enrollment,
Dayforce uses the later of the following dates to calculate eligibility:
The event date
The configured Benefits Cutover Date
In addition, Dayforce prevents users from entering an election's effective start date in the Benefits
> Benefit Elections screen in People before the benefits cutover date.
Important: If your organization uses the Benefits Cutover Date client property, Dayforce doesn't
assign employees who were hired before the cutover date to a PPACA calendar. See Assign
Periods.
Enable COBRA Provider Subscriber Tracking
Controls whether Dayforce tracks subscribers, based on the following logic:
If the employee's coverage is included in the COBRA event, the employee is assigned as
the Subscriber.
If a COBRA event is generated for one or more dependents and the employee isn’t included
in the event, the oldest dependent included in the event that loses coverage is assigned as
the Subscriber.
Only one Subscriber is assigned per COBRA event, unless the employee's eldest
dependents share a birth date. In this case, both dependents are assigned as subscribers.
If the COBRA event is assigned the “Not a COBRA Event” Reason, Dayforce doesn't
include the event record in the evaluation and a Subscriber isn’t assigned.
Select the checkbox, and Dayforce tracks subscriber information and shows an indicator in
employee records shown in Benefits Administration > COBRA. Clear the checkbox, and Dayforce
doesn't track subscribers.
Enable the use of the 'Exclude scheduled amount for 27/53 pay date' parameter for benefit
elections

-- 215 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 216 of 0
Controls whether Dayforce Benefits take into account the Exclude Scheduled Amount for 27/53
Pay Date property in earning and deduction definitions when calculating benefits per pay
amounts. Select the checkbox, and Benefits respects the setting of the property in the deduction
or earning definition. If the earning or deduction is configured to exclude the 27th and 53rd pay
dates and the benefits client property is selected, the 27th and 53rd pay periods are also
excluded in per pay amount calculations when applicable. Keep the checkbox cleared, and the
Benefits module ignores the property on the earning or deduction and calculates based on 27 or
53 pay periods when applicable.
If you have manually configured benefits per pay amounts to take into account the 27th or 53rd
pay periods, you should leave this checkbox cleared. The checkbox is cleared by default.
Important: Imputed income and per pay prorations are calculated based on 27 or 53 pay periods
in applicable years regardless of whether mapped earning and deduction definitions are
configured to exclude those pay dates in payroll calculations.
Enable the use of the 'Subject To Re-enrollment' parameter for benefit plans (Days)
Enter the number of days within which employees must be rehired to automatically re-enroll in their
previous benefits plan before termination. For example, if this field is set to 90, employees must be
rehired within 90 days to automatically re-enroll in their previous benefits plan. The Automatic Re-
Enrollment Allowed checkbox in the General tab of plans in the Benefits Setup > Plans and
Options work based on the value set in this field, when selected.
When configured, Dayforce uses the value defined in this field during benefits eligibility workflow
recalculations to determine enrollment assignment. If an employee is rehired within the specified
number of days and is subject to re-enrollment, Dayforce doesn’t assign new hire enrollments,
even if the employee is otherwise eligible. Instead, Dayforce applies re-enrollment rules based on
prior benefit elections and plan configuration. This behavior ensures that employees within the re-
enrollment period are processed according to re-enrollment rules rather than new hire enrollment
rules.
Enable Spouse Coverage Verification
Controls whether Dayforce shows the Offered Medical Coverage Elsewhere field in the Current
Dependent Information form.
Use Pay Group Country for Benefit Country Eligibility
Determines benefits eligibility based on the country associated with an employee’s pay group
instead of their primary address. When you select this checkbox, Dayforce uses the country
linked to the employee’s pay group. When you clear the checkbox, Dayforce defaults to the
country associated with the employee’s primary address. The employee's benefit country uses the

-- 216 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 217 of 0
existing eligibility criteria for plans, options, rates, and enrollments to determine if the employee
qualifies.
Example: An employee with a pay group country of the United States and a primary address
country of France begins the benefits enrollment process. When the Use Pay Group Country for
Benefit Country Eligibility checkbox is selected, Dayforce evaluates the employee’s eligibility
based on the United States as the benefit country. As a result, the employee qualifies for benefit
options available in the United States.
Enable moving employee to next eligible tiered option when dependent ages out
When this checkbox is selected, if an employee loses coverage when their dependent reaches
the maximum age limit, Dayforce moves the employee from the current plan option to the next
lower tier option. The coverage in the new plan option starts the next day after coverage ends in
the previous plan option. Additionally, Dayforce generates a COBRA event for the dependent who
aged out.
Dayforce moves employees through eligible tiers in the following order:
Employee & Family
Employee & Children
Employee & 5 Dependents
Employee & 4 Dependents
Employee & 3 Dependents
Employee & 2 Dependents
Employee & 2 or more Dependents
Employee & 1 Dependent
Employee & Child
Employee & Spouse/Legal Partner
Employee & 1 or more Dependents
Employee
If employees are enrolled in pre-tax or after-tax health plan options with the same plan subtype
and become ineligible because a dependent reaches the maximum age limit, Dayforce ends their
current benefit elections and transfers the employee and dependents to the next eligible options
with the same taxability settings.
Example: An employee is enrolled in the following plan options:
EE + Domestic Partner + Child (Pre-Tax)
EE + Domestic Partner + Child (After-Tax)
Their child dependent exceeds the maximum age limit. When the recalculation task runs,
Dayforce ends the elections and transfers the employee to the plan:

-- 217 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 218 of 0
Employee Only (Pre-Tax)
The employee isn’t moved to an after-tax option because an equivalent Employee Only (After-Tax)
option is unavailable.
Hide Dayforce Your Tax banner
When this checkbox is selected, the application hides the Dayforce Your Tax banner in the Year
End Forms tab of Earnings.
Suppress printing of employee 1095-C forms
When this checkbox is selected:
If the ACA year end filing doesn’t include any employees who lived in Washington, DC,
during the filing year, Dayforce doesn’t generate or send a print file to the Print Center.
If the ACA year end filing includes employees who lived in Washington, DC, Dayforce
generates a print file only for those employees who haven’t opted for electronic delivery.
Position Management
The Position Management section of the Properties tab in System Admin > Client Properties
contains the properties that you can use to enable the Position Management functionality in
Dayforce.
Enable Position Assignments
With this property enabled, users can assign employees as position occupants and update their
occupancy details.
Auto populate termination date as the expected vacancy date on employee's positions
With this property enabled, an employee's termination date is automatically populated on the
positions they occupied as the expected vacancy date of those positions.
Respect PM access authorizations on position change form
Restricts the positions that are available on the Position Change form so that the user can see only
positions that they have access to according to their access authorizations. If the user has only
manager view access, the form shows only positions under theirs in the hierarchy. If the user has
administrator view access, the form shows all available positions.
Derive Management Assignments from Primary Position Assignment Only
Determines how management assignments are handled when a manager moves into an interim
role as their primary position assignment. By default, the checkbox is cleared. The manager

-- 218 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 219 of 0
keeps their management assignments from their home position, and direct reports from the interim
position are added. With the checkbox selected, management assignments come only from the
interim position because it’s the manager’s primary assignment. Management assignments from
their home position are end-dated before the interim role begins.
Enable FTE Proration
When this client property is selected, the full-time equivalent ratio in an employee’s profile
determines if the employee is eligible. In Benefits Setup > Eligibility for the Employee Qualifier, use
the Min FT Equivalent Ratio and Max FT Equivalent Ratio fields to set the minimum and maximum
full-time equivalent ratios.
The full-time equivalent ratio is calculated using the following formula:
FT Equivalent Ratio = Normal Weekly Hours / FT Weekly Hours
You can find these values for an employee in People, in the Employment > Employment Settings
screen, in the Employment Status tab.
An employee is eligible if their full-time equivalent ratio on the effective date is as follows:
Equal to or greater than the Min FT Equivalent Ratio, and
Equal to or less than the Max FT Equivalent Ratio.
If the Enable FTE Proration client property isn’t enabled, Dayforce ignores eligibility based on the
minimum and maximum full-time equivalent ratios.
See Compensation Information.

The Security section of the Properties tab in System Admin > Client Properties contains the

Admin-assisted password reset option
Controls whether Dayforce sends the user an email with their new password, a password reset
link, or a password reset template when you reset a password for a user.
Login Assist Message
The message that Dayforce shows to users who are having difficulty logging in and click the Can't

-- 219 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide

The message that Dayforce shows to users who try to reset their password without having set up
their security questions. Part of this message will let them know that they need to set up their

Enable Email Verification
Select this checkbox and Dayforce sends verification emails when a user creates or edits an email
address in various locations throughout Dayforce with the Alerts checkbox selected. It also
enables the Verify Email button for email addresses with this checkbox selected.
Enable Password Reset (requires email verification)
Controls whether users can request a password reset.
Select the checkbox to allow users to request password resets via email; users also need the
Profile > Profile Menu > Settings > Security > Password Reset role feature assigned to their role to
select their security question and answers. To reset passwords, users are asked to provide their
answers to their security questions.
Clear the checkbox to deactivate this functionality.
Note: If you select this checkbox you must also select the Enable Email Verification checkbox,
because a verified email address is required for password reset.
Email Verification Time Limit
Defines the expiration date for the email verification message that's sent to employees, and allows
administrators to select from one to five days.
Moreover, the number of days selected is shown in the content of the verification message:
Login Algorithm Custom Format
Defines a custom format for generating new employee user names. This field gives your
organization the flexibility to use its preferred custom format, instead of a predefined one (that is,
F.Last, LAST.FIRST). For example, you can create a custom format that includes the employee's
first initial, followed by last name and then employee number. For more information about creating
custom formats, see Create Custom Login Algorithms.
Maximum number of automatic verification requests

-- 220 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 221 of 0
The number of times Dayforce sends an email verification request to an email address because of
the site-level Send Email Verification background job. This prevents Dayforce from repeatedly
sending verification messages to addresses when they’re incorrect or no longer in use.
For example, the Send Email Verification background job runs three times, each time sending a
verification request to the same email address. With this property set to 3, Dayforce doesn't send
a message to this address the next time that the job runs.
Important: This property doesn't affect users manually sending an email verification request. As
such, there continues to be no limit on how many times users can manually trigger a verification
request. Continuing the example above, while the email address will no longer receive an
automatic message the next time that the Send Email Verification job runs, users can still manually
trigger the message.
Enable first time access email
Select the checkbox to enable first time access email messages. By default, the checkbox is
cleared.
First Time Access Email Sender Name
The message author's name.
First Time Access Email Reply To Address
The reply-to email address.
First Time Access Email Expiration in Day(s)
Specifies how long before the link in the email expires. By default, this is set to 1 for security
reasons, but you can enter a value between 1 and 5 days.
Important: Although the email link's expiration can be extended for up to 5 days, doing so could
present a security risk, allowing more time for someone other than the intended hire to use the link
and access your system. As an alternative, you could increase the number of email delivery
attempts (using the First Time Access Email Maximum Delivery Attempts field) as a potentially
more secure way of giving people more time to log in to Dayforce, because each delivery
provides a new access link.
First Time Access Email Maximum Delivery Attempts
Specifies how many times to attempt delivery of the email. By default, this is set to 5, but you can
enter a value between 0 and 99.
Maximum number of first time access verification attempts

-- 221 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 222 of 0
The maximum number of attempts an onboarding employee can make before they are locked out
of Dayforce access verification. The employee is asked to enter the last four digits of their phone
number. You can select an attempt value between 1 and 3.
Enable Account Recovery Assistant (Requires password reset)
Enables the Account Recovery Assistant, a feature that is shown when users log in and are
missing security questions or a verified email on their profile. Using this feature, users can add this
information without having to go to their profile.
Disable Skipping of Account Recovery Assistant
(Only applicable when the Enable Account Recovery Assistant (Requires password reset)
checkbox in the same location is selected.) Select this checkbox for the Account Recovery
Assistant to show the Close button instead of the Skip button, so that employees must complete
their password reset information before they can access Dayforce.
When the Disable Skipping of Account Recovery Assistant checkbox is selected, users who don’t
have an employee profile in Dayforce (for example, system administrators) will still see the Skip
button, which they can click to continue to access Dayforce.
Block Biometric Logins into ESS
Select this checkbox and the Dayforce Touch Clock disallows employees from logging in to the
clock’s self-service mode with biometric verification.
Important: When this client property is enabled and the clock is configured to require biometric
verification, the clock prevents employees from logging in to self-service mode using both
biometric and password verification. This effectively disables self-service mode, because
employees can't enter a password to verify their identity when logging in. To allow employees to
log in to self-service using a password while this client property is enabled, you must deactivate
biometric verification in the clock’s config file, which also removes biometric verification from other
functions on your clock.
Reset Password Request Attempt Timespan (in minutes)
Defines the timespan used to limit the amount of reset password requests that can occur within a
specific time frame. If the number of reset password requests exceeds the number that you
defined in the Reset Password Request Maximum Attempts in Preset Timespan setting and these
requests occur within the timespan you defined, Dayforce shows an error message. By default,
this setting is set to 30 minutes.
Reset Password Request Maximum Attempts in Preset Timespan

-- 222 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 223 of 0
Defines the number of reset password requests that can be sent in the timespan that you defined
in the Reset Password Request Attempt Timespan (in minutes) setting. In the drop-down list, you
can select a numerical value from 3 to 10. By default, this setting is set to a maximum of 5
attempts.
Mobile App session timeout due to inactivity (in seconds, minimum 120)
Defines the number of seconds a mobile app session can remain idle before it times out and
closes due to inactivity.

Configure Clock Entry Validations

-- 225 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 226 of 0
In System Admin > Clocking Sequence Validation, you can configure the clock entry validations
that Dayforce performs on clock entries recorded on the Clock+ and in Work > Time Clock. The
Dayforce Touch Clock also uses these validations, but only when operating in online mode, which
means that the clock accepts all clock entries and transmits them to Dayforce for validation.
Alternatively, when operating in standalone mode, the Dayforce Touch Clock performs the
validations specified in its configuration file instead.
Each validation listed below has the following settings:
Active: Select this checkbox to configure Dayforce to perform that validation. Dayforce only
performs clock entry validations with this checkbox selected.
Execution Order: Enter a number that represents the order Dayforce performs that
validation, relative to other validations. For example, Dayforce performs a validation with
“10” in this field before one with “15.”
Apply to Offline Time Entries: Select this checkbox if Dayforce should apply the validation to
clock entries that were recorded when the clock was offline.
Apply to Supervisor Time Entries: Select this checkbox if Dayforce should apply the
validation to clock entries that are recorded by supervisors.
Dayforce can perform the following validations:
Biometric Consent Validation
Validates that the employee clocking in with biometric verification consented to submit their
fingerprint templates after reviewing the legal disclaimer. If the employee declined to consent to
the submission of their fingerprint templates, the clock entry is rejected.
Biometric Validation
For clocks using biometric verification, validates that the employee’s finger scan matches the
template saved in the database.
Break End Validation
Validates employees’ break end times when they clock back in from a break. When enabled, the
clock doesn’t allow employees to clock in from a break when they aren’t scheduled to.
Break Length Validation
Validates employees’ break lengths. When enabled, the clock doesn’t allow employees to clock in
from a break if the break they took didn’t meet the scheduled duration.
Break Start Validation
Validates employees’ break start times when they clock out for a break. When enabled, the clock
doesn’t allow employees to clock out for a break unless they are scheduled for one.

-- 226 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 227 of 0
Clock Entry Order Validation
Validates the order in which employees perform clock entries. For example, when enabled, the
clock doesn’t allow employees to clock out before they’ve clocked in for the day.
Consecutive Clock Entry Validation
Filters out consecutive clock entries of the same type time stamped within a specified time (for
example, when two directionless clock entries occur within a short time). The times are specified
in the application when time entry policies are set up.
Device Group Validation
Validates that the employee is eligible to perform clock entries using clocks in that device group.
Device Org Unit Validation
Validates that the employee is allowed to perform clock entries at the clock based on their work
assignment.
Directionless Clocking Validation
When the clock is using directionless clocking mode, this validation resolves directionless clock
entries to their “assumed” clock entry type.
Docket Validation
Validates the docket that the employees select when recording docket transfers.
Duplicate Clock Entry Validation
Validates that there aren’t any duplicate clock entries with the same type and time.
Employee Badge Validation
Validates employees badge numbers.
Employee Docket Validation
Validates that an employee is assigned to the docket they select when recording a docket
transfer.
Employee Job Assignment Validation
Validates that an employee is assigned to the job assignment they select when recording a job
assignment transfer.
Employee Location Validation

-- 227 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 228 of 0
Validates that an employee is assigned to the location they select when recording a location
transfer.
Employee PIN Validation
Validates the employee and supervisor PINs. This validation is used only if the clock is configured
to prompt for PINs in the <system> section.
Employee Project Validation
Validates that an employee is assigned to the project that they select when recording a project
transfer.
Employee Status Validation
Validates that the employee performing a clock entry has the necessary time entry policy
assigned and is active in the application.
Employee Transfer Validation
Validates that an employee can transfer to the work assignment that they selected for a work
transfer.
In With Transfer Validation
Validates that an employee can clock in and transfer to the work assignment they selected for a
work transfer.
Job Assignment Transfer Validation
Validates that an employee is permitted to record a job assignment transfer for the specified job
assignment.
Job Assignment Validation
Validates that a job assignment with the specified transfer code exists.
Labor Metrics Code Assigned Validation
Validates that an employee is assigned to the labor metrics code they select when recording a
labor metrics transfer.
Labor Metrics Code Validation
Validates that an employee entered a valid labor metrics code when recording a labor metrics
transfer.
Labor Metrics Time Entry Policy Validation

-- 228 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 229 of 0
Validates that the labor metrics type specified by the employee during a labor metrics transfer is
assigned to the time entry policy.
Labor Metrics Type Validation
Validates that the employee entered a valid labor metrics type when recording a labor metrics
transfer.
Location Validation
Validates that a location with the specified transfer code exists.
Manager Validation
Validates whether missed clock entries that were submitted by employees on Dayforce clocks in
self-service mode were approved or denied by their manager in Approvals.
Meal End Validation
Validates employees’ meal end times when they clock back in from a meal. When enabled, the
clock doesn’t allow employees to clock in from a meal when they aren’t scheduled to.
Meal Length Validation
Validates employees’ meal lengths. When enabled, the clock doesn’t allow employees to clock in
from a meal if the meal they took didn’t meet the scheduled duration.
Meal Start Validation
Validates employees’ meal start times when they clock out for a meal. When enabled, the clock
doesn’t allow employees to clock out for a meal unless they are scheduled for one.
Meal Subsidy Validation
Validates the meal subsidy entered by the employee on the clock based on your organization’s
time entry policy.
Multi Transfer Validation
Validates the multiple transfer codes that employees enter.
Network Location Validation
Validates the IP address associated with clock entries. This must be selected if you want to restrict
clock entries by IP address.
Out With Meal Break Validation

-- 229 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 230 of 0
Validates the information employees record when completing out with meal break clock entries,
and ensures that the meals and breaks the employees recorded fall within the shift times.
Pay Period Locked Validation
Validates that a clock entry doesn’t occur during a locked pay period.
Pay Period Transmitted Validation
Validates that a clock entry doesn’t occur during a transmitted pay period.
Picture Validation
For Dayforce Touch Clocks configured to use picture capture, validates that the clock was able to
capture a picture of the employee with their clock entry.
Note: The clock itself doesn’t compare the employee’s picture with the picture stored in the
database. Managers must manually compare the pictures in the application using the Clock Entry
Audits feature or in the Clock Data panel in the Timesheets feature.
Project Validation
Validates the project that the employees select when recording project transfers.
Quantity Validation
Validates the quantity that employees select when recording a docket transfer.
Shift End Validation
Validates employees’ shift end times when they clock out. When enabled, the clock doesn’t allow
employees to clock out for a shift if it violates their time entry policy (for example, clocking out too
early).
Shift Start Validation
Validates employees’ shift start times when they clock in. When enabled, the clock doesn’t allow
employees to clock in for a shift unless they’re scheduled.
Start System Validation
Validates that the clock time is correct.
Supervisor Badge Validation
Validates that the badge swiped to enter into supervisor mode belongs to a supervisor.

-- 230 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 231 of 0
Supervisor mode is used by managers, or other users set up as supervisors, to override other
clock validations. An example of this is clocking in on an employee’s behalf if they weren’t
scheduled, or if they’re trying to clock in later than the clock is configured to allow.
Supervisor Shift Override Validation
Not a validation, but used to return a message to the clock stating that a shift override is in effect.
Tip Type Validation
Validates the tip type that the user selects when recording tips.
Transfer Validation
Validates the transfer code employees enter.
Unordered Clock Entry Validation
Validates the order in which employees perform clock entries and rejects them if they’re out of
order. For example, when enabled, the application verifies that the employee didn’t clock out
before they clocked in for the day.
Encryption Methods
In System Admin > Encryption, you can configure encryption methods to be used by Dayforce
features such as exports and background jobs. Three encryption types are available: PGP, DES,
and Triple DES. Each have different requirements, depending on which type you’re configuring.
For DES or Triple DES encryption, you need to enter values in the Key and Initialization Vector
fields. For PGP encryption, you need to enter a value in the PGP PKey field.
If you’re using PGP encryption, and you’re importing files, make sure that the import files use only
the .csv extension, not the .pgp extension, or the files won’t load. See File Requirements.
For best results, add only one encryption method per encryption key.
Important: DES and Triple DES are provided for legacy integrations with environments that aren't
capable of using PGP. These encryption types shouldn’t be used for new integrations, because
these encryption algorithms are no longer considered secure. Use PGP encryption whenever
possible.
See the following topics:
Configure Encryption Methods
Configure Encryption by Background Job
Configure Encryption Methods

-- 231 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 232 of 0
In System Admin > Encryption, in the Encryption Methods tab, you can configure encryption
methods that can be used when you define export definitions.
To set up an encryption method:
1. Go to System Admin > Encryption.
2. In the Encryption Methods tab, click Add.
3. In the Name field, enter a name for the new encryption method.
4. In the Type drop-down list, select an encryption type.
5. Enter encryption information, depending on the encryption type:
DES and Triple DES require a key and an initialization vector.
PGP requires a key.
6. Click Save.
After you create and configure the encryption methods, you can select them as options when you
create export options. See Configure Export Options.
Configure Encryption by Background Job
In System Admin > Encryption, in the Encryption by Background Job tab, you can configure
encryption methods to be applied to exports associated with a selected background job. PGP
encryption is recommended.
You can configure one encryption method to be used for all background jobs by following the
steps below and selecting All in the Background Job drop-down list. Alternatively, you can select
a job from the list to configure the method only for that job. When you set up an encryption
method for a specific job, then that method overrides the method that was created with All as the
job name.
To configure an encryption method for a background job:
1. Go to System Admin > Encryption.
2. Click the Encryption by Background Job tab, then click Add.
3. In the Name field, enter a name for the new encryption method.
4. In the Background Job drop-down list, select a job name, or select All to apply the
encryption method to all background job exports.
5. In the Type drop-down list, select an encryption type.
6. Enter encryption information, depending on the encryption type:
DES and Triple DES require a key and an initialization vector.
PGP requires a key.
7. Click Save.
Export Definitions

-- 232 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 233 of 0
Dayforce contains functionality that you can use to export data from Dayforce into your
organization's other internal systems. For example, you can export employee information in bulk to
use for reporting or analytics in another system.
The export framework uses export definition files, which are in XML format. In the XML of the
export definition, you can specify the output details including the file name, parameters for the
contents of the file, and formatting.
Your Dayforce administrator will be given access to a secure FTP site where exported files are
placed in subdirectories based on export type. You can define the export file's name in the export
definition XML. Some XML templates are provided and you can use one of them when creating
your export definition. Users will need some understanding of XML to define the export definition.
It’s recommended that the file name include a timestamp to avoid overwriting any previous files.
See the following topics:
View Export Definitions
Create an Export Definition
Audit Information for Export Definitions
Configure Export Options
Filter HR Export
View Export Definitions
You can view data export definitions in Integrations > Export Definitions. The left side of the
screen shows a list of existing definitions, sorted into custom and system categories, and
subcategories based on the type of export. To refine the list, click Filter and add values for the
following filters: Name, Description, Export Type, and Export Options.
Create an Export Definition
In Integrations > Export Definitions, you can create export definitions to establish how data is
exported from Dayforce. When you build an export definition, you can start with a copy of an
existing one, or you can create one from scratch. You can use one of the XML templates that have
been provided to correspond with integrations in Dayforce such as the benefits export, or you can
edit the XML to suit your needs.
To create an export definition:
1. Go to Integrations > Export Definitions.
2. In the Export Definitions tab, do one of the following:
If the export definition you’re adding is similar to an existing one, click Copy and then
follow the rest of the steps below to edit the copy.
If you want to create a new export definition, click Add.

-- 233 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 234 of 0
3. Enter a name and description for the export definition.
4. (Optional) Select an option in the Export Option drop-down list. The options are configured
in the Export Options tab. See Configure Export Options.
Send the file to a specific SFTP other than the default one
Encrypt the file
Include headers
Include options related to Dayforce Link
5. (Optional) Select an option in the Pay Group drop-down list. The export includes data for
only the selected pay group.
6. Select an option in the Export Type drop-down list that corresponds to the type of data you’ll
be exporting. For more information about the different data export types listed, download
the Dayforce Interface Specifications ZIP file and see the files in the Exports folder.
7. (Optional) Click the Browse XML Templates link to view the XML templates that correspond
to the export type that you have selected. Complete this step if you want to use a
predefined template that corresponds to a specific integration (for example, benefit exports
for chosen vendors), or if you want to use a template as a base for your own definition.
8. (Optional) Select an option in the Template drop-down list and click Apply XML Template.
9. Edit the XML as required, and then click Validate. Dayforce shows any validation issues in
the Problems panel.
10. Note: Dayforce exports have a maximum row size of 8060 bytes. This validation looks only
at the structure of the XML and not at the expected row size for the export. You can avoid
failure of your export by including only the necessary columns in the export definition.
10. Click Save.
Audit Information for Export Definitions
Dayforce tracks all changes that are made to export definitions. You can view a list of the changes
in the Audit tab of the Export Definitions tab of Integrations > Export Definitions. When you go to
the Audit tab, a list of changes for the selected definition is shown with the date and time of the
change and the name of the user who made the change. You can click a row in the list to view
more details.
If a change was made by an employee, you can click the icon next to the person's name to view
more information in their employee card.
Configure Export Options
This section describes how to define the export options that control how Dayforce sends data
export files. Dayforce can be configured to send the files over FTP or SFTP. The export definitions
that you configure in the Export Options tab can be used for the export definitions that you
configure in the Export Definitions tab.
To create an export option:

-- 234 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 235 of 0
1. Go to Integrations > Export Definitions and click the Export Options tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and description for the option.
4. In the Output Type drop-down list, select the protocol to be used to send the export files to
a specific server.
Note: With Standard selected, the export files are saved on the Dayforce server and you
can't specify a server to send the export files to.
5. Select an option in the Encryption drop-down list. Encryption methods are configured in
System Admin > Encryption. See Encryption Methods.
6. If you selected an option other than Standard in the Output drop-down list:
a. Enter the server's details in the Host, Port, Login, and Password fields.
b. In the Folder field, enter the path of the folder you want export files saved in.
c. (Optional) In the Command field, enter any additional FTP or SFTP commands.
d. (Optional) Provide the key required to authenticate to the server in the SSH Key field.
7. Click Save.
Note: The options shown in the Dayforce section are used only to integrate with Dayforce
products.
To define options to integrate with other Dayforce products:
1. Select the Generate File Header checkbox to generate export files with a header.
2. Select an option in the Database Type drop-down list.
3. For exports processed by Dayforce Link, select the Generate Dayforce Link Header to
generate export files with a header.
4. Specify IDs in the Dayforce Link Recipient ID and Dayforce Link 401K Plan ID or Acct
Number fields for exports sent through the Dayforce Link. The plan ID should be a 5-digit
numeric value.
5. Select the Allow Tab Characters In Dayforce Link File checkbox to transmit the pay run
export data using a tab-delimited file.
6. Click Save.
Update Export Options
You can update custom export options in the Export Options tab of Integrations > Export
Definitions. System export options are read-only and can't be updated. If you want to update a
system export option, you can make a copy of it and edit the copy.
To update an export option, select it in the list of the left side of the screen and update the settings
as required and click Save. You can click Refresh to revert the changes you have made since the
last time you clicked Save.

-- 235 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 236 of 0
Note: To void the Password or SSH Key, you must erase the current one and then click Save. To
edit the Password or SSH Key, erase the current one first before adding the new one.
Filter HR Export
In the Export Definitions tab of Integrations > Export Definitions, the MappingDefinitions tag
in the XML code of export definitions supports the eq (equals) operator. You can use this operator
to filter the HR Export to include only employees who are assigned a record with a specific value.
For example, an organization requires that the HR Export only includes employees who are
assigned a specific checkbox employee property and have the checkbox selected. For the export
definition to perform this filtering, the Criteria tag in the XML contains the item attribute with
the reference code of the employee property, and the op attribute contains the eq operator:
<MappingDefinitions>
<definition>
<criteriaset>
<criteria item="EmployeePropertyXrefCode35" op="eq">True</criteria>
</criteriaset>
</definition>
</MappingDefinitions>
AI Assistant Configuration
In AI Assistant Admin, you can configure several AI Assistant features to meet your organization's
requirements.
The following topics contain more information about each configuration option:
Configure Disclaimers for AI Assistant
Configure Messages for AI Assistant
Configure Content Settings for AI Assistant
Configure Disclaimers for AI Assistant
In AI Assistant Admin, in the Disclaimers tab, administrators can customize the legal disclaimer for
AI Assistant. By default, AI Assistant shows a generic disclaimer telling employees that responses
might not be specific to their terms of employment, and advising them to refer to company
policies or their contract to confirm the response. You can customize the disclaimer and add links
to relevant resources. AI Assistant disclaimers can be up to 250 characters.
Role feature access: AI Assistant Admin
You can localize the disclaimer for each culture that is enabled in your Dayforce environment. The
list of disclaimers shows you which culture is the default for your organization. If an employee is

-- 236 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 237 of 0
using Dayforce in a culture that doesn’t have a disclaimer configured, they see the disclaimer for
the default culture. The default culture is configured in Site Setup > Client, in the Cultures tab.
A good disclaimer clearly states what AI Assistant can and can’t do, recommends that users verify
important information, and provides links for these details. For example, “Content might not be
specific to your terms of employment. Confirm by checking your company's policies or applicable
contracts.” If you don’t customize the disclaimer, AI Assistant shows a generic disclaimer by
default.
Add a Disclaimer
To add a disclaimer:
1. Go to AI Assistant Admin and click the Disclaimers tab.
2. Click New disclaimer.
3. Select the culture for the new disclaimer.
4. Enter the disclaimer text. You can click the link icon to add links to the text.
5. Click Save.
Edit a Disclaimer
To edit a disclaimer:
1. Go to AI Assistant Admin and click the Disclaimers tab.
2. In the list of disclaimers, find the one that you want to update and click the more actions
icon next to it.
3. Click Edit.
4. In the Edit disclaimer dialog box, update the text and click Save changes.
Delete a Disclaimer
To delete a disclaimer:
1. Go to AI Assistant Admin and click the Disclaimers tab.
2. In the list of disclaimers, find the one that you want to delete and click the more actions icon
next to it.
3. Click Delete.
4. In the confirmation dialog box, click Delete disclaimer.
Configure Messages for AI Assistant
In AI Assistant Admin, in the Messages tab, administrators can configure a custom message that
helps employees to find assistance when AI Assistant can’t give an appropriate response. The
message could contain contact details for their HR department or other information to help
employees find what they need. The message is shown when an employee uses the thumbs
down icon and submits negative feedback about AI Assistant.

-- 237 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 238 of 0
Before You Begin: If your organization uses HR Service Delivery, you don’t need to configure a
message because AI Assistant shows the Create a Case button instead of the message.
Role feature access: AI Assistant Admin
You can add a message for each culture that is enabled in your Dayforce environment. The list of
messages shows you which culture is the default for your organization. If an employee is using
Dayforce in a culture that doesn’t have a message configured, they see the message for the
default culture. The default culture is configured in Site Setup > Client, in the Cultures tab.
Add a Message
To add a message:
1. Go to AI Assistant Admin and click the Messages tab.
2. Click New message.
3. Select the culture for the new message.
4. Enter the message text. You can use the text editor to format the message as needed.
5. Click Save.
Edit a Message
To edit a message:
1. Go to AI Assistant Admin and click the Messages tab.
2. In the list of messages, find the one that you want to update.
3. Click the more actions icon next to the message in the list.
4. Click Edit.
5. In the Edit message dialog box, update the message and click Save changes.
Delete a Message
To delete a message:
1. Go to AI Assistant Admin and click the Messages tab.
2. In the list of messages, find the one that you want to delete.
3. Click the more actions icon next to the message in the list.
4. Click Delete.
5. In the confirmation dialog box, click Delete message.
Configure Content Settings for AI Assistant
In AI Assistant Admin, in the Content Settings tab, administrators can specify whetherAI
Assistant's responses include Dayforce guide content. When you allow guide content, AI
Assistant's responses can include information about features that your organization doesn't use. If

-- 238 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 239 of 0
you don’t want your employees to see this kind of user guide content, you can exclude that
content from AI Assistant's responses.
Role feature access: AI Assistant Admin
The Content Settings tab contains the Use Dayforce user guides switch. With the switch set to on,
AI Assistant uses Dayforce guide content when it generates responses to employee questions.
With the switch set to off, AI Assistant doesn't use Dayforce user guide content when it generates
responses.
Configure Disclaimers
Disclaimers are messages that Dayforce shows when you first log in. Dayforce prompts you to
accept the message before you can finish logging in.
To configure disclaimers:
1. Go to System Admin > Disclaimer and click Add.
2. Enter information in the Disclaimer Name, Disclaimer, Effective From, and Effective To fields.
3. To choose your organization, click Add in the grid below and then click the Organization
field. The organization hierarchy window opens, where you select and add your
organization.
4. Select the Display to Everyone checkbox.
5. Note: Selecting this checkbox shows the disclaimer to everyone in the associated
organization, regardless of whether the Show Disclaimer checkbox in System Admin > User
is selected for a given user.
5. (Optional) To localize the disclaimer message in the language of your choice:
a. Select your disclaimer and then click Localize.
b. In the Localize Disclaimer dialog box, click Add.
c. In the Language drop-down list, select your desired language.
d. Enter a name and, optionally, a description.
e. Click Save.
6. Click Save.
When you log in, Dayforce shows your disclaimer:

-- 239 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 240 of 0
When you click Next, Dayforce shows the Home page. If you click Cancel, Dayforce takes you
back to the login page.
Configure Exchange Rates
You can configure base currency and exchange rates in System Admin > Exchange Rates.
To configure base currency and exchange rates:
1. Go to System Admin > Exchange Rates.
2. In the General section, select an option in the Base Currency drop-down list.
3. Note: Dayforce doesn't convert currencies until currency conversion is enabled. After
currency conversion is enabled, you can't change the base currency.
3. In the Exchange Rates section, click Add.
4. Select an option in the Currency drop-down list.
5. Enter a value in the Exchange Rate field. This is the amount of the associated currency that
is exchanged for 1 USD.
6. Enter a date in the Effective From field and, optionally, the Effective To field.
7. Click Save.
Localization
In Dayforce, you can localize your organization's data, label/buttons, alert messages, and feature
names. Dayforce automatically shows localized text in many areas, based on the user's language
preferences (also called a culture setting). See Client Cultures.
Some areas of Dayforce aren't automatically translated, such as data created by users (for
example, pay categories, pay types, job names, and relationship types). For this data, you can
"localize" Dayforce to suit your organization's needs, meaning that you can customize your
organization's data according to a specific culture.
There are two reasons that you might want to use the localization feature:

-- 240 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 241 of 0
To localize the text that isn’t already translated (that is, user-created data).
To customize the text that is already provided. For example, you could change the New
button to Create.
This section includes the following tasks:
Localize Data
Localize Labels
Localize Notifications
Show Localization Keys
Localize Data
In Dayforce, you can localize your organization’s data. Data refers to the information that you enter
to customize Dayforce, such as pay categories, pay types, job names, and relationship types.
Role feature access: Application Container > Main Application UI > Localization
To localize data:
1. Go to the feature that you want to localize.
2. Click the data that you want to change. For example, to display a job title in French, click
the job name, such as Assistant Manager:
3. Click Localize. A dialog box opens that shows the existing localizations for the selected
data.
4. Click Add.
5. In the Language drop-down list, select a language. See Client Cultures.
6. In the Name field, enter the label as you want it to appear to the user.
7. In the Description field, enter the description as you want it to appear to the user.
8. Click Save.

-- 241 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 242 of 0
Note: To view your changes, you must have a user profile set up for the selected culture and log in
using that profile in a new session. See View User Accounts.
Show Localization Keys
Before you can localize labels or alerts, you must show localization keys. See Localize Labels and
Localize Notifications.
You can show localization keys by clicking the localize icon ( ) in the Dayforce header bar.
Click the localize button again to hide the keys.
Here’s an example showing the Save button in normal mode and in localization mode:
1.
Localization modes
Normal Mode 	Localization Mode
Role feature access: Application Container > Main Application UI > Localize Interface
Continue to the steps described in Localize Labels.
Localize Labels
In Dayforce, you can localize labels including buttons, column headers, and field names. For
example, you could change the Add button to Create.
Before You Begin: Ensure that you completed the steps described in Show Localization Keys.
Role feature access: Application Container > Main Application UI > Localization
To localize labels:
1. Go to the feature that you want to localize.
2. Locate the label that you want to localize and take note of the KEY: label
3. Click the user icon ( ) at the top right of the screen.
4. Click KEY: lblLocalize. The lblOverrideLabelStrings dialog box opens, which shows a list of
the existing label overrides.
5. Click Key: lblNew.
6. In the %%%Label%%% column, enter the name of the label that you want to change using
the same name displayed in localization mode. For example, to localize the New button,
enter lblNew.
7. In the KEY: Value column, enter the label as you want it to appear to the user. For example,
if you want the New button to display as Create, enter Create.

-- 242 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 243 of 0
8. In the KEY: Language column, select a language from the drop-down list. See Client
Cultures.
9. Click Save.
Note: To view your changes, you must have a user profile set up for the selected language and
log in using that profile in a new session. See View User Accounts.
Localize Notifications
Dayforce provides default messages for all notifications but you can localize the text in the subject
and body of notifications.
Most messages contain tokens, or variables, (such as, {0} or {1}) that Dayforce replaces with
information when the notification is sent. For example, to change the default message to alert the
user when associates are overdue for a meal or break, you can set up a message that includes
the names of the associates: "The following associates are due for a meal: {0}", where {0}
represents the names of the associates.
Before You Begin: You must assign the Application Container > Main Application UI > Localization
feature to the user roles responsible for localizing labels and notifications. See Role Features. You
also need to display the localization keys. See Show Localization Keys.
Important: Removing or modifying tokens significantly changes the meaning of the notification.
Edit tokens with caution.
To localize notifications:
1. Go to System Admin > System Notifications.
2. In the Subscriptions tab, click the notification that you want to localize.
3. Click the user icon at the top right of the screen.

-- 243 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 244 of 0
4. Click KEY: lblLocalize. The lblOverrideLabelStrings dialog box opens, which shows a list of
the existing label overrides.
5. Click KEY: lbl New.
6. In the %%% Label %%% column, enter the notification label. For example, to change the
message that Dayforce shows to associates when they’re due for a meal, enter
alertMealBreakOverDueAlertContent.
7. In the KEY: Value column, enter the notification as you want it to appear to the user. For
example, The following employees must be hungry: {0}.
8. In the KEY: Language column, select a language from the drop-down list. See Client
Cultures.
9. Click Save.
