Cross-Reference Codes
Cross-reference codes, sometimes referred to as reference codes or XREF codes, are used in
import and export files as unique identifiers for elements and entries being imported or exported.
For example, these cross-reference codes can uniquely identify each element of an org unit,
individual pay groups, or specific entries in employee records.
You can add many cross-reference codes directly to entries that you’re making in Dayforce, like
the Reference Code column for a legal entity in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity, or
the Reference Code field in Pay Setup > Pay Groups, in the Pay Group Properties tab.
System cross-reference codes can’t be added or edited in Dayforce, but must be included in
import and export files.
See the following topics:

-- 263 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 264 of 0
Cross-Reference Codes
System-Defined Cross-Reference Codes
Cross-Reference Codes
Cross-reference codes, also known as reference codes and XREF codes, are used by Dayforce in
imports and exports to integrate into other applications and systems used by your organization.
Cross-reference codes can also help you identify the different elements in the application in the
scripts and processes that export your organization's data from Dayforce.
You enter cross-reference codes in Dayforce for the elements in the application that you're
creating that will be included in imports and exports, such as your organization's jobs or
departments.
As a best practice, it’s recommended that you enter a cross-reference code that logically
represents the element that you’re creating. For example, if you’re configuring a Clerk Job in
Dayforce, you might use Clerk_Job as the cross-reference code. As long as each element has a
unique code, it can be used in exports of those elements to another system.
Elements in Dayforce don’t always need cross-reference codes to work properly, unless those
elements will be used in imports or exports, in which case, you only need to include reference
codes for those elements to be imported or exported. Nevertheless, it’s best practice to include
cross-reference codes in all entries for which you can in Dayforce in case the entries are ever
used for imports or exports.
System-Defined Cross-Reference Codes
Some fields don’t have cross-reference codes that can be edited or viewed in the Dayforce user
interface. To ensure that the required information is included in imports, you must include the
appropriate cross-reference codes for those elements. Some of these system-defined cross-
reference codes are described in the following sections:
EEO-1 Job Category
FLSA Status Cross-Reference Codes
KldB Job Classification
HR Incident Body Parts
HR Incident Injuries
Safety and Health Types

KldB Job Classification
The KldB Job Classification drop-down list is found in the Additional Job Details section of the
Jobs and Job Assignments tab in Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments. The
JobClassificationGlobalXRefCode is an 8-digit number comprised of the following:
Digits 1-5 represent the 5 digit KldB job classification code. These are listed on the Federal
Employment Agency's statistics website here. These are the numbers listed in the KldB Job
Classification drop-down list.
Digits 6-8 are 000 and are reserved for future use. When you import these codes, you must
ensure that the zeros have been included with the Federal Employment Agency's 5-digit
number for the job.
For example, the JobClassificationGlobalXRefCode for the job “Commissioned officers” is
01104000.

Security Configuration
Dayforce security settings are used to determine which users can access various areas of
Dayforce, such as department managers accessing Schedules but not People, and what
information they can access, create, or update.
Users need a user name to log in to Dayforce. The user name is associated with one or more user
roles. The user role determines which features the role has access to and the authorizations that
determine what the role can do in those features.
User names are configured in System Admin > User.
User roles are configured in System Admin > Roles.
Features are configured in System Admin > Roles in the Features tab.
Authorizations are configured in System Admin > Roles in the Authorizations tab.
This following topics describe these concepts in more detail:
User Roles
Role Features
Configure User Role Authorizations
Password Policies
User Roles
User roles control which features users can access in Dayforce, and they play an important part in
the security of Dayforce. User roles are assigned to user names. Security Configuration describes
the differences between user roles and user names.
You can configure as many user roles as your organization requires in System Admin > Roles. The
more granular the access requirements, the more user roles you'll need to configure.
For example, if your organization needed to provide access to a different set of features for
corporate management, location managers, assistant managers, and employees, you'd configure
four user roles, one for each of those groups.
Note that the term ESS (employee self-service) is used throughout Dayforce documentation.
Configurations can be different, depending on the needs of your organization, but ESS generally
refers to features that individual employees can access directly. These can include individual
earning statements, annual tax forms, timesheets, and various forms they can use to update tax or
other records.
When you’re creating user roles, you can arrange them in a hierarchy of parent and child roles.
Users with the highest level of access can assign features to other roles, and child roles can only

-- 270 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 271 of 0
use features to which they have been assigned access. Users can only assign features to other
user roles at or below their own role's level in the hierarchy.
See Configure User Roles.
User Role Properties
You can configure several different properties for each user role.
User role properties
Name 	Description
Name 	The name for the user role.
Description 	The description of the user role.
Parent Role 	The role under which the new role will be nested in the hierarchy.
Password Policy
The password policy that will govern the role. Required. This setting is
automatically populated with the default password policy, which is
configured in System Admin > Password Policy. See Password Policies.
ESS Role
Allows users with the role to access Dayforce through Employee Self-
Service.
With this checkbox selected, new users assigned this role don’t need to
be assigned additional security settings that are needed for other roles
that manage organizational units. This means that when this role is
selected while onboarding a new employee, Dayforce disables the
Location Visibility drop-down list in the New Hire form.
Termination Role
Allows users with the role to have limited access to required features of
Dayforce after their employment has been terminated.
You can only configure one termination role. If you select the
Termination Role checkbox when a termination role already exists,
Dayforce displays a prompt confirming if you want to change the current
termination role.
You must configure the termination role with the appropriate limited role
features and access authorizations. For example, if employees need to
access their historical earnings statements and year-end tax forms after

-- 271 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 272 of 0
their employment has been terminated, only these features and
authorizations should be assigned to the termination role.
The termination role functionality relies on the User Account Employee
Status Job to assign the role to terminated employees. See User
Account Employee Status Job.
Reference Code
The cross-reference code for the role. Cross-reference codes are used
to import and export data from Dayforce to other applications. See
Cross-Reference Codes.
Onboarding Role
Identifies the role as an onboarding role.
Onboarding roles allow new employees to access Dayforce before their
first day. This functionality is especially useful in the Onboarding
module, so that new hires can access these features before they
officially start work.
For more information, see the Onboarding Guide.

-- 272 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 273 of 0
access Dayforce using their Dayforce-specific credentials after
their SSO account is removed.
If your organization has the OData reporting feature enabled,
users with access to OData must have this option enabled to
retrieve data from Dayforce. OData doesn't support SSO users.
Exclude Employees
with this Role
from Delegation
Designates the user role as ineligible for delegation. With this option
selected, users with this role aren't displayed when configuring
delegation.
Anonymize TAFW for
employees with this
role
Select this checkbox and Dayforce restricts some time away requests
for the role. When this checkbox is selected and there’s a time away
request that involves a pay code that’s configured with the Is
TAFW and Is Anonymized checkboxes selected in Pay Setup > Pay
Code, Dayforce does the following for the role:
Hides the request in Approvals.
Shows the request in features such as Multi-Week Calendar,
Schedules, and Timesheets, but without the unique time away
reason (for example, Sick or Personal).
See Anonymization for Time Away Pay Codes.
Related topics:
Configure User Roles
Role Features
Configure User Role Authorizations
Configure User Roles
Before You Begin: Ensure that you're familiar with the general concepts about user roles in
Dayforce. See User Roles.
To configure a user role:
1. Go to System Admin > Roles.
2. Click Add.
3. In the General tab, configure the user role properties as required.
4. Click Save.
To continue configuring the user role, you need to complete these tasks:

-- 273 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 274 of 0
Role Features
Configure User Role Authorizations
After you configure user roles, you must assign them to users as part of the user configuration
process. See User Configuration.
Role Features
Role features map areas (or features) in Dayforce to the roles that can use them. You might
configure the role features for the location manager role type with access to both Schedules and
People, and configure the assistant manager role type with access to Schedules only.
Important: Not all features are displayed for all roles. Child roles can only view and update the role
features that have been assigned to them by their parent role. For more information on configuring
role hierarchies, see User Roles.
Each role you set up needs to be assigned to at least one feature in the Features tab of System
Admin > Roles.
In the following screenshot, the Employee Profile, Organization Chart, People List, and Reports
features, under the People feature, are assigned to the Canadian Manager role:
Feature Types
After features are assigned to a role they are either displayed or not displayed in the navigation
panel. To distinguish these two feature types, Dayforce displays two icons in the feature tree.
Feature type icons
Icon 	Description

-- 274 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 275 of 0
Navigation Panel Feature: A feature is considered a navigation panel feature if it’s shown in
the navigation panel. Navigation panel features are generally one of the following:
Features that map to feature screens.
Containers for features, for example, System Admin, or HCM Anywhere.
Feature Component: A feature is considered a feature component if it doesn’t have a target
Dayforce screen associated with it, and can't be used as a link in the navigation panel.
Feature components are generally one of the following:
Tabs.
Control flags that determine the display of a section or data point on a screen.
Something that controls part of the functionality of a screen.
Validation
Dayforce uses validation to prevent you from mapping containers for features to the navigation
panel and Favorite Features tab if they don’t contain features that map to feature screens.
Dayforce displays validation errors if you attempt to save the following changes:
An empty container for a feature, for example, System Admin.
A container for a feature where the role doesn't have access to the subfeature. For example,
if a role that has access to a feature but not the subfeature, users who are assigned that role
won’t see the subfeatures.
Validation error messages specify the navigation panel features that need to be fixed. You can
make corrections in the feature tree either by clearing the checkbox for the empty container, or by
selecting at least one navigation panel feature that is mapped to a feature screen.
See Assign Role Features.
Assign Role Features
To view descriptions of each feature and subfeature, see Appendix: Role Feature Library.
Before You Begin: Make sure that you're familiar with the general concepts associated with role
features. See Role Features.
To assign features and subfeatures to a role:
1. Go to System Admin > Roles and select a role.
2. Click the Features tab.
3. Select the checkboxes next to the features that you want to assign to the role. Most features
have subfeatures (children) underneath them. You need to first select the top (parent)

Configure User Role Authorizations
Role authorizations define what access rights a role has to different types of information in
Dayforce. You can assign four types of authorizations:
Can Create: The role can add new items of the associated information.
Can Read: The role can read items of the associated information.
Can Update: The role can edit the details of existing items of the associated information.
Can Delete: The role can delete items of the associated information.
See Apply Access Authorizations to Grids.
When you assign the Can Create, Can Update, or Can Delete access authorization, you should
also assign the Can Read authorization to ensure that the user role can view the information that
the role will access.

-- 282 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 283 of 0
Not all access authorizations are shown for all roles. Child roles can only view and update the
access authorizations that were assigned to them by their parent role. See User Roles.
Each role can have one, several, or no authorizations for a type of information in Dayforce. For
example, you could grant access to a Payroll Administrator role to all four authorizations for the
Pay Export Configuration item, which means users assigned the Payroll Administrator role can
read the Pay Export XML definitions configured in Pay Setup, change them, create an export
definition, or delete existing definitions, while a user with the Store Manager role that has only Can
Read access can view the export definitions but can't add, update, or delete Pay Export
XML definitions.
A role's authorizations can impact different areas of Dayforce. For example, the Pay Information
authorization impacts the ability to view employee pay rates and amounts in several timesheets
features. Roles without Can Read access for this authorization can't view this pay data, even when
they’re assigned role access to the features.
Access authorizations also control permissions for forms. When a user with a role that has
authorization to access to a form is assigned Can Create access, but not Can Update or Can
Delete access for the associated authorization, that user can create new employee records but
can't edit or delete existing records.
You can define as many role authorizations as you need to implement appropriate information
security. To assign role authorizations to role types:
1. Go to System Admin > Roles and select a role in the list.
2. Click the Authorizations tab.
3. Select the checkboxes for Can Create, Can Read, Can Update, or Can Delete
corresponding with each authorization to grant access permissions to the selected role.
4. Click Save.
Define New Hire Role Assignment Access
This section describes how to define the role access of the user roles configured in Dayforce. Role
access is used to describe what roles users can assign to new hires they set up in People.
Typically, users can only assign roles with equal or less access than their own. For example, you
would configure the manager role to be able to assign the manager, assistant manager, and
employee roles.
Roles are used to define what access users have in Dayforce; whether they can create schedules,
review time and attendance, or edit employee records are all common examples of the kinds of
access they provide.
For example, if you define the Manager role as being assigned role access to the Employee role
when users with the Manager role set up new hires in People, they can assign the Employee role

-- 283 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 284 of 0
to the new hires. In turn, those new hires can access Dayforce according to the Employee role's
security access.
To define new hire role access:
1. Go to System Admin > Roles and select a role.
2. Click the New Hire Role Assignments tab.
3. Click Add.
4. Select the role that you want to grant access to from the drop-down list under the Role
heading.
5. Enter the effective from and effective to dates for the role.
6. Click Save.
Create Custom Login Algorithms
You can define a custom format for generating new employee user names in System Admin
> Client Properties using the Login Algorithm Custom Format field. This gives your organization
the flexibility to use its preferred custom format instead of a predefined one (that is, F.Last,
LAST.FIRST, and so on). For example, you can create a custom format that includes the
employee's first initial, followed by last name and then employee number.
Before You Begin: Login algorithms can generate user names only for employees hired through
the new hire workflow and not for employees added to Dayforce via HR Import.
To define a custom login algorithm format:
1. Go to System Admin > Client Properties.
2. Click the Properties tab and then go to the Employee section.
3. In the Login Algorithm Custom Format field, enter any of the following tokens, in any
combination, depending on what format you want the user name to follow:
{FIRST}: Employee first name.
{LAST}: Employee last name.
{F}: First letter of employee first name.
{EMPLOYEENUMBER}: Employee number.
4. (Optional) Enter any of the following characters in combination with the tokens described in
step 3:
English alphabet characters (a–z)
Note: Letter case doesn't matter when creating user names because they aren't case
sensitive.
Base 10 digits (0–9)
Non-alphanumeric characters (such as, !._@,%$)
Unicode symbols (such as, éù£)
5. Click Save.

-- 284 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 285 of 0
Examples
The following screenshots show examples of custom formats for an employee named Allan Jones
whose employee number is 123456.
The following example format includes only tokens and no characters. Tokens used include the
employee's first initial followed by last name and employee number:
Using this format, Dayforce generates the following user name for Allan Jones: ajones123456
The next example also includes two tokens and one character, a period, between the tokens:
Here, Dayforce generates the following user name for Allan: jones.123456
Finally, the following example includes the company name (companyxyz), which isn’t a token, with
the employee number token:
Here, Allan is given the following user name: companyxyz123456
Note:
Dayforce doesn't require you to include a minimum or maximum number of tokens.
However, be sure to define a user name format so that it generates a unique user name for
each employee. For example, using only the {FIRST} token can be problematic because
many employees can have the same name.
User names can't exceed 128 characters or contain spaces.
User names are never case sensitive, regardless of the letter case that users type in the
Login Algorithm Custom Format field. For example, if you define this field with
CompanyXYZ{EMPLOYEENUMBER}, the user name generated won't require the employee to
enter any parts of their user name in uppercase letters.
Password Policies

-- 285 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 286 of 0
In Dayforce, you can define the password policies that you want to enforce for logging in and
using the application. To help secure Dayforce user accounts, you can use several optional
security features.
You must define at least one password policy. If necessary, you can define multiple password
policies that are assigned to different user roles. For example, you could have two password
policies, so that managers and administrators are assigned a stronger password policy than
employees.
In cases where a user has multiple user roles, and the roles are assigned different password
policies, Dayforce uses the strongest password policy assigned for that user. For example, if a
user is assigned both the Administrator and Manager user roles, but the Administrator user role
has a stronger password policy, Dayforce uses the password policy associated with the
Administrator role for that user. This means that when that user tries to change their password or
their PIN, Dayforce enforces the requirements defined in the Administrator password policy.
Note: Password policies impact every user that logs in to Dayforce and any changes to the policy
come into effect immediately; typically, a password policy is defined and configured before
Dayforce is in use by end users, but if you do need to make a change to the policy after users
have been logging on, ensure that it’s communicated to them in advance.
Add Password Policies
To add new password policies:
1. Go to System Admin > Password Policy.
2. Click Add.
3. Set the password policy security features by configuring the settings described in Password
Policy Parameters.
4. Click Save.
Password Policy Parameters
Properties
Name
The name for the password policy.
Description
A brief description of the password policy.
Default
Select this checkbox if this policy should be assigned by default.

-- 286 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 287 of 0
Default Password
Defines the default password assigned to new user accounts. Default passwords can contain any
of the following characters:
English uppercase characters (A through Z)
English lowercase characters (a through z)
Base 10 digits (0 through 9)
Nonalphabetic characters (for example, !, $, #, %)
Unicode symbols (for example, é, ù, £)
Default passwords must contain at least one token. Dayforce doesn’t allow you to save a
password policy if its default password doesn't contain any tokens. Examples of invalid
passwords include L0g1n! or P@33word123 or any combination of just letters, numbers, and
symbols.
You can use any of the available tokens, combined with other characters or on their own, to create
default passwords that are specific to each user.
Password tokens
Token 	Description
{BIRTHYEAR} 	Dayforce inserts the user's birth year into their default password.
{BIRTHMONTH} 	Dayforce inserts the user's birth month into their default password.
{BIRTHDAY} Dayforce inserts the user's birth day (for example, 25) into their
default password.
{FIRSTNAME} 	Dayforce inserts the user's first name into their default password.
{LASTNAME} 	Dayforce inserts the user's last name into their default password.
{LAST3SSN} Dayforce inserts the last three digits of the user's Social Security
number into their default password.
{LAST4SSN} Dayforce inserts the last four digits of the user's Social Security
number into their default password.
{EMPLOYEENUMBER} Dayforce inserts the user's employee number into their default
password.
For example, with the default password {BIRTHYEAR}Pass, new users are assigned default
passwords that are their birth year, plus the characters Pass. In this example, an employee who
was born in 1978 would have a default password of 1978Pass.
Note: When a new system user (for example, a system administrator, or other user who doesn't
have an employee record) is added in System Admin > User, Dayforce doesn't use the default
password from a password policy. Instead, the administrator enters a password in the Password
field when they create the user account in System Admin > User. See Add User Accounts.

-- 287 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 288 of 0
Default PIN
Enter the default PIN that Dayforce uses for new user accounts. Dayforce only accepts numeric
characters (that is, 0 to 9) and numeric tokens (for example, {BIRTHYEAR}).
Enforcement
Require Reset on Login
This checkbox controls whether users must change their password after it has been changed by
an administrator (typically when a system administrator resets the password). Select the checkbox
and users must reset their password the next time they log in after it has been changed by an
administrator.
Note: If the Enable Password Reset checkbox is selected in the Messages section of the
Properties tab in System Admin > Client Properties, this checkbox is enabled by default and can't
be changed. If the Enable Password Reset checkbox isn’t selected, you can clear the Require
Reset on Login checkbox and users don’t have to change their password the first time they log in.
However, if a default password is configured, Dayforce selects this checkbox by default when you
save the policy. This ensures that users who are provided a default password by the password
policy must change their password when they first log in.
Require Complex Password
This checkbox controls whether users must use complex or strong passwords when they’re
prompted to change their password.
Select the checkbox and users must use complex passwords. Clear the checkbox and complex
passwords aren't enforced.
Complex passwords must meet the following requirements:
The password might not contain any part of the user's full name or user account that is
greater than two characters long. Dayforce parses the user's full name for commas, dashes,
spaces, and other characters and checks for each separate section if any exist. For
example, a full name of Parr, Margaret H is parsed so that passwords can't contain 'Parr' or
'Margaret'; however passwords can contain the letter 'H' (the middle initial is 'skipped'
because it’s less than two characters long).
The password must contain characters from three of the following five categories:
English uppercase characters (A through Z)
English lowercase characters (a through z)
Base 10 digits (0 through 9)
Non-alphabetic characters (for example, !, $, #, %)
Unicode symbols (for example, é, ù,£ )

-- 288 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 289 of 0
History Duration
Enter the number of unique passwords (up to 24) a user account must specify before an old
password can be reused. The password history only checks for exact password matches when
determining if the user has specified a unique password. Enter 0 and the unique passwords
requirement isn’t enforced. Old passwords can always be reused.
Password
Minimum Length
Enter the minimum length (in number of characters) for the password. Passwords must be the
specified length (or longer). This value can't be blank or lower than six, and can't exceed the Max
Length value.
Maximum Length
Enter the maximum length (in number of characters) for the password. Passwords can't be the
longer than the specified length. This value can't be less than the Min Length value.
If you leave this field blank, Dayforce uses the default maximum length of 32 characters.
Minimum Age
Enter the number of days (up to 998) a new password must be used before the user can change
it. This value must be less than the Max Age value if Max Age isn’t set to 0. Enter 0 and the
minimum age requirement isn’t enforced; passwords can always be changed.
Important: Without a minimum password age, the unique password requirement set with the
History Duration parameter can't be enforced; users can cycle through passwords repeatedly until
they get to an old favorite.
Note: If the Require Reset on Login parameter is configured, Dayforce temporarily skips the Min
Age parameter, allowing for the user to create a new password on the first login. After the
password change, Dayforce continues to respect the Min Age parameter.
Maximum Age
Enter the maximum number of days a user can keep a password before it expires and they’re
prompted to change it. Enter 0 and passwords don’t expire.
Default Password Life (Hours)
Defines the amount of time, in hours, after which default passwords expire. Dayforce tracks when
default passwords are assigned to newly onboarded employees, either through an HR Import,

-- 289 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 290 of 0
People, or Self-Service forms, and only considers the password valid for the amount of time
specified.
For example, a system administrator could define that default passwords expire after 48 hours. An
employee is onboarded through the New Hire form on Monday, at 1:00 PM but that employee
doesn't attempt to log in to Dayforce until Friday morning. Because more than 48 hours have
elapsed since the default password was assigned, it has expired and the employee is prevented
from logging in to Dayforce.
If the employee logs in within 48 hours, in this example, and resets their password (or has it reset
by an administrator through System Admin > User), they can then log in normally using their new
password.
By default, this field is blank and default passwords don’t expire. With a value specified, Dayforce
expires default passwords after the specified number of hours have elapsed from when the
default password was first assigned to a new employee.
Note: The maximum value of the Default Password Life (hours) field is 720.
Password Lockout Rules
Failed Login attempts before Lockout
Enter the number of failed login attempts (up to 999) a user account can make before it’s locked
out. Enter 0 and Dayforce doesn't lock out user accounts for any number of failed login attempts.
Lock Account for (minutes)
Enter the number of minutes (up to 99,999) a user account remains locked out if it triggered the
Failed Login attempts before Lockout feature.
Enter 0 and the account is locked out indefinitely; it’s only unlocked when a system administrator
explicitly unlocks it.
Note: This parameter is only used if the Failed Login attempts before Lockout field has a value.
Employee Badge PIN
Minimum PIN Length
Enter the minimum number of characters for PINs. For example, to require PINs to be at least four
characters, enter 4.
Maximum PIN Length
Enter the maximum number of characters for PINs. For example, to limit PINs to four characters or
fewer, enter 4.

-- 290 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 291 of 0
Reorder Password Policies
Dayforce uses the order that password policies are arranged in to determine which password
policies are strongest. For this reason, you need to sort password policies by strength, so that the
strongest policy is at the top of the list.
When all of the necessary password policies are added, you can rearrange them using the Move
Up and Move Down buttons in System Admin > Password Policy:
Note: After you define the necessary password policies and sort them in the correct order, you
must assign the correct policy to each user role. See User Roles.
Two-Factor Authentication
Two-factor authentication (TFA) can be described as both "knowing" something and "having"
something. A user must know their user name and password, and they must have a device that is
registered to them. With two-factor authentication, Dayforce users log in to Dayforce as they
normally would, and then they’re prompted to verify their identity using a device registered to
them. This is especially useful for users who might have access to sensitive tasks like committing
payroll. However, it can be enabled for any user. This functionality can also be used with the
mobile app.
The following topics contain more details about how to use two-factor authentication with
Dayforce:
Duo Security Overview
Set Up Duo Security Accounts
Create the Dayforce Application in Duo Security
Enable Two-Factor Authentication in Dayforce
User Experience Using Two-Factor Authentication
Reset or Remove Users in Duo Security
Duo Security Overview
Dayforce uses Duo Security, a third-party provider, as one option for two-factor authentication. To
use this functionality, organizations need to create an account with Duo. The type of account
depends on the size of the organization. This is determined between Duo Security and the
organization.

-- 291 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 292 of 0
Note: Dayforce doesn't administer Duo accounts on behalf of its customers. Customers must
create an account with Duo and maintain it themselves to use two-factor authentication.
Administrators have access to a dashboard within their Duo account, where they can perform a
number of tasks including managing their enrolled users and customizing Duo's guided process.
For more information on Duo Security integration and services, see https://www.duosecurity.com/.
Service Level Agreement
One concern of integrating with a third party during the login process is that Dayforce is subject to
that third party’s availability. If the third party is offline, then Dayforce might be inaccessible (see
the section below regarding Fail Open vs. Fail Closed).
Duo publishes their SLA at https://www.duosecurity.com/sla. Per Mathew Varghese of Duo, their
uptime since inception is 99.995%. They have made improvements recently to increase uptime,
such as now being able to do upgrades without taking the system offline.
Set Up Duo Security Accounts
Before you can enable two-factor authentication, you must first set up an account with Duo
Security, enable that account for the appropriate API access, and generate the access keys.
Dayforce uses these APIs to allow users to log in using the Duo provided UI workflow process for
enrolling users the first time, and for authenticating them on subsequent logins.
The type of Duo Security account depends on the size of your organization, and must be
arranged by you and Duo Security.
It's critical that the account must support Web SDK integration and Admin API Integration. At the
time of writing, this is a Duo Security “Enterprise” account. You must ask Duo Security to
specifically enable Admin API integration because it isn’t enabled by default. Duo does this
because enabling it can allow customers to make large and irreversible changes to their account
programmatically. Dayforce uses the Admin API integration to enable the two-factor authentication
functionality in System Admin > User.
Web SDK Integration
This integration is required to allow users to log in using the Duo provided UI workflow process for
enrolling users the first time, and for authenticating them on subsequent logins.
Admin API Integration
This integration is required to enable functionality on the User Admin page to reset (delete) users
in the Duo system. This integration is also used on the Admin page where the TFA configuration
keys are entered to verify the keys are correct.

Create the Dayforce Application in Duo Security
After you create a Duo Security account, you must configure Dayforce and API integration within
DUO Security.
Create the Web Application
1. In the Duo Security menu, click Applications.
2. Click Protect an Application, and do the following:
a. Select Web SDK and click Protect this Application.
b. Enter Dayforce Web as Dayforce name.
c. Review the settings of Dayforce. Ensure that Require Enrollment is selected in the
Policy section. Other settings should remain at their default values.
d. Create a document with your word processing application and copy/paste the
integration key, secret key and API hostname into it. You’ll need these keys to set up
Dayforce.
e. Click Save Changes.
Create the Admin API Application
1. In the Duo Security menu, click Applications.
2. Click Protect an Application, and do the following:
a. Locate Admin API, and click Protect this Application.
b. Enter Dayforce Admin as Dayforce name.
c. Enable Grant read resource and Grant write resource.
d. Copy/paste the integration key and secret key into the document you created. The
API hostname will be the same, but the other keys will be unique. You’ll need these
keys to set up Dayforce.
e. Leave all settings at their default values and click Save Changes.
Important: The keys you have stored in the document you created are sensitive. They should be
treated like passwords and stored securely.

Two-factor authorization is enabled at the password policy level so it can be turned on for only
some users. After you generate the necessary Duo Security keys, you can enable two-factor
authentication in Dayforce.
To enable two-factor authentication in Dayforce:
1. Go to System Admin > Password Policy and click the Two Factor Authentication tab.
2. Copy and paste the keys that you generated in Duo into the appropriate fields:

4.
5. Adding these keys integrates Dayforce with the organization's Duo account. This task only

in until the provider becomes accessible again.
10. Note: To control network traffic, Dayforce pings Duo once every five minutes and then
caches that result. This means a five-minute lag could occur before Dayforce knowing that
Duo's availability has changed. If Duo becomes unavailable after a successful ping but
before verifying a user's device, the user will be unable to log in as if the Closed option were
selected.
10. Click Save.

When users log in for the first time using TFA, they have to complete a self-enrollment process,
which is provided by Duo and their Web SDK. Duo enrollment and authentication can be
completed They have both a "traditional" and "universal" enrollment module. You can choose
which one to use with the configuration settings in your Duo account. The main differences
between the "traditional" and "universal" enrollment modules are that the "universal" process is
designed to be more streamlined and involve fewer steps.
The process is embedded in the user interface of Dayforce so that users don’t have to log in to

Reset or Remove Users in Duo Security
In some situations, you will need to reset or remove a user from the Duo system. These situations
can include users who have left your organization and users who have changed devices and
need to enroll again. For most of these cases, you need to log in to the Duo Security
administration portal and perform these actions in the Users area.
Users with TFA enabled in their password policy are automatically deleted from Duo Security in
the following scenarios:
An administrator manually deletes the user in System Admin > User.
The employee is updated as terminated during HR import.
The User Account Employee Status Job sets the user to 'unapproved' (that is, it clears the
Approved checkbox in System Admin > User).
Note: Manually clearing the Approved checkbox in System Admin > User will not delete the
user from DUO Security
Dayforce doesn't automatically delete terminated users from Duo Security if they are assigned to a
termination role, because in this case they are still set to ‘approved’ in System Admin > User.

Add or Edit Your Direct Deposit Accounts
To add or edit your direct deposit accounts:
1. In My Profile, tap Edit and then tap Edit Direct Deposit.
2. Tap the account you want to edit, or tap Add an Account to add a new one.
3. The app displays the Deposit Account screen for editing, or the Add Account screen for you
to enter your new account Information. The app validates the information you enter in the
fields and automatically populates some of the information depending on your country.
3. In the Account Type section, select Dayforce Card, Checking, or Savings.
4. In the Account Information section, enter the account number, branch number, institution
number, and the name of the financial institution.
5. Select any of the following options in the Deposit Type section:
Remainder/Full Amount: Dayforce distributes all of your pay to this account.
Monetary Amount: Dayforce distributes the specified monetary amount to this
account. If you select this option, the app displays the Amount field for you to enter
the dollar amount.
Percentage: Dayforce distributes the specified percentage amount to this account. If
you select this option, the app displays the Amount field for you to enter the
percentage amount.
6. If you need to provide supporting documents, tap Add Document in the
Additional Documents section and then tap Choose File to upload a digital document, Photo
Library to select a photo from your device, or Take Photo to take a new photo using your
device's camera.
7. If required, tap to agree to the terms and conditions.
8. Tap Done. The app displays an Edited tag next to the account you added or edited.
9. Tap Submit to confirm the change. If your change requires approval, you will not be able to
make any other changes to your direct deposit accounts until it is approved.
Delete Your Direct Deposit Accounts
To delete your direct deposit accounts:
1. In My Profile, tap the Edit icon and then tap Edit Direct Deposit.
2. Tap the account you want to delete.
3. Scroll to the bottom of the account information and then tap Delete.
4. Tap Delete to confirm, or tap Cancel to keep the account.

Multifactor Authentication
With Dayforce multifactor authentication (MFA) enabled for your organization, users must verify
their identity by first entering their user name and password and then entering a time-based one-
time code that they receive by text message or voice call. This provides an extra layer of security
for user logins, and it can help protect against credential theft and fraudulent behavior in
Dayforce.
MFA needs to be enabled and configured for your organization by an administrator. After it has
been set up, users are prompted to enter their MFA contact information the next time they log in.
You can find more information on how to set up and use MFA in the following topics:
Configure Multifactor Authentication for Your Organization
First-Time Login with Dayforce Multifactor Authentication

-- 298 of 472 --

Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 299 of 0
Log in to Dayforce Using the Text Message or Voice Call Authentication Method
Update Your Multifactor Authentication Contact Information
Configure Multifactor Authentication for Your Organization
As an administrator, you can enable MFA for the users in your organization to provide an extra
layer of security. MFA is enabled in System Admin > Multifactor Authentication.
Role feature access: System Admin > System Admin > Multifactor Authentication
> MFA Configuration
Note: Dayforce MFA overrides DUO two-factor authentication settings. If you have DUO two-factor
authentication and you enable MFA, DUO security will no longer be applied to users who are
subject to MFA.
MFA configuration options
Option 	Description
When multiple policies
apply to a user, which
setting should be used to
determine the
appropriate policy?
Select one of the options to specify how the appropriate policy
should be determined when multiple policies apply to a user. The
first option ensures that the user is always required to use the most
secure policy available. The second option ensures that the policy
associated with the user's default role is implemented.
Enable daily MFA
registration reminder
notifications
Toggle the switch to enable or disable reminders for users who
have not registered and are subject to MFA. Reminders will be
sent based on the allowed notification channels and the user's
notification preferences.
Maximum number of
reminder notifications
Enter a number in this field to specify the maximum number of
reminder notifications sent to users. Reminders will be sent daily
based on the allowed notification channels in the user's notification
preferences. You can enter a value between 1 and 999 in this
field. The default value is 15.
Enabled
Toggle the switch to enable or disable MFA. After you enable it,
users are prompted to enter their MFA contact information the first
time they log in. MFA is only enabled for users who log in using
native authentication. If your organization has single sign-on users,
this setting doesn't change their log in process because MFA can't
be used together with single sign-on.

multiple policies apply. This option is enabled by default.

Dayforcewhen MFA
provider is unavailable
Select the checkbox to allow users to log in to Dayforce using

provider isn’t available. This option is enabled by default.
Allow VOIP phone
numbers
Select the checkbox and users will be able to use a voice over

Authenticator App: Users can set up MFA using an

Email: Users can set up MFA using a valid email address of
their choice.

Enter a number in this field to allow users to log in without going
through identity verification for the specified number of days after
the last successful identity verification. For example, if you enter
2, users aren't prompted for 2 days after they successfully verify
their identification.
The maximum number of days you can enter is 30. If you enter 0,
this option isn’t enabled, and users have to verify their identity
every time they log in to Dayforce. The default value is 14 days.

Exclude Users from Multifactor Authentication
You can temporarily exclude individual users from multifactor authentication (MFA). This
functionality can be used in situations where a user can't use MFA for some reason. For example,
you might use this feature if an employee is traveling overseas without access to their usual MFA
phone, or if a user's MFA account isn’t working but they have a business need to log in to
Dayforce right away.
Role feature access: System Admin > User > Maintain Multifactor Authentication Exclusions
You exclude users from MFA in System Admin > User, in the Multifactor Authentication tab:
To temporarily exclude a user from MFA:
1. Go to System Admin > User and select the user that you want to exclude from MFA.
2. In the Multifactor Authentication tab, select a date in the Exclude from MFA Through field.
3. Click Save.
After you complete the steps above, the user can log in to Dayforce using only their user name
and password until the specified date. After that date, they will again be required to use MFA.
MFA Exemption by IP Address

-- 302 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 303 of 0
This section describes how to exempt users by IP address from being required to authenticate
using multifactor authentication (MFA). This functionality gives you the ability to define a range of
trusted IP addresses that aren't required to authenticate using MFA when logging in to Dayforce.
Before You Begin: You must be a system admin user to exempt users by IP address from being
required to authenticate using Multifactor authentication (MFA) when they log in to Dayforce. Your
system admin role must also have access to the System Admin > Multifactor Authentication role
feature in the Features tab in System Admin > Roles.
When a user logs in to Dayforce using their login credentials and their user account is configured
to use to MFA, Dayforce checks their IP address against the list of enabled rules. If the IP address
is listed, the user is logged in to Dayforce without requiring them to pass a second factor
authenticator. If the IP address isn’t listed in the enabled rules, Dayforce prompts the user to
authenticate using MFA after correctly entering their login credentials.
To define the range of IP addresses that aren't required to authenticate using MFA:
Important: The range of IP addresses must be entered in ascending order. An error message is
shown in Dayforce if you enter a range of IP addresses in descending order.
1. Go to System Admin > Multifactor Authentication.
2. Click Add in the IP Address Exceptions section of the MFA Configuration tab.
3. Enter a description for the rule you are creating in the Description column.
4. Enter the lower IP address in the range in the Lower IP Address Range column.
5. Enter the higher IP address in the range in the Upper IP Address Range column.
6. Note: To allow a specific address, rather than a range of addresses, enter the same IP
address in both the Lower IP Address Range and Upper IP Address Range columns.
6. Select the Rule Enabled checkbox to enable the rule. Optionally, you can clear the Rule
Enabled checkbox to disable the rule.
7. Note: To enable or disable multiple rules at the same time, select or clear the checkbox
beside a rule and then select an option in the Enable/Disable drop-down list.
7. Click Save.
Delete MFA Exemption Rules
Users that log in to Dayforce using an IP address that is exempt from authenticating using MFA
can log in to Dayforce with just their login credentials. When you delete an MFA exemption rule in
Dayforce, the impacted user or users are required to successfully authenticate themselves using
two-factor authentication when they log in to Dayforce. This includes their login credentials and a
second factor authenticator such as, a SMS text message or a voice call containing a 6-digit code
that must be entered into Dayforce when logging in to Dayforce.
Before You Begin: You must be a system admin user to delete Multifactor Authentication (MFA)
exemption rules in Dayforce. Your system admin role must also have access to the System Admin

-- 303 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 304 of 0
> Multifactor Authentication role feature in the Features tab in System Admin > Roles.
Deleted rules can't be restored. You must recreate the rule in Dayforce if you need to use the rule
again. For your convenience, you can disable a rule, rather than delete it. For more information
about enabling and disabling rules, see MFA Exemption by IP Address.
To delete MFA exemption rules:
1. Go to System Admin > Multifactor Authentication.
2. Select the rules you want to delete from the list of rules in the IP Address Exceptions section
of the MFA Configuration tab.
3. Click Delete.
4. Click Save.
First-Time Login with Dayforce Multifactor Authentication
Multifactor authentication (MFA) adds an extra layer of security by requesting a code along with
your user name and password. This code changes every time you log in and is only valid for a
short time after it's generated. After your organization enables Dayforce MFA for your user role,
you need to set up MFA the next time you log in.
Before You Begin: An administrator must enable MFA for your organization. See Configure
Multifactor Authentication for Your Organization.
To log in with Dayforce Multifactor Authentication for the first time:
1. Go to your organization's Dayforce login screen and enter your login information.
2. In the Multifactor Authentication Setup screen, select an authentication method to use when
logging in:
SMS Text Message or Voice Call: Set up MFA using your mobile device. A 6-digit
code will be sent to your mobile device through either a text message or a voice call.
This code is used to verify your identity when you log in to Dayforce.
Authenticator App Code: Set up MFA using an authentication app of your choice. A
time-based one-time password will be generated by your authentication app that you
use to log in to Dayforce.
Email: Set up MFA using an email address of your choice. A time-based one-time
password will be sent to your email that you use to log in to Dayforce.
Note: If you choose to receive the verification code by text message, you’ll receive the
text message in the language according to your culture setting in Dayforce. If the
language in your culture settings isn’t supported, Dayforce sends the SMS message
in English (US).
3. Click Next.
To continue the log-in process, see the following steps and procedures defined for the
authentication method that you selected:

-- 304 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 305 of 0
If you selected SMS Text Message or Voice Call, see Set Up Multifactor Authentication Using
the SMS Text Message or Voice Call Option.
If you selected Authenticator App Code, see Set Up Multifactor Authentication Using the
Authenticator App Option.
If you selected Email, see Set Up Multifactor Authentication Using the Email Option.
Set Up Multifactor Authentication Using the SMS Text Message or Voice Call Option
After selecting SMS Text Message or Voice Call in the Multifactor Authentication Setup dialog box,
you're prompted to set up your contact information to receive verification codes by text message
or voice call.
Note: SMS text messages are sent in the language specified by your culture settings in Dayforce.
If the language specified in your culture settings isn’t supported, Dayforce sends the SMS
message in English (US).
To log in to Dayforce and set up your account for MFA using SMS text message or voice call
authentication:
1. In the Contact Information dialog box, select your country and enter the primary phone
number where you want to receive the code each time you log in.
2. (Optional) Select the Add Secondary Number checkbox to include a back-up phone
number.
3. Click Continue.
4. Select Text Message or Voice Call to indicate how you want to receive the code to verify
your primary number.
5. Enter the verification code that you received and click Next. If you didn't receive a code,
click Resend Verification Code via SMS or Receive Verification Code via Voice Call to try
again.
6. Note: If you selected the Add Secondary Number checkbox when setting up your contact
information, you will be prompted to enter and verify the secondary number.
6. Click Continue to log in to Dayforce
Set Up Multifactor Authentication Using the Authenticator App Option
After selecting Authenticator App Code in the Set up Multifactor Authentication screen, you are
prompted to set up the authenticator. This option lets you receive time-based one-time verification
codes through the authenticator app instead of text messages or voice calls.
To log in to Dayforce and set up your account for MFA using an authenticator application:
1. Download an authenticator application of your choice.
2. Log in to Dayforce.

-- 305 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 306 of 0
3. In the Set up Multifactor Authentication screen, select Authenticator App Code and
click Continue.

Method 1: Secret Key and Account: Manually enter the secret key and account name
shown on the screen into your authenticator app.
Method 2: QR Code: Use your authenticator app to scan the QR code shown on the

5. Click Continue.

Set Up Multifactor Authentication Using the Email Option
After selecting Email in the Set up Multifactor Authentication screen, you are prompted to set up

email address of your choice.
To log in to Dayforce and set up your account for MFA using email:
1. Log in to Dayforce.
2. In the Set up Multifactor Authentication screen, select Email and click Continue.
3. In the Contact Information screen, enter your email address. Click Continue.
4. Open your email and find the time-based one-time verification code from Dayforce.
5. In the Enter Verification Code screen, enter the verification code. Click Continue.
6. In the confirmation screen, click Continue to log in to Dayforce.

2. Go to Profile and click Settings > Security.

4. In the dialog box that opens, follow the prompts to update your MFA contact information.
IP Network Restrictions
Before You Begin: Your user role must be assigned access to the System Admin > IP Network
Restrictions feature in the Features tab of System Admin > Roles.
System Admin > IP Network Restrictions has two main sections: the first is a list of IP Network
Restrictions, and the second is a list of IP address ranges for the selected restriction. Further,
there are two main entries in the IP Network Restrictions list: the first contains your organization’s
namespace (in the following examples, Test Org), and System:
<your instance namespace>: Named after your organization. Lists any IP Restrictions that
you or another authorized user have created.
<user-created IP Restriction>: A specific IP Restriction that you create,
name, and configure for one or more user available from those set up in System
Admin > Roles.
System: Lists the default, system-level restriction types. You can configure a specific
IP address or a range of address by adding rules in the bottom panel, but you can’t create
new system level restriction types. The system-level restriction types can’t be set for specific
roles.
Clock Entry: Restricts clock entries for physical clocks and soft clocks only. These
restrictions don’t apply to clock entries from the Dayforce Mobile app.
Dayforce Service: Restrictions applied to external applications interacting with
Dayforce through web services.

apply for the user-defined restriction types, with examples of a range that is allowed and a range
that is denied:

Restrict Clock Entries by IP Address

-- 312 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 313 of 0
You can restrict clock entries by IP address, which allows you to ensure that employees can’t
perform clock entries from outside of a physical work location. This functionality doesn’t restrict
access to Dayforce from these locations. It only restricts whether the user can clock in or out for
work.
Role feature access: System Admin > IP Network Restrictions
When an employee clocks in or out, Dayforce checks their IP address against the list of allowed
addresses. If the IP address is allowed, Dayforce accepts the clock entry. If the IP address
doesn’t fall within one of the allowable ranges, Dayforce denies the IP address and rejects the
clock entry.
Even though clocks outside of the specified allowable ranges are rejected, you can also specify
IP addresses to deny in cases where an IP address or a range of IP addresses is problematic (for
example, an attacker).
To set which IP addresses are allowed or denied:
1. Go to System Admin > IP Network Restrictions.
2. In the list in the top half of the screen, select the Clock Entry option. Dayforce shows any
existing rules for clock entries in the bottom half of the screen.
3. Note: The Clock Entry option is a system option that is automatically available in System
Admin > IP Network Restrictions.
3. In the bottom half of the screen, click Add.
4. Enter the lowest IP address in the range in the Lower IP Address Range field.
5. Enter the highest IP address in the range in the Upper IP Address Range field.
6. Note: To allow or deny a specific address, rather than a range of addresses, enter the same
number in both the Lower IP Address Range and Upper IP Address Range fields.
6. Select Allow or Deny in the Access drop-down list, depending on whether you want the
specified address or range of addresses to be allowed or denied.
7. Verify that the Rule Enabled checkbox is selected.
8. Click Save.
Note: You must also select the Network Location Validation checkbox in the applicable time entry
policies. For more information about configuring time entry policies, see Time Entry Policies. As
well, you must ensure that Network Location Validation is enabled in System Admin > Clocking
Sequence Validation. For more information about clock entry validations, see Configure Clock
Entry Validations.
Restrict Dayforce Web Services by IP Address
To provide an additional layer of secure access to data, you can restrict the IP address (that is, the
network location) from which Dayforce Web Services can be accessed.

-- 313 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 314 of 0
Role feature access: System Admin > IP Network Restrictions
Dayforce Web Services are a set of application interface features that provide organizations with
near real-time communication between the Dayforce application and their internal systems. Some
programming (software development) effort is required on behalf of organizations that want to use
these features. See the Dayforce Web Services Introduction Guide.
The ability to define IP Network Restrictions is an optional feature that your organization can use to
provide an additional layer of secured access to data and limit malicious parties from overloading
application resources. With this feature, you can restrict access to your organization's Dayforce
Web Services so that only applications originating from your organization's specific hosting
environment can use access and use them.
The Dayforce Service option is a system option that is automatically available in System Admin
> IP Network Restrictions.
To define which IP addresses are allowed or denied:
1. Go to System Admin > IP Network Restrictions.
2. Click the Dayforce Service option.
3. In the section below the list of IP restriction types list, click Add, and then do the following:
Select the Rule Enabled checkbox.
Specify the IP addresses included in the rule by doing one of the following:
a. To allow or deny a specific address, enter the same number in both the Lower
IP Address Range and Upper IP Address Range fields.
b. To allow or deny a range of addresses, enter the lowest IP address in the Lower
IP Address Range field and enter the highest IP address in the Upper
IP Address Range field.
In the Access drop-down list, select Allow or Deny, depending on whether you want
to allow or deny access for the specified address or range of addresses.
(Optional) Enter a value in the Description and Service Provider fields.
4. Click Save.
5. Click Refresh.
Overview of Account Recovery Assistant
You can configure Dayforce so that when users are missing a verified email address or security
questions, the Account Recovery Assistant can be shown after logging in to allow them to update
this information without visiting their profile. Having a verified email address and security questions
recorded allows users to reset a forgotten password without contacting a Dayforce representative
or their administrator.

-- 314 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 315 of 0
Dayforce log in process. This functionality isn’t applicable for the Dayforce mobile apps.
Note: Users can update their email contact information directly through this functionality.
Therefore, it should be enabled only if employees are permitted to maintain their own contact
information in Dayforce.
When you enable this functionality, employees who are missing a verified email address or
security questions are prompted with the Account Recovery Assistant dialog box as the first
message after they log in:
If the employee already has some of this information, the dialog box only asks for the missing
information. For example, if the employee has already set up security questions but has no email
address, the dialog box only includes the section for updating their email address.
If the employee has an email address on file, but it isn’t verified, they can select it from the list to
verify it. They can also select Other and enter a new email address to verify:

-- 315 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 316 of 0
They can add the required information and click Submit, or click Skip to close the dialog box and
continue using Dayforce. Dayforce continues to show this dialog box after each log in until this
information is recorded.
The Account Recovery Assistant can also be configured to show the Close button instead of the
Skip button, so that employees must complete their password reset information before they can
access Dayforce. In this case, when an employee clicks Close, the application shows a message
indicating that they must provide the required information to access Dayforce.
If they click Return, the application shows the Account Recovery Assistant, where they can
provide the required information and click Submit to access Dayforce. If they click Logout, they
are returned to the main log in screen.
When users submit a new email address, Dayforce adds it to their profile as a personal email
address. Dayforce sends a standard verification link to the address that was either selected (for
pre-existing unverified addresses) or added. See Email Verification.
They can click Resend to send another verification link or OK to close the dialog box and continue
using Dayforce. Clicking the Need to use a different email address? link allows users to either add
a new address or choose from a pre-existing address to send the verification link to.
If the user doesn't take action on the verification link, or the link expires, Dayforce shows the
Account Recovery Assistant the next time they log in. Any pre-existing email address (including
the address that they previously added) is shown and they can resend the verification link.
Note: When the Account Recovery Assistant dialog box is configured, Dayforce doesn't display
the default log in messages that appear when an employee doesn't have a verified email. See
Email Verification.

Email verification methods
Method Description
Method A
When users click Verify for the email address in the Contact Information dialog
box, which Dayforce is shown when you update contact information in the

-- 318 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 319 of 0
The Send Verification button is only shown when you save an email address with the
Alerts checkbox selected.
Method
C
When Dayforce automatically sends out an email verification request. It sends out
requests for any email address that is still not verified after an initial verification
request was sent out.
If the user doesn't respond to the initial request by a given time, the messages
begin to be sent by this method. Verification requests are usually sent daily.
Dayforce stops sending a message when one of the following occurs:
1. The user verifies their email address successfully.
2. The email address is marked as rejected. See Rejected Email Addresses.
3. The number of times that the email can automatically be sent reaches a
maximum. See Messages.
Note: When a user's email address is already assigned to another account, you can't send
verification emails, and the user can't use that address to reset their password or log in to
Dayforce. However, they can receive other alerts at that address.

Rejected Email Addresses
A rejected email means that the user might have added an incorrect email, and then the
unintended recipient clicked the This is not my email address link in the verification message
(described in the previous section). When an email is rejected, it no longer receives automatic
verification messages (that is, those sent from method C, described previously).
Moreover, the following occurs:
The rejected icon is displayed for the email address in the following areas:
The Contact Information dialog box, which is opened by updating contact information
in the Personal > About Me screen in Profile.
The Email Addresses section of the Personal > Contact Information screen in People.
When users log in, a message prompt informs them that their email was rejected. See
Verification Message Sent Out.
When users edit the email address and save changes, the rejected status is removed from the
email address.

Organization Hierarchy
Organization (or org) hierarchy reflects your organization’s structure. Org hierarchy in Dayforce is
used to allocate taxes, to control access, to filter for scheduling and reporting, for general ledger
allocation, and in the mapping of jobs.

-- 327 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 328 of 0
Designing and configuring the organization hierarchy in Dayforce is important for several reasons.
Dayforce uses the structure that you set when it determines security access, filtering the various
feature areas in Dayforce that you and people in your organization use. These feature areas can
include People, Schedules, Timesheets, and so forth. Correctly configuring your organization is
important so that the information that’s available, or unavailable, to each user in Dayforce is
appropriate.
At the bottom of the hierarchy are departments. Departments roll up to, or belong to, zones.
Zones roll up to sites, also known as locations. Sites (locations) can be organized into one or more
groups or subgroups, such as districts or regions, in the organizational hierarchy. And, finally,
districts and regions roll up to the top (or corporate) level of the org hierarchy.
The following list describes the various org levels available in Dayforce:
Corporate: This is the top level of an organization. This org level contains all of the other
hierarchy levels in the organization, and it’s the first level that you create.
Region: (Optional) A region represents a group of districts. For example, a region is often
used in organizations that operate in more than one country or more than one continent.
This org level contains districts, sites, departments, zones, and on-site departments.
District: (Optional) A district represents a group of sites. For example, if an organization
operates on more than one continent, it might divide the organization into districts by
country grouped under a region, such as France, Germany, or Belgium in Europe, and the
United States and Canada in North America.
Site: A site represents a location where people are employed. A site can be a physical
building, a collection of buildings, a town, a city, or province, or it can be virtual.
Department: A department represents the area that needs a job to be done. A department
can represent a function (Finance, Sales), an area of responsibility (Production Line), or
even a virtual area (Union Duties).
Zone: A zone represents a grouping of on-site departments for the purposes of scheduling.
On-Site Department: An on-site department is made up of a site and a department that are
configured in Dayforce. For example, New York (site) + Packaging (department) = New
York Packaging (on-site department).
When you're finished configuring your organization, Dayforce contains a hierarchy that mirrors that
of your organization.
The way that you configure your org structure in Dayforce affects how employee work
assignments are set up, affecting jobs and job assignments. In Dayforce, a job assignment is
made up of a job and a department. A job is a set of activities that need to be done, and a
department can be an area that needs a job to be done. The department can be an area of
responsibility (Front Desk or Production Line), a functional area (Finance or Sales), or a virtual area
(Union Duties). See Jobs and Job Assignments Configuration.

-- 328 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 329 of 0
The following screenshot shows an example of how an organization's hierarchy has been defined
in Dayforce:
The top level of the hierarchy in the screenshot is labeled Corporate and includes two regions:
Manufacturing Co. Canada and Manufacturing Co. Mexico. Each region contains sites, and each
site contains departments. You can click the arrow next to an org unit to expand the view the next
level of the hierarchy. To view all levels beneath a specific org unit, select the unit and click
Expand in the toolstrip.
Note: This is just an example. The organization hierarchy can represent any organization,
including those in other verticals or industries such as retail or the service industry. Locations and
organizational units are defined in the same way for any vertical or industry.
The way that you configure your organization's hierarchy levels determines the behavior of
multiple features and elements in Dayforce. For example:
Management can be driven by location (org level) in the org hierarchy. Employees can be
filtered and scheduled by location.
Legal entities are tied to the site and are required for processing in the Payroll feature.
Timesheets are approved by site.
General Ledger information and details can be determined by the configuration of the
employee, department, org unit, job, and job assignment, as well as earning and deduction
codes in the system.
Schedules are loaded by site. Zones can be used to filter within a schedule.
Security and access are determined by org hierarchy. Users have visibility to different
locations in the org structure, and user roles control access to data.
Configuring the structure, or hierarchy, of your organization can involve several tasks, each of
which is described in the following topics:

-- 329 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 330 of 0
Configure Organizational Groups and Subgroups
Configure Departments
Create Zones
Create Zone Packages

in People. Because employees need to be taxed based on the location where they

Location Addresses
Mobile Org Addresses
Legal Entity
Organization setup in Dayforce is done in Org Setup in the appropriate subfeature. For example,
general organization setup is done in Org Setup > Organization. Legal entity setup for an
organization is done in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup.

Payroll Setup > Location Addresses.
Employee jobs are associated with on-site department locations for workforce management tasks,
such as timesheet approval, scheduling, and budgeting purposes. However, some employees
might work remotely or in locations that aren’t listed as physical locations in your organization’s
hierarchy.
Because employee taxation is based on the actual physical location where employees perform
their work, you might need to enter an employee work location override for an employee who
physically works in a different location than the site or on-site department work location assigned
to them in Dayforce.

-- 330 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 331 of 0
Note: You can apply the work location override only for employees who are part of pay groups of
native payroll countries.
The Employee Work Location Overrides screen shows a list of any employee work location
overrides that you have set up. Each entry has four columns:
Location Name: Name for the employee work location override.
Description: Optional description of the employee work location override.
Allow Legal Entity Override: Checkbox that you can select to allow the employee work
location override to override a legal entity.
Reference Code: Field for an XRefCode for imports and exports.
There can also be two tabs for each entry:
Address: This tab contains address information for the employee work location override.
Legal Entity: This tab is shown if the Allow Legal Entity Override checkbox is selected. You
can use this tab to configure a legal entity override for the work location override.
By setting up an employee work location override, you can specify the physical location where the
employee works, which helps to ensure that the employee’s taxes are properly calculated based
on that physical location.
For example, if an employee works out of a rented office space that isn’t one of the organization's
offices, then the address of the rented office space needs to be configured as a work location
override and assigned to the employee.
Say an employee works remotely from a location in Big Horn, Wyoming, but your organization
doesn’t have a site or on-site department configured in Big Horn, Wyoming. You must configure
an employee work location override for that employee so that the employee’s manager can assign
that work location override to the employee. That way, the employee is taxed for working in Big
Horn, Wyoming, as shown in the following screenshot:
Create Employee Work Location Overrides

Before You Begin: Make sure you're familiar with the concepts related to employee work location
overrides in Employee Work Location Overrides.
To create an employee work location override:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Employee Work Location Overrides.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter the employee work location override details:
a. In the Location Name field, enter a name for the work location override.
b. (Optional) Enter a description for the work location override.
c. In the Allow Legal Entity Override column, select the checkbox to enable the override.
d. In the Reference Code field, enter an XRefCode for the work location override.
4. In the Address tab, enter the address details for the employee work location override.
5. Click Save.
You’re now ready to apply this work location override in the employee profile in People, in the
Work > Work Assignments screen.
Note: You can apply the work location override only for employees who belong to pay groups of
native payroll countries.
Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity
A legal entity is an organization that federal tax authorities recognize. A single organization might
have one legal entity or several. Because each legal entity belongs to one country, organizations
paying employees in more than one country need a separate legal entity for each country they
operate in. For example, if your organization has employees in both Canada and the United
States, it must have at least two legal entities configured: one for US employees and one for
Canadian employees.
Before You Begin: You should be familiar with how to set up organizations in Dayforce. General
information about organization structure is available in Organization Hierarchy.
In Dayforce, every organizational unit configured with Site selected in the Org Level drop-down list
in Org Setup > Organization must be assigned to a legal entity, and every organizational unit
configured with On-site department selected in the Org Level drop-down list in Org Setup >
Organization can have a legal entity explicitly assigned or can inherit the assignment from its
parent site.
Configuring legal entities involves the following general tasks:
Creating legal entity entries
Entering customer funding identifiers and bank information for legal entities
(Canada only) Entering employment insurance factors and funding identifiers

The legal address of the legal entity on tax forms. The address

Contains workers' compensation classification codes. In
Canada, the provincial workers' compensation boards issue

either by state workers' compensation boards or private
insurance companies.
