If you're using WFM only, without the Payroll module, tax authority information is set up so
that taxes can be correctly calculated and included in pay run exports to be handled by the
customer's payroll solution.
If you're using the Payroll module in Dayforce for payroll calculation and disbursements,
legal entity tax authority information is set up as described in these topics. Information about
the payroll taxes configured for their organization in Payroll Setup > Payroll Taxes is
available in Payroll Setup > Payroll Taxes. If you need to add taxes to legal entities, you can
find specific information about the taxes in Payroll Setup > Payroll Taxes and use that
information to add the taxes to the legal entity in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal
Entity.
Tax Authorities
Dayforce calculates and applies employer and employee taxes based on the tax authorities
assigned to a legal entity. The tax authorities configured for legal entities determine the specific
taxes paid by both the legal entity and by its employees, whose taxes can also depend on where
they work and where they live.
Tax authorities are configured for each legal entity in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity.
Legal entities' associated taxes are listed in the Tax Authorities tab.
Tax authorities are assigned to a legal entity based on the addresses of the legal entity sites where
employees work. Also, tax authorities are assigned to a legal entity depending on the primary
residence addresses of its employees. Employee address information is configured in People.
For example, if a US legal entity has locations in Massachusetts, California, and New York,
Dayforce determines and lists the applicable federal taxes, as well as the state taxes from
Massachusetts, California, and New York as separate tax authorities. State and local taxes are
then applied to individual employees based on their home states, work states, and, in some
cases, their specific addresses.
Dayforce determines the possible taxes that are applicable to a legal entity after the following
tasks have been performed:
The legal entity is linked to organizational units.
Sites assigned to the legal entity have their address recorded in the Address tab.
Employees are assigned to work at the sites in the Work > Work Assignments screen of
People.
After these steps have been performed, the application runs its tax locator functionality and
returns the taxes that a legal entity and its employees should potentially be paying. These taxes
are client-responsible, meaning that customers are responsible for filing them. Dayforce marks
payroll taxes that are client-responsible with a checkmark in the Client Responsible tax field.
These taxes aren't filed by Dayforce on behalf of customers and therefore are the customer's

-- 340 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 341 of 0
responsibility to file. You can report on these taxes using the Client Responsible Taxes Report
available in Payroll.
View, Add, or Refresh Tax Authorities
To view or add tax authorities associated with a legal entity:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity.
2. Select the legal entity and then click the Tax Authorities tab.
3. Select the tax authority from the list.
4. Click Add in the Tax Setting section to the right of the list of tax authorities.
5. Enter a date in the Effective Start field to indicate when the tax starts using the supplemental
tax method.
6. (Optional) Enter a date in the Effective End field to indicate when the supplemental tax
method expires.
7. Select an option in the Supplemental Tax Method drop-down list, if applicable. For the
Supplemental Flat Rate tax method, select an option in the Supplemental Alternate
Calculation Method drop-down list.
8. Click Save.
As changes are made to the organizational hierarchy, such as sites being opened in new states or
provinces, employees changing locations or residential addresses, there might be new taxes
applicable to legal entities.
Refresh Employee Taxes
To check for new tax authorities based on the current organizational hierarchy, employee work
assignments, and addresses, run the Dayforce tax locator functionality by doing the following:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization.
2. Click the Organization tab.
3. Click Refresh Employee Taxes.
Columns in the Tax Authorities Tab by Country

Manually Add Taxes
Before You Begin: Manually adding taxes is only available for US employees and legal entities.

-- 343 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 344 of 0
Important: If you’re an Implementation Consultant planning on making manual changes to either
state or federal tax rates or to state insurance rates—outside of the regular quarterly update done
by DTS—you must make sure of two things:
Ensure that you receive appropriate management approval for the change.
Ensure that the effective date of any change is set to the first of the quarter.
You can manually add taxes at the legal entity level for all or a filtered list of the entity’s
employees, or you can add taxes to individual employees. This allows you to correct omissions of
the application’s tax locator functionality.
For example, if Dayforce doesn’t fully recognize an address and can’t locate the appropriate local
or county taxes, you can manually add the appropriate tax.
Add New Taxes to Employees
Important: Manually added taxes must be tied to an address so that Dayforce knows if the tax still
applies. If the employee’s address changes, or the end date for a selected address has passed,
Dayforce automatically stops applying the tax to the employee’s pay.
To manually add a new tax to a US employee:
1. Go to People, open the employee profile, and click Payroll > Tax Definitions.
2. In the Employee Payroll Tax section, click Add New Taxes.
3. The application shows the Add New Taxes dialog box.
3. In the Tax Type drop-down list, select the type of tax you want to add.
4. Enter values in the other filter fields. You can filter by the tax authority's title, or filter by the
tax's description.
5. Click Apply Filter.
6. Dayforce shows a list of taxes that match your search terms.
6. Select the appropriate tax.
7. Select the employee's applicable from the Employee Address field.
8. Click Add Selected Tax.
9. The application adds the tax to the list shown in the Employee Payroll Tax section with the
Manually Added Tax checkbox selected.
Add New Taxes at the Legal Entity Level
You can manually add new taxes to a legal entity so that it applies to some or all of the legal
entity's employees.
To manually add new taxes at the legal entity level:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity and select the US legal entity.
2. Select the Tax Authorities tab.

-- 344 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 345 of 0
3. Click Add New Taxes.
4. Select the type of the tax that you want to add in the Tax Type drop-down list.
5. Search for the tax you want to add by providing values in the other filter options; you can
filter by the tax authority's title, or filter by the tax's description.
6. Click Apply Filter.
7. Select the appropriate tax.
8. Click Add Selected Tax to add the tax to the legal entity. Next, you need to define which
employees in the legal entity are taxed for the manually added tax.
9. Select the manually added tax.
10. In the Tax Qualifier section, click Add.
11. Specify an effective start of the new tax in the Effective Start field.
12. Do the following to specify which employees in the legal entity are taxed:
Leave the Locations field and the Work Location Overrides field blank and the tax is
applied to all of the legal entity's employees.
Specify values in the Locations field and the Work Location Overrides field to filter the
list of employees the tax is applied to.
13. For example, to configure Dayforce to apply only the new manually added tax to employees
working at three of the five locations in the legal entity, select those three locations in the
Locations field.
13. Click Save.
Configure Tax Exempt Status for US Legal Entities
Important: If you configure a legal entity as exempt from either the Federal Social Security or
Medicare Tax, you must mark the legal entity as tax exempt for both the employee and
corresponding employer tax. The application displays an error message if just one in the pair of
employee and employer tax for either the Federal Social Security or Medicare Tax is marked as
exempt.
To configure tax exempt status for a US legal entity:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity and select a legal entity.
2. Click the Tax Authorities tab and select the tax authority in the list.
3. Click Add in the Tax Setting section, to the right of the list of tax authorities.
4. Enter a date in the Effective Start field to indicate when the legal entity and its employees'
tax exempt status begins.
5. (Optional) Enter a date in the Effective End field to indicate when the tax exempt status
expires.
6. Select the Exempt Tax Only, Update Wages checkbox to exempt the tax, but calculate
taxable wages. For some taxes, you can select the Exempt Tax And Taxable Wages
checkbox to apply the exemption and disregard the taxable wages.
7. Note: You can select either the Exempt Tax Only, Update Wages checkbox, or the Exempt
Tax and Taxable Wages checkbox, but not both.

-- 345 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 346 of 0
7. Click Save.
Tax Settings and Tax Qualifiers for Tax Authorities
Some employer and employee taxes have additional settings that can (or must) be configured so
that the taxes are calculated correctly. These settings are configured in the Tax Setting section for
a selected tax in the Tax Authorities tab in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity.
In addition to the Tax Setting section, some tax authorities also have a Tax Qualifier section.
Tax authority settings are available for taxes in Canada, the United Kingdom, and the United
States. However, not all tax authorities have tax settings or tax qualifiers available. These sections
are available for those taxes where the federal, state, provincial, territorial, county, local, or other
tax authorities have legislated additional tax settings or configurations for the calculation or
collection of taxes.
Tax Setting Columns
Tax Setting columns
Column 	Description
Start Date 	Start date for the tax setting. Required.
End Date 	End date for the tax setting. Optional.
Exempt Tax Only, Update

Tax Qualifiers
Similar to how some tax authorities have tax settings, some tax settings have associated tax
qualifiers. Tax qualifiers are used in relation to tax settings to configure qualifiers for the tax setting
for a given tax authority. They’re often associated with manually added municipal, local, or other
taxes, for example, Joint Economic Development Districts, or JEDDs. The qualifiers section
generally contains the following:
Effective Start and Effective End dates:
Locations: Locations specific to the legal entity associated with the tax authority.
Work Location Overrides: Overrides to the location setting with which you can specify the
physical location where the employee works, ensuring that the employee’s taxes are
properly calculated based on that physical location.
Projects: Projects specific to the legal entity associated with the tax authority.
The Dayforce Tax Service engine automatically locates tax authorities based on published
regulatory records of physical geographic boundaries. Where a tax authority does NOT have a
physical boundary that can be located, you can use the Tax Qualifiers section as an override to
specify a work location that should locate this tax on an employee assigned to that location.
Tax Rates
Similar to how some tax authorities have tax settings, some, but not all, tax settings have
associated tax rates. Tax rates are used for some tax authorities like Workers’ Compensation to
configure specific tax rates for those tax withholdings. For example, for some workers’
compensation withholdings have different rates for both employer and employee.
The following two tables contain details about the workers’ compensation tax authorities for
employer and employee for specific states that must be specially configured:

Configure Supplemental Tax Methods
To configure supplemental tax methods at the legal entity level:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity and select a legal entity.
2. Click the Tax Authorities tab and select the tax authority.
3. Click Add in the Tax Setting section, to the right of the list of tax authorities.
4. Enter a date in the Effective Start field to indicate when the tax starts using the supplemental
tax method.
5. (Optional) Enter a date in the Effective End field to indicate when the supplemental tax
method expires.
6. Select an option in the Supplemental Tax Method drop-down list, if applicable. For the
Supplemental Flat Rate tax method, select an option in the Supplemental Alternate
Calculation Method drop-down list.
7. Click Save.

PSD Codes for Pennsylvania
Dayforce automatically determines the correct Political Subdivision Code (PSD) for both work
location addresses and employee primary residential addresses. PSD codes are six -digit
numbers that designate each of the 69 tax collection districts in the state of Pennsylvania, which
are used to ensure that taxes are remitted to the proper taxing authority.
The application displays the read-only PSD Code field in the Personal > Contact Information
screen of People for employees whose primary residence address is in Pennsylvania. It
automatically updates the code if the primary residence changes to an address in a different tax
collection district.
PSD Codes are also displayed in the Address tab of Org Setup > Organization for physical
locations defined in Org Setup once an employee has been assigned to work at the physical

-- 352 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 353 of 0
location.
This information is provided to Dayforce Tax Service to help ensure that taxes are remitted to the
appropriate taxing authority.
BC Employer Health Tax (BC EHT)
The British Columbia Employer Health Tax (BC EHT) is payable by employers on the earnings of
their BC employees when total BC employee earnings exceed the yearly exemption limit.
The remittance requirements for BC EHT specify that employers must pay this tax in equal
quarterly installments that are based on an estimate of the total earnings for BC employees for the
year. If the amount of tax paid based on the estimate is lower than the actual amount owing, the
outstanding amount is subject to interest.
These remittance requirements are different from those of other Canadian provincial health taxes
for which installment amounts vary and are based on the actual tax calculated during the
installment.
Important: Because the installments of BC EHT are based on estimated earnings and require
equal installments, Dayforce does not support the calculation or remittance of this tax and only
supports the tracking of taxable wages. This means that you need to calculate and remit this tax
to the BC government outside of Dayforce.
While the application does not calculate or remit this tax, you still need to update the tax details in
Dayforce to track taxable wages. Dayforce provides the tax value BC EHT in the Tax Authorities
tab for Canadian legal entities in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity. The tax authority
number for BC EHT is 1011000020.
In the Company Tax ID Number column for this tax, you need to record the BC tax account
number for the legal entity. If the legal entity doesn't have a BC tax account number, you can enter
EHT-9999-9999 as a placeholder.
In the Tax Setting section for this tax, you need to create a record with effective start and end
dates covering the year. As is the case with other health taxes, you need to create a tax setting
record each year.
If you select the Exempt Tax and Taxable Wages checkbox in the record, the application does not
track taxable wages. It is a best practice to leave this checkbox cleared so that you can monitor
whether the legal entity is nearing or over the exemption limit for the tax, and to ensure the
estimated installment amounts do not fall below the actual tax owing.
Because the application does not calculate this tax, the Exemption Allocation, Exemption Amount
and Gross Annual Payroll parameters of the record are non-editable.
Information about Calculating Tax Installments

-- 353 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 354 of 0
You can calculate the tax installments using the health tax calculator on the BC government
website: https://forms.gov.bc.ca/taxes/employer-health-tax-calculator/.
In this calculator, you need to enter an estimate of total BC earnings based on the lesser of
the following:
the previous year's tax
estimated tax for the current year
You can obtain the BC earnings recorded in Dayforce for the previous year by running the
Payroll Summary Report. Group the report by work province and run it for the relevant legal
entities. In the report, the Gross to Net section for BC displays the total earnings.
You need to monitor the taxable wages of the BC EHT tax in Dayforce for the current year to
ensure that the estimated earnings that are used to calculate the installment do not fall
below the actual earnings. This will allow you to avoid interest fees for extra amounts owing.
You can monitor this by running the Payroll Summary Report. Group the report by work
province and run it for the relevant legal entities. In the report, the Tax Expense Summary
section for BC displays the limited taxable wages for BC EHT.
More information about BC EHT is located on the BC government
website: https://www2.gov.bc.ca/gov/content/taxes/employer-health-tax.
Configure Reduced Quebec Health Services Fund (HSF) Rates
Client administrators can configure a reduced Quebec Health Services Fund (HSF) rate. The
reduced rate applies to qualified Quebec legal entities identified as small or mid-sized businesses
(SMBs) in the primary and manufacturing sectors with less than $5 million in annual payroll.
To configure reduced Quebec HSF rates:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity and select a legal entity.
2. Click the Tax Authorities tab and select the Quebec Health Services Fund.
3. In the Tax Setting section to the right, click Add.
4. In the Effective Start field, enter the date that the reduced rate takes effect.
5. (Optional) In the Effective End field, enter the date that the rate expires.
6. Select the Exempt Tax And Taxable Wages checkbox, if necessary.
7. In the Gross Annual Payroll field, enter the amount for the setting.
8. In the Reduction of the HSF Contribution Rate drop-down list, select SMB in the Primary or
Manufacturing Sector.
9. Click Save.
When configured, Dayforce applies a reduced HSF rate based on the legal entity's gross annual
payroll total.
Part XIII Tax

-- 354 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 355 of 0
Part XIII tax is a federal withholding tax on specific types of income paid out to employees who
are non-residents of Canada. As a Canadian employer, you must withhold this tax and remit them
to the Canadian Revenue Agency (CRA) as well as fill out a NR4 slip for every non-resident whose
income was deducted.
Dayforce calculates the Part XIII tax on earnings that are configured to report the tax, and on
employees set up as non-residents in their employee record in People. See Earnings Subject to
Part XIII Tax.
In Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity, the Part XIII tax authority is shown in the Tax
Authorities tab for Canadian legal entities.
In the Company Tax ID Number column for this tax, you need to record your organization's non-
resident account number. You must include the letters NRF at the beginning of the account
number. This account number is used on the NR4 slips.
In the Tax Setting section for this tax, you can override the default tax rate by entering a value
between 0 and 25%. Any other value will be ignored and the default rate is applied instead.
More information about Part XIII tax is available on the Canadian government
website: https://www.canada.ca/en/revenue-agency/services/tax/international-non-
residents/payments-non-residents/nr4-part-xiii-tax/part-xiii-withholding-tax.html.
Employment Allowance and SER for Legal Entities
Eligible employers can configure UK legal entities in Dayforce to claim an Employment Allowance
or Small Employers' Relief (SER).
The Employment Allowance can qualify the legal entity for a reduction in its National Insurance bill.
For details about Employment Allowance and employer eligibility requirements, see the site
https://www.gov.uk/claim-employment-allowance.
Important: As of 6 April 2020, there is no longer a flat-rate amount for the Employment Allowance.
Employers must apply to be awarded an Employment Allowance, and the amount can be different
for each employer. The amount is also cleared at the start of every fiscal year and must therefore
be entered manually each year.
The SER can qualify a legal entity to reclaim certain amounts for statutory pay, (for example,
Statutory Maternity Pay, Paternity, Adoption and Shared Parental Pay). Detailed information about
partial and full recovery of SER, as well as the rules governing the effective start date and the
calculation of SER, can be found at https://www.gov.uk/recover-statutory-payments.
Employment Allowance details and Small Employers' Relief are included in the EPS file
transmitted to HMRC, which you can verify in the Tax Month Management sub-tab in Payroll
> Post Commit Management, in the Tax Month Preview slide-out panel, in the EPS Summary tab.

-- 355 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 356 of 0
Employment Allowance and Small Employers' Relief are both configured in Org Setup > Org
Payroll Setup > Organization for a selected legal entity, in the Tax Setting section of the Tax
Authorities tab for the National Insurance ER (employer) entry. These tax settings are start-date
effective, because requirements can change at the start of the tax year. To allow for mid-year
implementation, enter the start date that the parameters go into effect to ensure that the correct
processing period is used for calculation.
The Tax Setting section for National Insurance ER (employer) contains the following options:
Agriculture Sector: Select this checkbox to indicate that the tax setting is for the agriculture
sector. This is included in the EPS file.

allowance.

allowance must be calculated.
Employment Allowance: Enter the annual employment allowance amount. As of 6 April
2020, the employment allowance amount must be entered manually every year.
Expected annual payroll exceeds Apprenticeship Levy Threshold: Select this checkbox to
indicate that the annual payment exceeds the apprenticeship levy threshold and that the
annual apprenticeship levy must be calculated.
Important: If you select this checkbox, you must also select one of the sector checkboxes or
the State Aid Rules Do Not Apply checkbox, otherwise you will not be able to save this
record.
Fisheries and Aquaculture Sector: Select this checkbox to indicate that the tax setting is for
the fisheries and aquaculture sector. This is included in the EPS file.
Industrial Sector: Select this checkbox to indicate that the tax setting is for the industrial
sector. This is included in the EPS file.
Road Transport Sector: Select this checkbox to indicate that the tax setting is for the road
transport sector. Included in the EPS file.
State Aid Rules Do Not Apply: Select this checkbox to indicate that the tax setting is exempt
from state aid rules.
Statutory Payment Recovery Type: Select one of the following options: None, Partial, or Full.
None: The statutory recovery compensation isn’t applicable. This is also the option if
the field is left blank.
Partial: Recovery = Amount*92% and NIC Compensation = 0.
Full: Recovery = Amount and NIC Compensation = Amount*3%.

Specify Employee Tax Percentage for Washington Paid Family Leave
The Washington state paid family leave program provides up to 12 weeks of protected leave in a
12-month period for eligible employees. By default, the employee pays up to 63% of the premium
cost (EPFL & EMLI combined) and the employer pays the remaining 37% (MLIR).
You have the option to specify the percentage rate responsible by employees and employers for
Washington Paid Family Leave employee taxes and medical premiums in Dayforce for medical
leave and paid family leave (regular and voluntary) tax authorities. For example, you can pay more
than the 37%, such as a 50/50 amount, to override the contribution amount by the employee or
employer that doesn’t allow selecting an option below 37%.
You can specify the unemployment insurance tax rate based on the employer's experience rating
that was assigned by the state agency (that is, other than the standard rate) in the Experience
Rate field in the Tax Setting section. By doing so, you override the default contribution rate that is
used in the system and apply the specified rate to all employees for its tax authority. When
specifying the unemployment tax rate in the Experience Rate field, enter the percentage rate in a
decimal format. For example, if the tax unemployment rate is 3.25%, enter 0.0325. See Tax
Settings and Tax Qualifiers for Tax Authorities.
To specify percentage rate for Washington paid family leave employee taxes:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity and select a US legal entity.
2. Click the Tax Authorities tab and select the Washington tax authority from the list displayed.
For example, Washington - Paid Family Leave Voluntary - Employer.
3. Click New in the Tax Setting section, to the right of the list of tax authorities.
4. Enter the date that the unemployment insurance leave starts in the Effective Start field.
5. (Optional) Enter the date that the unemployment insurance leave expires in the Effective
End field.
6. Enter the unemployment insurance tax rate that was assigned to you by the state agency in
the Experience Rate field in a decimal format.
7. Click Save.

Setup > Legal Entity, which is described in detail in the topic Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity

2. In the Check Details section, select the checkbox next to the option Use for Non-Dayforce
Checks.
3. In the Authorizing Messages 2 field, enter the alternate message to display on non-Dayforce
checks.
4. Click Save.

The Workers Comp Tab
The Workers Comp tab in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity has a list of any tax
authorities configured for the legal entity.
For Canada legal entities, you must configure WCB rates for all provinces in which your legal
entity has employees.
For US legal entities, the Workers Comp tab is used to add information about the organization and
its legal entities to the Workers Compensation Report. The report allows a client to collect data and
complete state-required filing returns or to provide the required information to third-party providers
who assist with these filings.

Multiple Worksite Reporting
Multiple Worksite Reporting helps in the collection of statistical reporting data for employers who
have more than one physical worksite in a state; that is, a primary worksite and at least one
secondary worksite.
Before You Begin: This topic applies to US legal entities only.
Generally, the Multiple Worksite Report (or MWR) is required for employers who have a total of 10
or more employees in a state with both primary and secondary worksite locations that are covered
under a single State Unemployment Insurance (or SUI) account. This means that if your
organization has multiple worksites in a state, and the total number of employees working in all
locations in the state is 10 or more, you are probably required to file the Multiple Worksite Report.
For information about Multiple Worksite Reporting, including requirements, see the U.S. Bureau of
Labor Statistics site, https://www.bls.gov/respondents/mwr/home.htm.
Configuring Multiple Worksite Reporting involves the following:

-- 364 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 365 of 0
Adding unique worksite numbers to each worksite location for a legal entity (in Org Setup
> Org Payroll Setup > Multiple Worksite Reporting).
If you're already familiar with the concepts covered in this topic, you can go to Configure Multiple
Worksite Reporting.
To configure Multiple Worksite Reporting in Dayforce, you must assign unique worksite numbers to
each location that is covered under a single SUI account. Assigning each worksite location a
unique identification number allows you to report all locations covered under that SUI.
You can add as many worksites as necessary. After you have configured your worksites, you must
assign the worksite numbers to the appropriate site locations in the organizational hierarchy under
Organization > Legal Entity, in the slide-out panel for the site, in the Legal Entity tab, in the
Worksite [State-Number] drop-down list.
Multiple Worksite Reporting for Legal Entities
A list of multiple worksite reporting locations for US legal entities is shown in Org Setup > Org
Payroll Setup > Multiple Working Reporting if you have added any worksites.
You can configure multiple worksite location entries to produce the Multiple Worksite Report. Enter
the name and contact details of the person responsible for multiple worksite reporting for the legal
entity.
Multiple Worksite Reporting options
Option 	Description
Multiple Worksite Reporting
Select the checkbox to configure the legal entity to use
multiple worksite reporting.

checkbox, you must also enter contact details in the
provided fields.

Configure Multiple Worksite Reporting
Some states require legal entities to define and assign worksite numbers to all their locations when
those legal entities have multiple locations that are covered under a single Unemployment

-- 365 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 366 of 0
Insurance (UI) account. Those states then require those legal entities to report on those locations.
The following states are required to file Multiple Worksite Reports: Alabama, California, Colorado,
Florida, Georgia, Iowa, Kansas, Louisiana, Maine, Maryland, Minnesota, Montana, Nebraska,
Nevada, New Hampshire, New Jersey, New York, North Carolina, North Dakota, Ohio, Oklahoma,
Oregon, South Carolina, Vermont, Virginia, West Virginia, Puerto Rico and the Virgin Islands.
Multiple worksite reporting can only be configured on legal entities with locations in the United
States.
To configure multiple worksite reporting:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Multiple Worksite Reporting and select a legal entity.
2. Select the Multiple Worksite Reporting checkbox.
3. Provide a multiple worksite contact name, title, and phone number in the available fields.
4. Click Add.
5. Select the state in the Worksite State drop-down list.
6. Enter the five-digit, numeric Worksite Number assigned for the worksite. This number is
provided by the state.
7. Enter a name and description of the worksite in the available fields.
8. Enter the reference code.
9. Enter effective dates for the worksite.
10. Enter the worksite's address in the available fields.
11. Select a comment code in the Comments drop-down list. These are provided by the US
Department of Labor's Bureau of Labor Statistics.
12. Click Save.
You can configure as many worksites as necessary. After you configure worksites, you need to
assign the worksite numbers to the appropriate locations in the organizational hierarchy.
Assigning Worksite Numbers
To assign worksite numbers to the physical location or site it represents in the organizational
hierarchy:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and click the Organization tab.
2. Browse the hierarchy, clicking the arrow button to expand levels, until you find the location
or site that you want assigned a worksite number.
3. Select the location and then click the Legal Entity tab.
4. Select the worksite number in the Worksite Name [State-Number] drop-down list.
5. Click Save.

Taxation Parameters for Canada
This section describes how to configure taxation parameters for legal entities in the Taxation
Parameters tab of Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity.
Configure Canadian Status Indian Taxation
If the legal entity employs Status Indian employees that work in a location that meets the
government definition of a reserve, you can configure how the application applies Status Indian
exemptions.
Note: If a payroll administrator records tax amounts for a Status Indian employee in the
Adjustments, Checks, or Quick Entry tabs, the application applies the tax amount regardless of
the configuration.
To configure Status Indian taxation parameters:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity and select a legal entity.
2. Click the Taxation Parameters tab.
3. Select the Apply Status Indian Calculations to Legal Entity’s Employees checkbox.
4. In the Calculate CPP For Status Indians drop-down list, select one of the following options:
Calculate CPP to include CPP/QPP totals in the employee’s tax calculations.
No CPP to exclude CPP/QPP totals in the employee's tax calculations.
5. Click Save.

The STP Parameters Tab
Important: The Australian Taxation Office (ATO) requires that if a legal entity is considered as a
related entity to other entities with different Australian Business Numbers (ABNs), and the legal
entity needs to submit Single Touch Payroll (STP) data for other entities in the group, the related
entity must get a business authority to lodge STP on their behalf.
This authorisation is needed before the initial STP submission. For detailed instructions or more
information, contact the ATO or visit their website at: https://www.ato.gov.au/Business/Single-
Touch-Payroll/Start-reporting/STP-checklists/.
Australian payroll processing works with STP to simplify business payroll reporting obligations to
the ATO. General information about STP is available in Overview of Australian Payroll.
STP parameters are configured for legal entities in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity,
in the STP Parameters tab. The following table contains information about each of these options to
set up the reporting of payroll activity to the Australian Tax Office (ATO).

field.

Overview of New Hire Reporting
New Hire Reporting is configured in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity in the New Hire
Reporting tab.
Before You Begin: This topic applies to US legal entities only.
Role feature access: Org Setup > Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity > New Hire
Reporting
When US employers hire new employees, or rehire previous employees, federal law requires the
employers to report basic information on the new or rehired employees to the state in which the
employees work within 20 days of their hire or rehire date. Some states require employers to report
new hire and rehire information sooner.
After new hire reporting information is sent to states, the states forward the information to the
National Directory of New Hires, which child support agencies use to locate parents who owe
child support and issue income withholding orders. The National Directory of New Hires is
maintained by the Office of the Administration for Children and Families, which is part of the US
Department of Health and Human Services (HHS).
General Process for New Hire Reporting
Dayforce supports the reporting of new hires with the Department of Health and Human Services
(HHS). The following is a summary of this process in Dayforce:
When you commit a pay run, Dayforce automatically runs the Payroll New Hire Export
background job to generate a file based on specifications configured by the Dayforce back
office.
After the file is generated, Dayforce Back Office transmits it to the various state agencies, or
to the single designated state if you are registered as a multistate employer.

-- 377 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 378 of 0
This process of generating the report is automatic and doesn't require user action. However, you
can override certain details about the file for specific legal entities. To override the file, you can
configure the following settings in the New Hire Reporting tab under Org Setup > Org Payroll
Setup > Legal Entity:
Override Employer Address
Override Employer Address Type
Override Employer Contact
Suppress New Hire Reporting
Multistate Employer Reporting
By default, new hire reports are sent to each state in which your newly hired or rehired employees
work. You can, however, configure your instance of Dayforce for multistate reporting, which
requires you to register with HHS as a multistate employer. For general information and details
about requirements for registering as a multistate employer, see the site
https://www.acf.hhs.gov/css/employers/employer-responsibilities/new-hire-reporting.
Registering as a multistate employer and configuring Dayforce so you can report new hires as a
multistate employer minimizes the number of times employees must be reported as new hires,
which is helpful in cases where they are later hired, or rehired in a different state by the same legal
entity.
When you configure Dayforce for multistate employer new hire reporting, you must add an
employer contact, or the report fails. the name of an employer contact, as well as a single
employer address and address type for the contact. This establishes a single contact for new hire
reporting, as well as a central location where any garnishment paperwork can be sent, instead of
each different state location where employees are hired. Instructions for configuring a legal entity
as a multistate employer are available in Configure New Hire Reporting for a Multistate Employer.
Configure New Hire Reporting for a Multistate Employer
When you configure Dayforce for multistate employer new hire reporting, you must add an
employer contact, or the report fails. the name of an employer contact, as well as a single
employer address and address type for the contact.
Important: This topic applies to US legal entities only.

selection for preexisting legal entities, and treats a blank selection as regular payroll.

Single Sites with Multiple Legal Entities
You can assign multiple legal entities to a single site within your organization by using overrides at
the On-Site Department level. This gives you greater flexibility in structuring the organization. It
also provides an additional level of override so that on-site departments within a site can all report
to their own legal entities and each have their own taxation address.
Before You Begin: Make sure that you are familiar with the general concepts in Organization
Hierarchy.
How Overrides Are Applied
Dayforce is bound by the following constraints when applying overrides:
If the Employee Work Location Override is configured, it sets the override.

-- 382 of 472 --

Site level settings are the default if there are no other configurations.
If an On-Site Department level override is configured, it overrides the Site level.
If an override is needed, the tabled address must be used; otherwise the Site level address
applies.
Free form addresses in the Site level are used for taxation unless a tabled address is
selected in the Site level.

Override the Coordinates of Location Addresses
As part of assigning multiple legal entities to a single site, you can enter location addresses for the
legal entities to override the site-level address. Dayforce uses a third-party geocoding tool to
ensure the accuracy of the addresses you've entered. The tool generates a set of coordinates
when it validates the address. These coordinates are then used to determine the appropriate tax
jurisdiction for payroll calculations. When needed, you can override the validated coordinates in
Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Location Addresses.
Note: The override coordinates feature should only be used for US states with local government
taxes.
Before You Begin:
Make sure that you're familiar with the general concepts in Single Sites with Multiple Legal
Entities
Configure the location addresses for the legal entity.
Role feature access:
Org Setup > Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Location Addresses
Org Setup > Org Setup > Organization > Organization > Taxation Address Available
To add override coordinates for a legal entity's location address:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Location Addresses.
2. Expand the custom location address that you want to update.
3. Select the Geo Points Override checkbox.
4. Enter the override coordinates in Latitude and Longitude. The accepted range of values in
Latitude is between +90 and-90. The accepted range of values in Longitude is between
+180 and -180.
5. Important: Dayforce isn’t responsible for the accuracy of the override coordinates you enter.
5. Click Save.
To ensure that the correct tax jurisdiction is used in the payroll calculations, Dayforce clears the
override coordinates when you change any of the following fields in the location address: Country
Code, State/Province, Address, Address Line 2, County, City, and Zip/Postal Code.
Configure Legal Entity for Early Filing Status

-- 386 of 472 --

In the United States and Canada, when a legal entity is sold or goes out of business mid-year,
employers must generate, print, and distribute tax forms to employees within 30 days of notifying
the government. Also, within these 30 days, employers must send the completed tax forms to the
government for processing. In Dayforce, you can update the legal entity with an end date and
update the status to report an out of business, lost tax form, or new seasonal operation status for
government mid-year reporting for early filers.
Note: Amendments aren’t available for early filers until February of the following year. Also, US
1099 and D2X tax forms aren’t eligible for early filing.
To configure a legal entity for early filing:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity and select the US or Canadian legal
entity.
2. In the Legal Entity Status drop-down list, select the applicable status such as Lost with Tax
Forms and Filing or Out of Business (Accelerated).
3. In the Effective End field, enter an end date.
4. Go to Year End > Canada Year End or Year End > USA Year End, select the applicable
year from the Year drop-down list to run the year end process for the affected legal entity.
5. In the Process Job drop-down list, select a filing option such as Generate Preview, Request
Print, or Distribute for Filing.
6. Click Save.

Customer Funding Identifiers for Canadian Legal Entities
For Canadian legal entities, you can specify the funding account used by the legal entity to pay its
employees in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity in the Customer Funding Identifiers
tab.
You can also set the funding account at the pay group level in Pay Setup > Pay Group, in the
Payroll Properties tab, by entering the account number in the Identifier field. As a best practice,
you should configure a funding identifier at the pay group level, even if you are configuring a legal
entity level funding identifier. Additional information is available in Pay Groups.
Important: Legal entity funding identifiers override pay group funding identifiers.
Configuring a customer funding identifier for a Canadian legal entity ensures that employees in
pay groups under that legal entity are paid using the account associated with the legal entity
funding identifier, regardless of any identifier set at the pay group level.
The process to determine what funding identifier to use is determined by Dayforce during the
sales and contracting process.
Customer Funding Identifiers for Canada
Canadian customer funding identifiers conform to the following specifications:
The customer funding identifier must start with the letters E, F, or L (to indicate the series),
then have an alphanumeric character other than O, I, or Z, then have three numeric
characters.
The identifiers E4000, F4000, and L4000 are reserved and cannot be used.

Employment Insurance in Canada

-- 389 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 390 of 0
In Canada, both employees and employers make contributions to employment insurance (or EI)
premiums. Employee contribution amounts are determined by employee insurable earnings
multiplied by the federal (or provincial, in Quebec) rate, up to a maximum annual insurable
earnings amount. You can locate the latest Federal and provincial (Quebec) EI premium rates and
maximums by visiting https://www.canada.ca.
Employers must contribute EI premiums based on a factor of 1.4 times the employee's premium
contribution (there can be exceptions: see https://www.canada.ca and talk with your
implementation consultant). If we take Linda as an example again Employers also have a federal –
or provincial, for Quebec – maximum annual employer premium amount. As a rule, the employer
is responsible for the following:
Deducting employee EI premiums from the employee's insurable earnings up to a maximum
annual premium amount
Contributing employer EI premiums, calculated by multiplying employee contributions by
1.4, up to a maximum annual employer premium amount
For the year 2018, for employee contributions, the federal rate is 1.66% on a maximum annual
insurable earnings amount of $51,700, for a maximum annual employee contribution amount of
$858.22. The employer maximum annual premium amount is $1,201.51.
For example, if Linda lives in Ontario and earns $30,000 annually, her total annual EI contribution
amount would be $489, calculated as follows: $30,000 x 1.66% = $489
The employer's total annual EI contribution amount would be $684.60, calculated by multiplying
Linda's amount by 1.4: $489 x 1.4 = $684.60
However, if Linda's annual salary were $95,000, her total EI contributions would be $858.22, and
her employer's contributions would be $1,201.51, because the 2018 maximum annual insurable
earnings amount is $51,700.
To set the employment insurance factors for a legal entity, you need to create at least one EI rate
group and reference code entry and save it, effectively assigning it to the legal entity.
If the legal entity has received permission from Service Canada to remit employment insurance
premiums at a lower rate, you can enter an additional EI rate group and reference code with a
lower defined factor. If you configure multiple EI rate groups for a legal entity, you can override the
default rate group at the employee level in People for a selected employee in the Payroll > Tax
Definitions screen in the Employee Payroll Tax section. Instructions and additional information are
available in the topic Assign EI Rates to Employees.
In the following screenshot, you can see the entries for employment insurance rates for a selected
legal entity in the Employment Insurance sub-tab:

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 391 of 0

Dayforce Implementation Guide

After you have created employment insurance rates for a legal entity, you can assign them to
employees. See Assign EI Rates to Employees.
Set the Employer EI Rate for a Legal Entity
When the legal entity gets permission from Service Canada to remit employment insurance (EI)
premiums at a lower rate, you need to set custom EI rates (or factors) for a legal entity. To set a
custom rate, you must create at least one EI Rate Group with a corresponding Reference Number
with the lower factor, and assign the rate group to the legal entity.
If more than one EI reference number is configured for a legal entity, you can assign a preferred
reference number at the legal entity level or at the employee level. A number assigned at the
employee level in People in Payroll > Tax Definitions in the Employee Payroll Tax section overrides
the number assigned at the legal entity level.
Before You Begin: Make sure you're familiar with the concepts in Employment Insurance in
Canada.
To set a custom EI factor for a legal entity:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity and select a legal entity.
2. Click the Employment Insurance tab.
3. To create the EI rate group entry:
a. Click Add.
b. In the Rate Group field, enter the rate group name.
c. In the Reference Code field, enter the EI reference number that is four digits long.
d. Select the Is Default checkbox to set this entry as the default rate for the legal entity.
e. Click Save.
4. To enter an EI rate for the rate group entry:
a. In the Rates section, click Add.
b. In the Rate field, enter the EI factor. The rate for the default should be 1.4.
c. In the Start Date field, enter or select the effective start date for the EI factor.
d. (Optional) In the End Date field, enter an effective end date of the EI factor. Dayforce
only uses the factor during its effective date range up to the end date.
e. Click Save.
After you've created an EI factor entry, you can assign it to employees in People, in the Payroll
> Tax Definitions screen, in the Employee Payroll Tax section. Information and instructions are
available in Assign EI Rates to Employees.
Assign EI Rates to Employees
In some cases, a specific employee might be entitled to a different employment insurance rate.
Employee-level employment insurance factors can override the factors set at the legal entity level.

-- 392 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 393 of 0
Note: The employment insurance Override Parameters section is only displayed when you select
a Canadian employee.
You can record employment insurance factors for specific employees in the Employee Payroll Tax
section of the Payroll > Tax Definitions screen in People.
To record employment insurance rates for specific employees:
1. Go to People, open the employee profile, and click Payroll > Tax Definitions.
2. In the Employee Payroll Tax section, select the employer's employment insurance tax.
3. Click Add.
4. Enter the effective start date of the employment insurance rate in the Effective From field.
The application uses the factor only during its effective date range.
5. (Optional) Enter the effective end date of the employment insurance rate in the Effective To
field.
6. In the Override Parameters section under the effective dates, select the employee's
reduced rate group in the Reduced EI Rate drop-down list. This list is populated with the
EI rate groups configured in Org Setup. See Employment Insurance in Canada.
7. Click Save.
Configure Payroll Numbers for Specific Payments (Canada Only)
In some cases, your organization might choose to set up supplementary wage insurance to top
up the amounts paid by government when employees are laid off, go on parental leave, or are
absent from work for other legitimate reasons. This can require making and reporting separate
payments to private insurance programs.
To accommodate this, you will need the following:
Two separate RP (payroll) numbers - an existing one and another to apply to the specific
payments
One or more new rate groups
A new (or modified existing) check template
One or more new (or modified existing) payroll policies that include the Canadian
Employment Insurance Rate Rule that includes (or excludes) the appropriate check
template or templates
To set up payroll numbers:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity.
2. Locate and select the Canadian legal entity you want to work with.
3. Click the Employment Insurance tab, which loads a list of any existing rate groups and a
Rates section below that displays rates for the selected rate group.
4. Click Add.

-- 393 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 394 of 0
5. Enter a name in the Rate Group field.
6. In the Reference Code field, enter the payroll (RP) number.
7. In the Rates section, click Add to add a rate for this group.
8. Click Save.
After you have created the new rate groups, the next task is to determine which of your check
templates should be targeted to it. Typically, you will need to create a check template for this
purpose. Information about check templates and how to configure them is available in Check
Templates and Check Types.
Finally, you will need to create or update an existing payroll policy for Employment Insurance
rules. One policy must be configured to include your new rate group and include your new check
template. Another must be configured to include your other rate groups and to exclude your new
check template.
Link Legal Entities to Org Units
Each location in the organization configured as a site needs to be part of a configured legal entity
so that the employees working at each site are paid by the appropriate legal entity.
The application links legal entities to org units based on the legal entity's country, as well as the
country selected for the org unit's address in the Address tab within the Organization tab of Org
Setup > Organization.
To link legal entities to sites:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and click the Organization tab.
2. Select the site you want to assign a legal entity to.
3. Ensure that the org unit has a country selected in the Country Code drop-down list in the
Address tab.
4. Click the Legal Entity tab.
5. Click Add.
6. Select an entity in the Legal Entity drop-down list.
7. If you have configured multiple worksite reporting, you can select the worksite number
applicable to the org unit in the Worksite Name [State-Number] drop-down list.
8. See Configure Multiple Worksite Reporting.
8. Define an effective date range for the legal entity assignment.
9. Click Save.
Historical Payroll Data Loading
When implementing Dayforce Payroll mid-year for an organization, all payroll information for the
year up to the point that the organization starts using Dayforce Payroll must be loaded in
Dayforce.

-- 394 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 395 of 0
Before You Begin: The audience for this content is Dayforce Services Representatives and
Implementation Consultants who have database access and can log in to the application using a
user role configured as a Service Role.
The following topics describe the process of loading historical payroll data into Dayforce before
switching over to Dayforce Payroll.
Set the Payroll History Load Type
Load Payroll Historical Data
Enter YTD Amounts of Employer Taxes for Canadian Legal Entities
Set the Payroll History Load Type
You must set the payroll history load type to load payroll history in Dayforce. You must have
database administrator access to perform this task.
There are three options for setting the database field PayrollHistoryLoadType on the
Client table:
0: No earning statement history was loaded.
1: Earning statement history was imported using the Earning Statement Import to show
historical earning statements prior to the payroll cut over date.
2: Earning statement history was imported using the Pay Run History Import as archived
pay runs and to show historical earning statements for those archived pay runs prior to the
payroll cut over date.
Set the Payroll History Load Type
To set the payroll history load type:
1. Set the database field PayrollHistoryLoadType on the Client table to enable the
features you require. The recommended setting is 2.
2. Set the PayrollCutoverDate field on the Client table to the date that marks the
boundary between payroll history imported from another application and live payroll data
generated and calculated by Dayforce Payroll.
3. Note: This date can be overridden at the pay group level in Pay Setup > Pay Group if a date
has been defined on the Client table.
Setting PayrollHistoryLoadType to 2 enables the following behaviors:
Record of Employment (ROEs)
ROEs read values from the MigratedROEData import for any periods prior to the cut-over date.
This data can be imported using the Dayforce Migrated ROE History Import.

-- 395 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 396 of 0
Earning Statements
All earning statements read imported data, if it exists, for pay periods prior to the cut-over date.
This data can be imported using the Dayforce Pay Run History Import.
Payroll Reports
Payroll reports are not available for periods that are prior to the cut-over date.
Employer YTD Taxes
For Canadian customers, there is no dependency on the PayrollHistoryLoadType value. At the
legal entity level for each Canadian pay group, the YTD taxes can be inserted for the migration
year and the Payroll Register Report, Payroll Summary Report, the Preview tab in Payroll, and any
year end files generated use the inserted amounts in the aggregation (at the pay group level
only) of YTD totals.
Load Payroll Historical Data
After the payroll history load type has been set, you can load payroll historical data using the
Dayforce Pay Run History Import interface specification.
Download the Dayforce Interface Specifications ZIP file and see the Dayforce Pay Run History
Import Specification document for information on how to use this interface.
Incomplete Payroll Historical Data
Functionality exists that allows Dayforce Service Representatives implementing Dayforce Payroll to
import incomplete historical data, missing either wage or tax amounts for different tax authorities,
and have Dayforce recalculate the pay run and generate the missing data based on the earnings
and deductions data imported, as well as Dayforce’s current configuration.
For example, the historical data being imported for an employee contains $1,200 in regular
earnings, $500 in bonus earnings, but no wage or tax amounts. Using this functionality, Dayforce
can calculate what employer and employee taxes were paid in the imported pay run. The
calculations are based on a variety of factors that must already be configured in Dayforce for the
recalculation to occur, including:
The employee must have a valid payroll policy applied to them that applies their earnings
and taxes.
The employee’s home and work address information.
The organizational hierarchy and legal entity configuration.
Earning and deductions are configured with the appropriate tax and compliance codes.

-- 396 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 397 of 0
The effectiveness of the recalculation of wages and taxes is tied to the proper and complete
configuration of Dayforce. To calculate the appropriate New York state taxes the employee pays
on the imported earnings, as an example, the employee’s home and work address must be
accurate in Dayforce.
It’s important to note that when migrating customers to Dayforce Payroll every effort should be
made to import the appropriate data from the previous payroll system; the functionality described
in this entry should only be used when the complete data does not exist.
Before You Begin: This functionality should only be used before Dayforce Payroll has gone live
and before any pay runs have been committed.
Note: This functionality requires database access and can only be performed by Dayforce
Services or Support Representatives accessing Dayforce using a user account configured as a
service role.
To import incomplete historical data:
1. Services Representatives can specify 0 in the fields in the import file where the data does
not exist. Specifically, record 0 in the Amount, CurrentWageBasis, and TotalTaxableWages
fields of the PayRunTax and PayRunTaxMethodDetail sections of the import file.
2. Dayforce still accepts the import file with a 0 value in these fields; the historical pay run is
imported as normal. If viewed or reported on in Payroll > Pay Run Management, the
imported pay run wouldn’t contain tax or wage amount for the tax authorities imported with 0
values in these fields.
2. A representative with database access needs to mark within the database that the pay run
can be recalculated. This is done by updating the IsSetup field to 1 in the PRPayRun table
for the imported pay run with incomplete data.
3. Log in to Dayforce using a service role.
4. Define for which tax authorities Dayforce should calculate tax and wage amounts within the
pay run. This functionality is controlled by the Generate Tax in Setup Pay Run and Generate
Wages in Setup Pay Run checkboxes in Payroll Setup > Payroll Taxes.
5. By default, these checkboxes are cleared for each tax authority. Select the appropriate
checkbox for each corresponding tax authority that was imported with missing data.
6. For example, if the imported pay run didn’t contain tax amounts for the California State
Withholding Tax, select its Generate Tax in Setup Pay Run checkbox to configure Dayforce
to calculate the tax amount based on the imported earnings.
7. Note: To perform these steps, you must access Dayforce using a service role. ‘Service role’
refers to a user role configured to access restricted areas of Dayforce. These roles are
limited to Dayforce Services and Support Representatives.
5. Run the Calculate Payroll background task in System Admin > Background Jobs, specifying
the pay run’s start and end date in the appropriate fields, selecting the run’s pay group in
the Pay Group drop-down list, and selecting the Include Committed Data Only checkbox.

-- 397 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 398 of 0
10. The task calculates the tax and wage amounts for the tax authorities with the Generate Tax
in Setup Pay Run and Generate Wages in Setup Pay Run checkboxes selected for any pay
run with IsSetup set to 1 in the database that intersects the date range specified in the
task’s Start Date and End Date parameters.
11. Dayforce creates additional records in the pay run results for the calculated amounts and
does not modify any imported values. This means that if a tax or wage amount for a tax
authority was imported and then incorrectly flagged for recalculation, by selecting either the
Generate Tax in Setup Pay Run or Generate Wages in Setup Pay Run checkbox, both the
imported and calculated amount records are included in the pay run results and the
amounts will be doubled.
12. Important: It’s crucial that only the taxes without tax or wage information that have been
imported with 0 values are calculated using this functionality.
13. Because calculated amounts never overwrite imported amounts, if there are imported
amounts that need to be corrected, the data needs to be reimported.
Enter YTD Amounts of Employer Taxes for Canadian Legal Entities
To keep their tax records accurate, Canadian legal entities that start using Payroll midyear in
Dayforce must enter amounts already paid for EI, CPP, QPP, and various provincial and territorial
health taxes. Many of these legal entities migrated to Dayforce Payroll midyear, or began by using
the WFM features and later added Payroll to their Dayforce system.
In the YTD Amount tab in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity, you can enter the
employer deductions paid for the year to date before the payroll start date. These amounts must
include total taxable wages and limited taxable wages.
Before You Begin: This topic is meant for Implementation users. You should only use the
YTD Amount tab if you can't include one or more employer taxes in the Pay Run History Import as
part of the implementation process. For details about that import, download the Dayforce Interface
Specifications ZIP file and see the Dayforce Pay Run History Import Specification document.
If the legal entity has more than one pay group, create a record for each pay group and split the
amounts appropriately.
To enter YTD amounts for a migrating Canadian legal entity:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity and select a Canadian legal entity.
2. Click the YTD Amount tab.
3. In the Pay Group drop-down list, select a pay group for which you want to enter previous
YTD amounts.
4. In the Funding Identifier drop-down list, select a funding identifier.
5. In the Migration Year drop-down list, select the year when the legal entity migrated to
Dayforce Payroll.

-- 398 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 399 of 0
6. In the Employer Employment Insurance (EI) section, click Add to create an entry and fill out
the following fields:
EI Rate Group: Select the EI rate group.
Tot Taxable Wage: Enter total taxable wage.
Ltd Taxable Wage: Enter limited taxable wage.
Taxes: Enter taxes.
7. In the Employer Canada Pension Plan (CPP) section, click Add to create an entry and fill out
the following fields:
EI Rate Group: Select the EI rate group.
Tot Taxable Wage: Enter total taxable wage.
Ltd Taxable Wage: Enter limited taxable wage.
Taxes: Enter taxes.
8. In the Health Taxes section, enter the insurable wages earned by the pay group's
employees in the Wages field of the appropriate taxes and premiums. For example, enter
the pay group's insurable wages for EI in the Wages field in the Employer Employment
Insurance (EI) section.
9. Enter the taxes paid for the pay group's employees in the Taxes field of the appropriate
taxes and premiums.
10. Click Save.
The health tax wage amounts affect whether the health taxes are applied. Each tax has an
exemption amount, so when wages are below that limit, the tax isn’t paid. When a legal entity
reaches the legislated threshold for each health tax, Dayforce automatically calculates and
applies the tax. The prior wage amount entered in the YTD Amount tab helps determine when that
threshold is reached for a legal entity in a migration year. These amounts are also reported in the
Payroll Register and Payroll Summary Report.
The Fiscal Calendar Feature
A fiscal calendar is essentially an annual accounting period that might or might not coincide with
the calendar year. Fiscal calendars are used for accounting, the general ledger, and for producing
annual statements. Payroll Setup > Fiscal Calendars is divided into two tabs: Fiscal Calendars,
where you can create and manage fiscal calendars; and Fiscal Years, where you can create and
manage fiscal years.
The concept of the fiscal year is associated with fiscal calendars. If your organization uses a fiscal
year (or accounting period, if you are in the United Kingdom) that does not coincide with the
calendar year, you have the option of configuring one or more fiscal calendars in Dayforce that
you can assign to legal entities in your organization.
You must configure a fiscal calendar if you intend to configure an earning or deduction grouping
using an accumulation type. Additional information is available in Deduction and Earning
Groupings.

-- 399 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 400 of 0
Important: One example of a fiscal calendar that does not correspond with the calendar year is
the fiscal calendar for the United Kingdom, which has a fiscal year of April 6 to April 5. However, it
isn’t mandatory to configure a fiscal calendar for UK legal entities in Dayforce as part of normal
setup for UK payroll.
As a rule, the fiscal calendar has nothing to do with year end processing for employee taxes.
To use a custom fiscal calendar in Dayforce, you must create a fiscal calendar and then assign a
legal entity to the year. There are two steps to this process:
Create a fiscal calendar in the Fiscal Calendar tab. See The Fiscal Calendar Tab.
Assign the calendar to a legal entity in Org Setup > Organization. See Assign a Custom
Fiscal Calendar to a Legal Entity.
A potential third step is the addition of a fiscal year to a fiscal calendar. See Fiscal Years Tab.
The Fiscal Calendar Tab
You use the Fiscal Calendars tab in Payroll Setup > Fiscal Calendar to create new or manage
existing fiscal calendars. The fiscal calendars created in this tab can be used in the Fiscal Years
tab.
The Fiscal Calendars tab contains the following fields and controls:
Name: The name for the fiscal calendar.
Description: The description of the fiscal calendar.
Month by Payroll Date: Specifies when a pay period is considered part of a month and has
two options:
Pay Date: The pay date determines the fiscal month. For example, if a pay period
ends in April, but has a pay date in May, then Dayforce considers the pay period to
belong to the fiscal month of May.
Pay Period End Date: The pay period end date determines the fiscal month. For
example, if a pay period ends in April, then Dayforce considers that pay period to
belong to the fiscal month of April.
Start Date: The start date for the fiscal calendar.
Starting Month: The starting month for the fiscal calendar.
Quarter Pattern: The pattern that determines the number of weeks in each of the quarters
for the fiscal year. For example, to set quarters to have two 4-week periods and one 5-week
period, select the 4-4-5 pattern. The options are:
4-4-5
4-5-4
5-4-4
Last Quarter Pattern: The pattern that determines the number of weeks in the last quarter of
the fiscal year. The options are:

-- 400 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 401 of 0
4-4-6
4-5-5
4-6-4
5-4-5
5-5-4
6-4-4
You can also change existing calendars in the Fiscal Calendar tab. When you select a calendar
row, its fields become editable. You can make any changes you need and click Save to commit
them.
Three other options are available for managing calendars:
Copy: Creates a duplicate instance of the selected calendar at the top of the list, where you
can make such changes as you need and click Save to save the new calendar.
Delete: You can delete a calendar by clicking this and then clicking OK when asked to
confirm the deletion.
Localize: Opens a dialog box where, by clicking Add, you insert a row to the localization list
that enables you to select the local language for the calendar from the Language drop-
down list, and to enter a localized Name for the calendar, and a Description.
In the following example screenshot, you can see a fiscal calendar with a starting month of May
that has a quarterly pattern of 4-4-5 at the bottom of the list.
You can add fiscal years to your new calendar in the Fiscal Years tab. See Fiscal Years Tab.
Add Fiscal Calendars
To add a fiscal calendar:
1. Go to Payroll Setup > Fiscal Calendar.
2. Click the Fiscal Calendars tab.
3. Click Add.
4. Enter a name and, optionally, a description for the fiscal calendar.
5. In the Month by Payroll Date drop-down list, select Pay Date or Pay Period End Date.
6. In the Start Date field, enter a start date for the fiscal calendar.
7. In the Starting Month drop-down list, select the month the calendar should begin with.
8. In the Quarter Pattern drop-down list, select the pattern of weeks for the quarters.

-- 401 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 402 of 0
9. In the Last Quarter Pattern drop-down list, you can optionally designate a different pattern
of weeks for the last quarter of the fiscal year.
10. Click Save.
When you click Save, the calendar is also available for use in the Fiscal Year tab.
Fiscal Years Tab
The Fiscal Years tab provides the means to manage fiscal years, and is accessed by going to
Payroll Setup > Fiscal Calendar and selecting the Fiscal Years tab. This tab contains the fiscal
calendar settings created for the fiscal years, and can contain a list of more than one year for a
selected fiscal calendar. After you have created the basic fiscal calendar entry, you can create a
calendar for individual years by specifying the start date, the starting month, and configuring a
pattern for the quarters.
At least one fiscal calendar must exist in the system before you can add and configure a fiscal
year. If there are no calendars available when you access the Fiscal Years tab, you will need to
add a calendar in the Fiscal Calendars tab. See The Fiscal Calendar Feature.
The Fiscal Years tab contains the following fields and controls:
On the left, the list of available fiscal calendars and the fiscal years currently grouped under
them.
A General section, displaying the following fields:
Name: The name for the fiscal year (required)
Fiscal Year: The fiscal year calendar year (for example, 2019) (required)
Begin Date: The starting date inherited from the fiscal calendar (required)
Fiscal Calendar: The fiscal calendar that the fiscal year is grouped under. This is an
important consideration because the fiscal year will inherit the calendar's start date
and year and weekly periods from its parent fiscal calendar.
Description: A general identifier for this fiscal year
A Periods in Year list, displaying:
Fiscal Period: The number of the fiscal period
Name: The period's name
Description: A general identifier for the period
Weeks In Period: The number of weeks in the period
Quarter: In which fiscal quarter the period occurs
Begin Date: The date the period begins
A Weeks in Period list, displaying:
Period Week: The number of the period week within the period
Fiscal Week: The number of the fiscal week within the period
Begin Date: The date the fiscal week begins

Two additional options are available:
Delete: You can delete a year by clicking this and then clicking OK when asked to confirm
the deletion.
Localize: Clicking this opens a dialog box where, by clicking Add, you insert a row in the
localization list that enables you to select the local language for the year in the Language
drop-down list, enter a localized name for the year in the Name field, and enter a
description in the Description field.
Add Fiscal Years
To add a fiscal year:
1. Go to Payroll Setup > Fiscal Calendar.
2. Click the Fiscal Years tab.
3. Click Add and select the fiscal calendar you want the new fiscal year to be assigned to.
This selection preconfigures the Begin Date and Fiscal Calendar fields (and locks them),
and the Periods in Year and Weeks in Period lists.
4. Enter a name and, optionally, a description for the fiscal year.
5. In the Fiscal Year field, enter the year the fiscal year begins.
6. Click Save.

Medicare-Only Legal Entities and Filers
Both Medicare-Only and Regular employers each have separate validation rules for creating legal
entities and employee records, committing payroll, and creating reports. The following tax types
are affected:
Fed MWT EE: Federal - Employee Medicare Tax
Fed MWT ER: Federal - Employer Medicare Tax
FICA EE: Federal - Employee Social Security Tax
FICA ER: Federal - Employer Social Security Tax
Regular filers must either be exempt from all of FICA EE, FICA ER, Fed MWT EE, and Fed MWT
ER, or exempt from none of these. It isn’t possible to exempt a legal entity or employee from one
or more of these taxes unless they are exempt from all of them. If you try, Dayforce returns the
following error message:
Copy
Invalid tax exemption attempted. Please ensure that Medicare ER, Medicare EE, SocS
Medicare-only filers must be exempt from FICA EE and FICA ER, but must not be exempt from
Fed MWT EE or Fed MWT ER. If you try, Dayforce returns the following error message:
Copy
Invalid tax exemption attempted. Please ensure that SocSec ER and SocSec EE are ma

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 405 of 0
The validations described for Medicare-only legal entities and employees apply when the
employment code for the legal entity is configured for Medicare qualified government employment
– Form 941 in Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup. You can find this by going to Org Setup > Org
Payroll Setup > Legal Entity, selecting a legal entity and clicking the Quarterly/Annual Reporting
Parameters tab.
If you are setting up the tax authorities for a legal entity that is exempt from Federal Medicare and
Social Security Taxes, or if you are setting up employees of a regular filing legal entity who are
exempt from Federal Medicare and Social Security taxes, you must select Exempt Tax And
Taxable Wages for each of the following tax types:
Fed MWT EE: Federal - Employee Medicare Tax
Fed MWT ER: Federal - Employer Medicare Tax
FICA EE: Federal - Employee Social Security Tax
FICA ER: Federal - Employer Social Security Tax
If all four aren’t set, Dayforce returns the following error message:
Copy
Invalid tax exemption attempted. Please ensure that Medicare ER, Medicare EE, SocS
If you are setting up the tax authorities for a Medicare-only legal entity, you must select the option
Exempt Tax And Taxable Wages for each of the following tax types:
FICA EE: Federal - Employee Social Security Tax
FICA ER: Federal - Employer Social Security Tax

Verify Medicare-Only Settings for Legal Entities
To verify Medicare-Only settings for a legal entity:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Legal Entity and select a legal entity.
2. Click the Quarterly/Annual Reporting Parameters tab.
3. In the Employment Code drop-down list, ensure that Medicare Qualified Government
Employment - Form 941 is selected.
4. Click the Tax Authorities tab to view the taxes associated with the legal entity. When you
have selected a tax, view the Tax Setting section to the right of the list of tax authorities.
5. Verify that the Exempt Tax and Taxable Wages checkbox is selected.
6. Repeat steps 5 and 6 for the Federal Employee and Employer Medicare Taxes and Federal
Employee and Employer Social Security Taxes.
Verify Medicare-Only Settings for Employees
To verify Medicare-only settings for an employee:
1. Go to People, open the employee profile, and click Payroll > Tax Definitions.
2. In the Employee Payroll Tax section, select a tax.
3. Verify that the Exempt Tax And Taxable Wages checkbox is selected.
4. Repeat steps 3 and 4 for the Federal Employee and Employer Medicare Taxes and Federal
Employee and Employer Social Security Taxes.
Configure Mobile Org Units
To configure a site as a mobile org unit:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and click the Organization tab.
2. Select a site-level org unit, and click the Properties tab.
3. Ensure that the Physical Location checkbox is selected.
4. Select the Is Mobile Org checkbox.
5. Click Save.
Configure Mobile Org Addresses
After you have configured a mobile org unit, you must also configure mobile org addresses.
To configure mobile org addresses:
1. Go to Org Setup > Org Payroll Setup > Mobile Org Addresses.
2. Enter the name of the mobile org unit.
3. (Optional) Enter a description and reference code.
4. In the Color Code drop-down list, select a color to color-code the mobile org unit for easy
reference in the Mobile Org Schedules feature.

After you have saved one or more mobile org addresses, you must assign them to the mobile org
