Tax reporting parameters for employees are specified at the federal and state level. These
parameters are configured by going to People, loading an employee profile, expanding the
Payroll > Tax Definitions screen, and locating the Quarterly/Annual Reporting Parameters section.
The Quarterly/Annual Reporting Parameters section contains a section in which you can add to
the list of quarterly/annual reporting parameters (if any) for the selected employee. When you
create an entry, or select an existing entry, the entry expands and displays an additional two
sections: General and Details. The choices you make in the General section determine what is
displayed in the Details section. The General section contains the following fields:
Jurisdiction: Drop-down list with federal and state options.
Effective From: Mandatory field that indicates the start date of the parameter
Effective To: Optional field that indicates the end-date of the parameter.

tab.

A driver who distributes beverages (other than milk), or meat, vegetable, fruit, or bakery

wholesalers, retailers, contractors, or operators of hotels, restaurants, or other similar
establishments. The goods sold must be merchandise for resale or supplies for use in the
buyer's business operation. This work must be the salesperson's principal business activity.

Configure Organizational Groups and Subgroups
This section describes the first step to configuring your organization: configuring the groups and
subgroups that make up your organizational hierarchy. You need to configure the top of your
organization and the organizational groups and subgroups, often referred to as org units, that
make up your organization, such as districts and regions, so that the other organizational
elements can be assigned to the appropriate groups in the organization.
It’s important to define and assign levels in a logical manner to the different organizational units
within the organizational hierarchy. Levels don’t have to be parallel, meaning under the Corporate
level (the top of the hierarchy). You can define an organizational unit as a district, with several
sites underneath it, as well a region, which has several districts, each with their own sites
underneath.
For example, the first or top level is the Corporate level but the second level (or the units directly
underneath the first) can be both a district and a region. In this sense they aren’t parallel: there is
an org unit 1 level down from Corporate that is a district but there are also org units 2 levels down
from Corporate that are districts.
Dayforce Payroll uses the levels assigned to org units to group payroll data in some of its reports.
To determine grouping, Dayforce starts at an employee’s site and traverses up the tree until it
finds the org unit with the org level the report is being grouped by and groups the employee’s
data under that org unit.

-- 418 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 419 of 0
As a result, it’s important to logically structure the organizational hierarchy and assign appropriate
levels to the org units in it.
You can configure as many org units as you need to mirror your organization’s structure in Org
Setup.
To configure organizational groups and subgroups:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and click the Organization tab.
2. In the organization hierarchy, select the item under which to create your entry from the
organizational hierarchy. If you’re creating the first org unit, you won’t have any existing org
units to select from, and you can continue to step 3.
3. Click Add.
4. In the slide-out panel that opens, enter the unit’s name and description.
5. (Optional) Select or search for which item in your organization you want the new item to be
under in the Parent Org Unit drop-down list. By default, the new item’s parent is the item you
selected in the organization tree. For the top of the organization, the Parent Org Unit is itself.
6. Click the Effective From calendar icon and select the date on which the unit is an active part
of your organization. By default, Dayforce uses today’s date.
7. (Optional) Select the date on which the location is no longer a part of your organization in
the Effective To field. By default, this field is blank and the new item won’t be removed from
your organizational chart unless you delete it.
8. Enter a cross-reference code in the Reference Code field. Cross-reference codes are used
to export data from Dayforce to other applications and must be unique for each org unit.
9. Important: Don’t use special characters such as hyphens in cross-reference codes. This
can cause an issue where employees are unable to record time in Work > Timesheet.
Dayforce validates the location reference code value against existing values and you can’t
save duplicate values when you edit an existing location or create a location.
9. In the Level drop-down list, select the new item’s level in your organization. By default, new
items can be classified under one of the following levels:
Corporate: Represents the top level of your organization. Typically, you wouldn’t add
new items with the corporate level.
Corporate Site: Represents a physical location where employees at the top of your
organization work; a head office.
District: Represents a group of sites.
On-Site Department: Represents a physical area within a location.
Region: Represents a group of districts. Typically, regions are the levels directly
underneath the corporate level.
Site: Represents a physical location.
10. You can configure additional org levels as required. See Configure Additional Organization
Levels.

-- 419 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 420 of 0
10. Select which week day is considered the start of the week from the Start Day of Week drop-
down list. The application uses this value to determine the start day of the week for the
calendars in Work, Schedules, and Timesheets.
11. Note: When the Start Day of Week setting isn’t specified in the org setup for a user’s primary
location, Dayforce uses the configuration specified in the First Day of Week setting in Site
Setup > Client. If Start Day of Week and First Day of Week have been specified, the
calendars show the Start Day of Week. If both the Start Day of Week and First Day of Week
aren’t specified, the calendars show Sunday as the first day of the week.
11. Skip the following fields for now, because they’re used only for locations, which you will
specify later in the organizational groups definition process: Department, Zone, Comparable
Org Unit, Physical Location, Opening Date, Closing Date, Ledger Code, and Clock Code.
12. Note: For the top of your organizational hierarchy, regions, districts, or any other group or
sub-group in the hierarchy, leave these fields blank. You should select the Physical Location
checkbox only for organizational units with the Site and Corporate Site Org Level.
12. Click Save.

1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and select an org unit.

Form I-9 for completion.

After you configure org levels, they can be selected in the Org Level drop-down list, in the
General subtab of Org Setup > Organization. Org levels are supported by the HR Export
interfaces, using dynamic export tokens to return values associated with the configured levels.
To define a custom organization level:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization.
2. Click the Levels tab, and then click Add.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description for the org level.
4. Enter a cross-reference code in the Reference Code field.
5. Reference codes are used to export data from Dayforce to other applications.

-- 420 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 421 of 0
6. Important: Don’t use special characters such as hyphens in cross-reference codes. This
can cause an issue where employees can’t record time in Work > Timesheet.
5. Click Save.
Override the Coordinates of Site Addresses
Dayforce uses a third-party geocoding tool to ensure the accuracy of the addresses you've
entered. The tool generates a set of coordinates when it validates the address. These coordinates
are then used to determine the appropriate tax jurisdiction for payroll calculations. When needed,
you can override the validated coordinates for site-level addresses in Org Setup > Organization in
the Organization tab.
Note: The override coordinates feature should only be used for US states with local government
taxes.
Before You Begin:
Make sure that you're familiar with the general concepts in Configure Organizational Groups
and Subgroups
Configure the site addresses for your organization.
Role feature access: Org Setup > Org Setup > Organization > Organization
To add override coordinates for a legal entity's location address:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization.
2. In the Organization tab, expand the site address that you want to update.
3. Select the Geo Points Override checkbox.
4. Enter the override coordinates in Latitude and Longitude. The accepted range of values in
Latitude is between +90 and-90. The accepted range of values in Longitude is between
+180 and -180.
5. Important: Dayforce isn’t responsible for the accuracy of the override coordinates you enter.
5. Click Save.
To ensure that the correct tax jurisdiction is used in the payroll calculations, Dayforce clears the
override coordinates when you change any of the following fields in the location address: Country
Code, State/Province, Address, Address Line 2, County, City, and Zip/Postal Code.
Configure Departments
This section describes how to set up your organization’s generic departments in Dayforce.
Departments contain the jobs employees are scheduled to work and are linked to zones, which
receive a portion of a location’s labor budget.

-- 421 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 422 of 0
It’s important to configure all of the different departments that can be in your organization’s various
locations as Dayforce uses departments and zones to organize schedules, jobs, and labor
budgets.
Departments are used in job assignment configuration. See Jobs and Job Assignments
Background.
You can also import departments instead of manually adding them. See Org Setup Import and
Export Configuration.
To add a department:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and click the Departments tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter the department’s name and description.
4. Enter a cross-reference code in the Reference Code field. Reference codes are used to
export data to other applications. These codes must be unique and must not contain
special characters.
5. Click Save.
Zones Configuration
In Dayforce, zones are used to organize a location for labor planning, scheduling, and security
access. Zones are an area in a location that uses part of the labor budget and has employees
scheduled to work in it. A common example of a zone is an area in a store that sells similar
products, like the Home Theater zone in an electronics store. However, a zone doesn't need to
generate sales or transactions. A stock room in a clothing store is a zone because employees are
scheduled to work in it and those labor hours are budgeted for, but the zone doesn't directly
generate sales. Similarly, organizations in the manufacturing industry wouldn't consider sales
when deciding what areas of a plant need to be zones. They might have a zone for each line in
the plant.
Although you need to configure a zone for each staffed area in your location, each location
doesn’t need to have a zone. Zones might only describe certain locations in your organization. For
example, in a hotel chain, the Lounge zone needs to be configured to plan, schedule, and track
the performance of the bar and lounge in the company's high-end hotels. Because the bar and
lounge area are only present in high-end hotels, the Lounge zone is only assigned to certain
locations.
Assigning appropriate zones helps users manage their locations. A manager of a hotel without a
lounge wouldn't want it as a department on the hotel's schedule or see it in the labor budget in
Plan, as the hotel won't use any of its labor budget staffing an area it doesn’t have.

-- 422 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 423 of 0
You can organize your locations into as many zones as needed. For example, a specialty audio
retail store that tracks sales between headphones, mini-systems, speakers, and receivers would
need at least four zones configured in Dayforce. The store could also have zones for customer
service, receiving, or any other staffed area.
All zones configuration, from creating zones and zones packages to linking them to
merchandising departments, is completed in the Zones Configuration feature.
When deciding how many zones locations require, keep a few items in mind:
Zones and departments might be configured with a one-to-one ratio.
A single zone can contain multiple departments. This allows for the management of a larger
employee base than just a single department per zone.
Zones are the lowest or most granular unit used in Dayforce for planning, forecasting, and
scheduling.
The general process flow for configuring zones in Dayforce consists of the following:
Create Zones
Create Zone Packages
Create Merchandising Departments
Link Merchandising Departments to Zones
Create Zones
To create zones:
1. Go to Org Setup > Zones Configuration and click the Zones tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description of the zone.
4. In the Organization field, specify where the zone can be assigned in your organization by
selecting the checkbox next to the appropriate locations in the organizational tree.
5. In the Efficiency Score Method drop-down list, select the option you want to use for
calculating the zone’s efficiency score. A zone's efficiency score is a percentage score that
reflects how close its schedule matches the labor demand. A zone’s efficiency score is a
percentage score that reflects how close its schedule matches the labor demand. You can
select one of the following options:
DayOnly: Dayforce compares the number of employees scheduled to the labor
demanded for the day.
QuarterHourOnly: Dayforce compares the number of employees scheduled to the
labor demand at each quarter hour. Any time the zone is understaffed or overstaffed
is subtracted from this score.
BothServiceInsideHOO: Dayforce uses both quarter hour and daily coverage scores
inside the location's hours of operation. However, outside the hours of operation,

-- 423 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 424 of 0
Dayforce uses the daily efficiency score.
BothServiceOutsideHOO: Dayforce uses both quarter hour and daily coverage
scores. The quarter hour method is used for service activities and the daily method for
non-service activities.
6. In the Scheduling Method drop-down list, select how the Dayforce autofill feature creates
schedules for the zone:
Deployment Template: Dayforce follows a template that breaks up the zone's daily
labor demand into multiple curves, one for each different activity specified.
Manual or None: Dayforce doesn't autofill the zone’s schedule. If autofill is run for the
location, Dayforce leaves the schedules of any zones configured with this option
blank so that a manager can create the schedule for the zone manually.
Note: Autofill doesn’t distinguish between selecting Manual or None. In both cases, it
skips the zone and doesn’t schedule shifts to it.
Optimization: Dayforce doesn't consider activities when creating a schedule. It
considers one labor demand curve and attempts to fill the schedule so that the
demand is met at every point in the curve.
7. In the Priority Order field, enter the relative order in which the zone is staffed when autofill
runs.
8. In the Max Staffing Level field, enter the maximum demand level, in number of employees,
the zone can reach at any time. When Dayforce distributes labor to the zone, it never
exceeds this level at any time. For example, if there are five cash registers, set the value for
the zone to 5, because the demand for cashiers shouldn't exceed the number of available
registers.
9. In the Sort Index field, enter a number that represents the sort order of this zone relative to
other zones. This number is used to sort zones on schedules. For example, to configure a
zone so that it is always shown first when schedules are sorted in ascending order by zone,
enter 1. Zones without a Sort Index are shown last when sorted in ascending order, and first
in descending order.
10. Note: If none of the zones are assigned a Sort Index, Dayforce doesn’t sort schedules by
zone. Instead, it either sorts by the next sort option (for example, if zone was the primary
sort option, it would sort by the secondary one instead), or sorts by employee name in
cases where zone was the tertiary sort option.
10. (Optional) Enter a cross-reference code in the Reference Code field. This code must be
unique and must not contain special characters.
11. Click Save.
Repeat these steps to create the different zones in your locations. You assign them to locations
using zone packages, which are created after you configure all of your zones. See Create Zone
Packages.
Create Zone Packages

-- 424 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 425 of 0
Zone packages are a collection of departments and zones that are used to quickly assign zones
and departments to new locations that you create in Dayforce.
A zone package can be company wide, specific to a region, a district, or a single location.
Dayforce applies default zone packages in such a manner that it takes the “closest” zone
package on the organizational hierarchy. As Dayforce starts at the location and browses up the
organizational hierarchy, the first zone package it “finds” is assigned to the location.
For example, if you assign the “All Zones” package to the top of the hierarchy, but the “Specialty”
zone package to the “Eastern” district of the organizational hierarchy, all of the locations in the
“Eastern” district are assigned the “Specialty” zone package by default. The rest of the locations
receive the “All Zones” package by default.
Note: You can assign any zone package to any new location when you define locations. Where
zone packages are assigned in your organizational hierarchy only impacts which package
Dayforce assigns to a new location by default.
Zone packages link departments to zones in the locations they are assigned to. For example, in a
grocery chain, most of the locations have a butcher department, but smaller stores only sell
prepackaged and sliced meat without a butcher on site, and as a result don’t employ butchers.
In both cases, stores are configured with a “Deli” zone, but the smaller stores don’t have a
butcher department linked to their Deli zone.
You create as many zone packages as needed in Org Setup > Zones Configuration. The more
locations with different combinations of zones and departments there are in your organization, the
more zone packages you need to create.
To create zone packages:
1. Go to Org Setup > Zones Configuration and click the Zone Packages tab.
2. Click Add.
3. In the General section, enter a name and, optionally, a description for the zone package.
4. In the Organization field, select the areas of your organization that are assigned the zone
package.
5. For the first zone package you create, select the Is Master checkbox.
6. Note: You should configure only one zone package with the Is Master checkbox selected.
6. (Optional) Enter a cross-reference code in the Reference Code field. This code must be
unique and must not contain special characters.
7. In the Zone Department Configuration section, Dayforce shows a list of departments. For
each department you want to include in the zone package, select which zone it belongs to
in the Zone drop-down list.
Note: For the Is Master zone package, you should include every department.

-- 425 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 426 of 0
8. (Optional) Select the Hide Unassigned Departments checkbox to hide departments that
aren’t assigned a zone in the Zone column.
9. Click Save.
Create Merchandising Departments
In Dayforce, merchandising departments are used to track sales by assigning products to the
appropriate department. Products in stores are often organized by departments. For example, an
electronics store might have a computer department and a home theater department. When
customer service puts through the sale of a television, the sale is linked in the Point-of-Sales (POS)
system with the home theater department. Merchandising departments are used in Dayforce to
link this POS data with the corresponding zone. As Dayforce uses zones for labor planning and
scheduling, it’s important to link the two so that accurate data can be used for labor planning.
Note: Although a retail company’s use of merchandising departments is a common example,
departments can be configured for organizations in other industries to track drivers for the labor
budget as well. For example, the number of transactions in a bank branch, tied to different areas
of the branch, can be used to set up merchandising departments which track the transactions
and link them to appropriate zones in the bank.
You create as many merchandising departments as you need in Org Setup > Zones Configuration.
The higher the number of departments locations track their sales against, the more merchandising
departments you'll need to set up.
To define a merchandising department:
1. Go to Org Setup > Zones Configuration and click the MDSE Departments tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description of the merchandising department.
4. Enter a reference code in the Reference Code field. This code must be unique and must not
contain special characters.
5. Important: If you are linking the merchandising department in Dayforce with a department
tracked by your POS system, this needs to be the same code the POS system uses to mark
sales from the department. That way, sales data is correctly attributed to the merchandising
department in Dayforce.
5. Click Save.
Next, you need to link it to a zone in the Zone MDSE Department tab.
Link Merchandising Departments to Zones
After you've created the merchandising departments your organization uses to track its location's
performance (commonly sales), you need to link the merchandising departments to the
appropriate zones. Typically, this is the zone that earns the merchandising department's sales. For

-- 426 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 427 of 0
example, say you've defined several merchandising departments that divide music sales by
genre:
Rock - CD
Rap HipHop - CD
Country, Blues - CD
International - CD
Alternative - CD
These merchandising departments correspond to codes in the store's POS system.
Because stores plan their labor and schedule employees based, in part, on their CD sales in
general and not on the sale of one particular genre, all of these merchandising departments are
linked to one zone. This way, the sales data from any CD sale drives the labor budget for the
CD zone, which in turn gives managers more labor hours to spend in the CD zone when creating
schedules.
You can create as many merchandising departments to zone links as you need in Org Setup,
although typically you wouldn’t link one merchandising department to more than one zone. This
would result in the sales from that department being counted twice by Dayforce. Any number of
merchandising departments can link to a single zone, though.
Additionally, the same zone in different zone packages can be linked to different merchandising
departments. The links are specific to each zone package. Continuing the example above, in the
East Region zone package, the CD zone contains all of the CD merchandising departments.
However, in the Central Region zone package, the International - CD merchandising department
isn’t linked to the CD zone because stores in that region don’t carry any products from the
International - CD merchandising department.
To link merchandising departments to zones:
1. Go to Org Setup > Zones Configuration and click the Zone MDSE Department tab.
2. In the left side panel, select the zone package and zone you want to link to a merchandising
department.
3. The application shows zone packages and zones hierarchically. The top-level items in the
list are zone packages. Click a zone package to expand the list, and Dayforce shows the
zones linked to the zone package.
3. Select the Include checkboxes next to the merchandising departments that you want to link
to the selected zone.
4. Click Save.
Configure Locations
To create a location:

1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and click the Organization tab.
2. In the Manage Locations drop-down list, click Add Locations to open the wizard.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description for the new location.
4. Enter the effective from date to specify when the location becomes a part of your
organization; locations can be added to your organization before they’re open.
5. Enter the opening date to specify when the location opens.
6. In the Ledger Code field, enter the code you want to represent the location in payroll
records. This code is used when Dayforce exports the payroll information; Dayforce tracks
the hours worked in each location and it represents where the labor cost of your

7. In the Parent Location field, specify the org unit the location belongs to.
8. Click Next.

package’s template.

define for new locations, as described below.
Finalize Location Configurations
To finalize location configurations:
1. Select the location in the organization hierarchy.
2. Click the Opening Date calendar icon and select the date the new location opens. By
default, Dayforce uses today’s date.
3. (Optional) Select when the location closes using the Closing Date calendar. By default, this
field is blank and the location will stay open until you edit the location and specify a closing
date.
4. Note: When you add locations to the organizational tree in Dayforce, it’s important to select
an appropriate opening and closing date, because Dayforce treats open locations
differently from closed locations.
4. (Optional) Enter a cross-reference code in the Reference Code field.
5. Cross-reference codes are used to export data from Dayforce to other applications. See
Cross-Reference Codes.
5. Enter the code you want to represent the location on Dayforce clocks in the Clock Code
field.
6. Depending on your Dayforce configuration, the hardware clocks upon which employees
clock in and out for work can be used to record location transfers. Location transfers are
required when an employee spends time working outside of their primary location. The

-- 428 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 429 of 0
clock code is the number an employee types on the clock’s number pad when transferring
to that location.
6. Select what time zone the location is in from the Time Zone drop-down list. Dayforce might
use this information in Work > Time Clock (if available) to calculate the time employees are
clocking in or out, instead of relying on the time and time zone of their local machine.
7. Select which weekday is considered the start of the week, if it’s different for this location
than your organization’s default, in the Start Day of Week drop-down list.
If a value is specified, when users view information for the location, such as its timesheet or
schedule, Dayforce shows the week starting on the selected day. If blank, Dayforce uses
the default week start day for the location.
Note: When the Start Day of Week setting hasn't been specified in the org setup for a user’s
primary location, Dayforce uses the configuration specified in the First Day of Week setting
in Site Setup > Client.
8. Click Save.
Dayforce can track additional information as you add locations to your organizational tree in Org
Setup. With a location selected, you can:
Enter the location’s address: Click the Address tab and specify the location’s address in the
provided fields.
Note: These fields should be set for organizational units at the On-Site Department level if
minimum wage rates have been defined for the organization. See Minimum Wage

Enter the location’s contact information: Click the Contact tab and specify the location’s
contact information in the provided fields.
Dayforce also provides a history of changes made to the location (click the History tab to
view) and a chart of where the org unit sits in your organizational hierarchy (click the Chart tab to
view).
It also shows a summary of the employees assigned to work in and manage the location. Click the
Authority tab to review a list of employees assigned to manage the location. A location’s manager
is responsible for approving or denying any requests, such as time away from work requests,
made by employees working at that location. The list of employees assigned to work at a location
is shown when you click the Employee tab.

Edit Locations and Org Units
This section describes how to move or close locations or org units, such as regions or districts, in
your organizational hierarchy. You can move and close locations and org units that were
previously configured, as outlined below:
Move Locations and Org Units
Close Locations and Org Units
Close Location Validation
When you enter a date in the Effective To field in the Open and Close Location dialog box,
Dayforce uses validation which prevents you from end dating the organization when any of the
following situations apply:
The organization has open employee work assignments where the effective to date occurs
after the organization's effective to date.
The child organizations have open employee work assignments where the effective to date
occurs after the organization's effective to date.
Some organizations are scheduled to become children of the selected organization at a
future date (effective from is in the future). These organizations have open employee work
assignments with an effective to date that occurs after the selected organization's effective
to date.
In the validation error message, Dayforce shows the name of the org and its navigational path in
the org tree so that you can identify the org unit that’s causing the validation error. In addition to
the validation message, Dayforce shows an export button so that you can export the list of
validation messages.

-- 431 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 432 of 0
Move Locations and Org Units
To move locations or org units:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and select the relevant location in the organizational
hierarchy.
2. In the Manage Locations drop-down list, click Move Location.
3. Dayforce opens the Move Location dialog box.
3. Click the org icon to select a parent location.
4. Dayforce opens the dialog box for you to search for and select an organization.
4. Specify the effective from date.
5. Click Save.
Close Locations and Org Units
To close locations or org units:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and select the relevant location in the organizational
hierarchy.
2. In the Manage Locations drop-down list, click Open and Close Location.
3. Dayforce opens the Open and Close Location dialog box.
3. Specify the following dates, as necessary:
Opening Date
Closing Date
Effective To
4. Locations that are closed aren’t open for business, but Dayforce stores active records for
them. You can assign employees to closed locations in People, but they aren’t included in
the Dayforce planning and forecasting features.
5. Locations that have been end dated aren’t open for business, and Dayforce doesn’t store
active records for them. Employees can’t be assigned to them, and they aren’t shown in the
organizational hierarchy.
6. Both closed and end-dated org units (where these dates are in the past) aren’t shown in the
hierarchy when the Active/All switch is set to Active. They are both shown when the switch is
set to All.
4. Click Save.
Create Dockets
Dayforce uses dockets to track logged time against a quantity of produced work. Typically, this
quantity represents a number of “pieces” made in the docket, like the number of windshields
installed in a car assembly line. This information is helpful for paying employees bonuses or
premiums for their production. Dayforce can be configured to pay employees extra based on their
output. It multiplies the docket’s piece rate by the number of pieces an employee produced

-- 432 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 433 of 0
during their shift. Before employees can enter their time against a particular docket or work order,
you need to create the docket in Org Setup > Docket.
You can also configure and import dockets in Org Setup using CSV (comma-separated
values) files. The information can be quickly created or updated, using the Import and Export
functions. See Org Setup Import and Export Configuration.
Important:
The Ledger Code field in this task (see step 6) can be used only if Dayforce is configured to
use the Payroll features. When running as a standalone Workforce Management application,
Dayforce doesn’t use this field.
Dayforce supports only whole numbers in fields where employees specify their quantity of
completed docket pieces.
To create a docket:
1. Go to Org Setup > Docket and click Add.
2. Enter the name and, optionally, a description of the new docket.
3. In the Organization field, select which levels or locations the docket applies to.
4. In the Piece Rate field, enter the amount (in dollars) that employees are paid, over and
above their hourly rate, for completing each piece of work in the docket. You can specify a
decimal amount in this field to represent cents.
5. In the Clock Code field, enter a code to represent the docket on Dayforce clocks.
6. The hardware clocks which employees clock in and out on can be used to enter docket
transfers, which occur when an employee spends time working outside of their primary or
normal docket. The clock code is the number that an employee enters on the clock's
number pad when transferring to that docket.
6. In the Ledger Code field, enter the ledger account associated with this job so that Dayforce
associates the pay amounts for each job with the appropriate general ledger account. This
information can be exported with the Payroll GL Export background job.
7. (Optional) Enter a cross-reference code in the Reference Code field. This code must be
unique and must not contain special characters.
8. Click Save.
Define Comparable Locations
This section describes how to define comparable locations for some locations, typically newly
opened ones, to be used with forecasting; when configured, Dayforce uses actual historical data
from a location’s comparable location for a specified period of time when forecasting. Comparable
locations are configured in Org Setup > Organization.
Typically, comparable locations are used in forecasting for the times when locations don’t have
enough historical data to generate a forecast. A common example occurs when an organization

-- 433 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 434 of 0
opens a new location; this new location wouldn’t have enough historical data to base a forecast off
of, often for longer than the location’s first year.
The amount of historical data Dayforce needs at a location to generate a forecast depends on
how Dayforce forecasting is configured. For example, a forecast that uses a trend of historical
average where the past 8 weeks are compared to the same 8 weeks from last year needs 14
months' worth of historical data to properly generate a forecast.
In this example, the location needs to use historical data from its comparable location for the first
14 months it’s open; after that, Dayforce can examine the location’s own historical data to generate
the forecast.
Comparable locations can be specified for the overall location and for each zone within a location;
Dayforce can be configured so that different comparable location can be specified for each.
To configure comparable locations:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and select a location.
2. Click the Comparable Site tab.
3. Click Add.
4. Select the comparable location in the Location drop-down list.
5. Select options in the Source Zone and Target Zone drop-down lists.
6. Typically, each zone from one location is compared to the same zone in the comparable
location, but this isn’t required.
6. Enter a number that represents the expected deviation, in percentage, from the comparable
location's historical data in the Deviation (%) field.
7. With a value specified, Dayforce adjusts the comparable location's data values up or down
by the specified percentage; specify a positive or negative percentage value in the
Deviation (%) field and Dayforce adjusts the values accordingly.
8. For example, when configuring a comparable location that performed an estimated 15%
better than the new location, specify -15 in the Deviation (%) field and Dayforce reduces
the historical data from the comparable location by 15% before generating a forecast from
it.
7. Enter the effective date range of historical data that Dayforce uses in place of any historical
data that Dayforce has for the location, when generating forecasts. This date range doesn’t
define the forecasted dates during which Dayforce uses the comparable location’s historical
data; it defines the dates of the historical data that Dayforce uses.
8. For example, a new location opens June 1, 2011. When Dayforce generates a forecast for
this location in Plan, it examines the last eight weeks and compares it to the same eight
weeks from the previous year. Because the new location doesn’t have any actual results to
make this comparison, it uses a comparable location’s historical data. The time period of the
historical data it uses from the comparable location runs from April 6, 2010 to June 1, 2011.
9. On June 1, 2011, to generate a forecast, Dayforce needs historical data from the previous
eight weeks of last year; this dictates the April 6, 2010 start date. Because the location

-- 434 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 435 of 0
starts recording results starting June 1, 2011, any forecast that requires historical data from
June 1, 2011 or later can use the location’s actual historical data. As a result, the end date is
set to June 1, 2011.
8. Click Save.
Configure Temporary Site Closures
You can define periods where a site in your organization is temporarily closed in the Closures
subtab of the Organization tab in Org Setup > Organization. For example, if your organization is
temporarily closing a site to renovate, you can define the duration of the closure and Dayforce
marks the site as closed during those dates in some features.
Before You Begin: This functionality is available only for site-level org units. Further, the Closures
subtab is available only for users assigned access to the Location Property Values or Location
Type Values role features under Org Setup > Org Setup > Organization > Organization in the
Features tab of System Admin > Roles.
To configure a temporary site closure:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization.
2. Click the Organization tab. Dayforce shows your organizational hierarchy.
3. Expand the hierarchy and click a site name. Dayforce shows the site details in a slide-out
panel.
4. Click the Closures subtab.
5. Click Add.
6. Enter a name and description for the temporary closure.
7. Enter the effective date range for the closure.
8. If you’re configuring an open-ended closure, you don’t need to enter an end date.
8. Enter a reference code. This code must be unique and must not contain special characters.
9. (Optional) Repeat steps through 8 to add another temporary closure for the site.
10. Click Save.
Configure Compliance Properties for Sites
Before You Begin: The Compliance Properties tab is shown only for sites and is applicable only for

Configure Location Properties
Dayforce retains information or attributes about your organization’s locations for use in task
management and labor deployment. This information can be used by management to compare
locations. For example, in the Task Management and Task Setup > Task Templates features, you
can cater the budget of ad hoc tasks and task templates to suit the properties of your locations,
such as square footage. To do this, you’d create a “Size in Square Feet” location property.
After you configure the different attributes you want to track in Dayforce, you need to provide
values for each location, the process for which is also described below.
You can add as many location properties in Org Setup as your organization tracks.
To configure a location property:
1. Go to Org Setup > Locations and click the Location Properties tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and description for the location property.
4. In the Default Value field, enter the value Dayforce uses for the property, by default.
5. (Optional) Enter a reference code for the location property in the Reference Code field. This
code must be unique and must not contain special characters.
6. Click Save.
Configure Location Daily Properties
Location daily properties are similar to location properties in that they are measurable properties
of locations within an organization that can be created for specific locations and used with task
management and labor planning. They are helpful in situations where activity demand times vary
from location to location.
For example, location managers can use location daily properties in certain labor deployment
rules to allow the rule's start and end times to reference the location daily property. Managers
have access to all of the location daily properties for their locations and have the ability to change
the default values or create exceptions.
You can configure as many location daily properties in Org Setup as your organization tracks.
To configure a location daily property:
1. Go to Org Setup > Locations and click the Location Daily Properties tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description for the location daily property.
4. In the Data Type drop-down list, select a data type for the property:

-- 436 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 437 of 0
Time Range: Select this option to configure the property with a time range value. This
allows you to use the location daily property when configuring several labor
deployment rules in Plan Setup > Labor Deployment. See Labor Deployment
Rules.This also allows you to specify fixed or offset times when you add values to the
location daily property.
Numeric: Select this option to configure the property with a numerical value. If you are
tracking a productivity value for use with performance-based scheduling, you must
select a numeric value.
5. Select the Secured checkbox to restrict editing and access of this location daily property to
one store in the Location Daily Properties tab of Schedules.
6. Click Save.

Configure Time Range Location Daily Property Values
To configure a time range location daily property value:
1. Go to Org Setup > Locations.
2. Click the Location Daily Property Values tab and then click Add.
3. In the Organization drop-down list, select the organization you want to add location daily
property values for.
4. In the Location Daily Property drop-down list, select the location daily property you want to

Fixed Time/Offset: Specify whether this property will use fixed times, offset times, or
whether to disable it by choosing one of the following options from this drop-down list:
Fixed: Select this option to use a fixed start or end time for this property.

-- 438 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 439 of 0
Offset: Select this option to use an offset start or end time for this property.
Offset times allow you to start an activity relative to a store's opening hours. For
example, in a large store, the baking activity might start three hours before the
store opens to customers. In a small store, the baking activity might start two
hours before the store opens to customers. Offsets allow you to configure your
location daily properties to meet these demands.
Disabled: Select this option to disable the start or end time of the property for
this day.
Start Time/End Time: If you selected Fixed in the Fixed Time/Offset drop-down list,
enter the time the property starts in the Start Time field and, optionally, enter the time
the property ends in the End Time field.
Offset (minutes): If you selected Offset in the Fixed Time/Offset drop-down list, enter
the number of minutes to offset the property here. For example, enter 30 to have the
property start or end 30 minutes before or after opening or closing.
Before/After: If you selected Offset in the Fixed Time/Offset drop-down list, select
Before or After depending on whether the offset will be before or after the value in the
Start Basis column.
Start Basis: If you selected Offset in the Fixed Time/Offset drop-down list, select Close
or Open.
8. Click Save.

Configure Location Types
This topic describes the optional configuration of location types for sites in the organizational
hierarchy. A location type can represent any physical area in a location, such as different stations
in an assembly line, desks, booths, or ticket windows. After configuration, managers can schedule
employees to work in physical locations in their location by assigning a location type to their shifts.
For example, employees working on assembly lines need to be scheduled to specific stations on
their line. Although Dayforce tracks the different lines with existing functionality, each assembly
line is configured as a zone, each with its own labor demand. This functionality allows
organizations to specify more granular information, such that the body assembly line has eight
different stations.
To configure location types:
1. Go to Org Setup > Locations and click the Location Types tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and description of the location type.
4. The location type’s name is shown in Schedules when users schedule employees to that
location.
4. (Optional) In the Reference Code field, enter a cross-reference code. This code must be
unique and must not contain special characters.
5. Click Save.
After you configure location types, you must assign them to locations in Org Setup > Organization,
in the Location subtab.
To assign location types:
1. Go to Org Setup > Organization and click the Organization tab.
2. Select the relevant location. A slide-out panel opens.
3. Note: You can assign location types only to locations with Site selected in the Level drop-
down list in the General subtab of the Organization tab in Org Setup > Organization.
3. Click the Location subtab.
4. In the Location Type drop-down list, select the location types you want to assign to the
location.
5. Click Save.
When assigned, the location type drop-down list appears in Schedules when you add or edit
shifts. The location of this drop-down list varies, depending on which view you use in Schedules:
Bar View: Shift details slide-out panel.

Position Certification Rule and Position Skill Rule.

Configure Pay Approval Structure
The way in which managers select pay details to review, lock, and approve in Pay Approve
Checklist and Pay Admin Checklist can be based on organizational units, managers, or a mix of
both (where some employees are grouped and approved by the location where they work and
others are grouped based on their manager). Dayforce can be configured so that approvals are
performed per organizational unit, such as a location manager approving pay for all of the

-- 446 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 447 of 0
employees in the location they manage, but also per manager for some locations, such as head
office, where the pay in head office isn’t approved at once, by one user. Rather, the employees
are split between their different managers so that, for example, the VP of marketing approves pay
for all of their employees and the VP of accounting approves pay for theirs.
This section describes how to complete this configuration.
Configuring how employees are grouped (by their location or their manager) for pay approval
involves selecting or clearing the Approve By Manager checkbox in the General tab for a selected
site in the Organization tab in Org Setup > Organization.
When the Approve By Manager checkbox is selected for a site, Dayforce groups employees in the
same pay group working for the same manager, and pay for each manager’s employees is
approved at once.
When the checkbox is cleared, Dayforce groups employees in the same pay group working at
that location, and pay for the entire location is approved at once.
Dayforce distinguishes how the pay approval is structured in both checklists:
In the preceding screenshot, two approvals are shown in Pay Approve Checklist: one, for the
Cloverleaf location, is grouped by location, and the other, for Ted, is grouped by manager.
Approving pay for Cloverleaf approves all of the employees working at that location that belong to
the Default Pay Group. Approving pay for Ted approves all of the employees working at the
Cranberry location who have Ted as their manager.
Similarly, for Pay Admin Checklist, Dayforce shows one record per pay group for organizational
units grouped by location. For locations with Approve By Manager selected, Dayforce shows one
record for each manager with employees in that location, per pay group.

Jobs and Job Assignments Configuration
In Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments, you can add or import the jobs and job assignments
that can be worked in your organization so that employees can be staffed appropriately.
This feature contains the Jobs and Job Assignments tab, where most configuration takes place,
and several other tabs for creating additional values that can be associated with jobs and job
assignments.
See also:
Jobs and Job Assignments Background

Create Jobs
Create Job Assignments

Jobs and Job Assignments Background
In Dayforce, jobs, job assignments, and departments are key values that are defined as follows:
Job: A general set of duties that employees are eligible to perform such as Analyst, Director,
Coordinator, and Manager.
Job Assignment: A specific instance of a job that is tied to a department.
Department: A generic area that can exist across your organization, like Finance, Marketing,
Sales, and HR. See Departments Overview.
Jobs, job assignments, and departments form a hierarchy where a job is a template for a set of
job assignments under it that are each tied to a department.
For example, the Clerk job can contain the Meat Clerk, Produce Clerk, and Seafood Clerk job
assignments, which are assigned to the Meat, Produce, and Seafood departments. This hierarchy
is represented in the left sidebar in the Jobs and Job Assignments tab:

-- 451 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 452 of 0
Departments Overview
In Dayforce, there is a distinction between departments and the on-site department level org units
that are part of an organizational hierarchy.
Department: A department represents the area that needs a job to be done. A department
can represent a function (Finance, Sales), an area of responsibility (Production Line), or
even a virtual area (Union Duties).
On-Site Department: An on-site department is made up of a site and a department that are
configured in Dayforce. For example, New York (site) + Packaging (department) = New
York Packaging (on-site department).
Departments are configured in the Departments tab in Org Setup > Organization, and on-site
departments are configured in the Organization tab of Org Setup > Organization.
Job assignments and org units can both be assigned a department. A department creates a link
between job assignments and the org units where a job assignment can be worked. A job
assignment can only be worked in org units that have the same department assigned.
For job assignments, the department is assigned in the Department drop-down list of the
Assignments section in the Jobs and Job Assignments tab in Org Setup > Jobs and Job
Assignments. In this example, the Produce Clerk job assignment is assigned to the Produce
department:
For org units, the department is assigned in the Department drop-down list of the General tab in
the Organization tab of Org Setup > Organization. In this example, the Produce department is
assigned to the Store 320 - Produce org unit:

-- 452 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 453 of 0
Continuing this example, the Produce Clerk job assignment can be worked at the Store 320 -
Produce org unit because both the job assignment and the org unit are assigned the Produce
department. The job assignment can also be worked at other org units that have the Produce
department selected.
Job Assignments in Work Assignments Overview
Work assignments are a combination of the job assignment and the org unit where an employee
works. They are used in various areas of Dayforce such as scheduling and payroll.
After you configure jobs and job assignments, you can use work assignments to assign job
assignments to employees. You can add a work assignment to an employee's profile through the
following methods:
A form (such as the New Hire form)
Directly in the Work > Work Assignments screen of People
By importing

Management by Job Assignment Overview
As an optional feature, you can configure management by job assignment to define an
employee's manager based on their primary job assignment, such as an employee working a
Sales Associate job assignment that is managed by an employee working the Sales Manager job
assignment.
Job assignment management is configured in the Headcount Allocations subsection of the
Assignments section of a job assignment's details in the Jobs and Job Assignments tab of Org
Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments. When you create a headcount allocation record in this
section, you need to select a job assignment in the Managing Job Assignments drop-down list.
Job assignment management needs to be configured for individual locations. To define job
assignment hierarchy for a job assignment that is associated with multiple locations, you must
configure a separate headcount allocation record for each location. Also, the work assignment of
the manager and employee being managed must be at the same org unit.
Management by job assignment is optional, and the configuration can be used in addition to the
other management hierarchy configurations. When multiple configurations are used, Dayforce
sets the following order of precedence to determine employee management:
1. Direct management
2. Job assignment management
3. Derived by org
Note: You can run the Employee Manager Recalc background job to keep management
assignments by job assignment up to date. In the Org Units setting of the background job's
parameters, you must select the specific location of the headcount allocation record.
Example
In the Headcount Allocations section of the Sales Associate job assignment, you create a
headcount allocation for the Toronto site. For this record, you select Sales Manager in the

-- 454 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 455 of 0
Managing Job Assignments drop-down list.
Stacey Jacobs works the Sales Manager job assignment at the Toronto - Sales onsite department
of the Toronto site. Also at the Toronto - Sales department of this site, Michael Collins works the
Sales Associate job assignment. As such, Stacy is automatically Michael's manager based on her
job assignment.
In the Managers section of the Work > Management Assignments screen of Michael's profile in
People, Stacy is shown as his manager. Also, the Derivation Method column of the record shows
Job Assignment and is read-only:
See Work > Management Assignments in the HR Administration Guide.
Jobs and Job Assignments Configuration Overview
Before you configure jobs and job assignments, you need to complete the following prerequisites:
Create the org units in your organizational hierarchy where employees can work. This is
done in the Organization tab in Org Setup > Organization. See Configure Organizational
Groups and Subgroups.
Create the generic departments that can be worked across your organization. See
Configure Departments.
In Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments, configuration involves the following process:
Creating values that can be associated with jobs and job assignments, such as job families
and job functions. Configuring these values is optional but can be useful for reporting and
tracking. While it is a best practice to create these values before you start creating jobs and
job assignments, you can still configure them afterward as needed. See Initial Configuration
for Jobs and Job Assignments.
Adding or importing jobs and job assignments in the Jobs and Job Assignments tab. For
more information, see the following:
Jobs and Job Assignments Tab Overview
Create Jobs
Create Job Assignments
Org Setup Import and Export Configuration
Configuring pay grades that can be assigned to jobs. See Pay Grade Configuration.

-- 455 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 456 of 0
Creating workers comp codes and defining which jobs they are associated with. See
Workers Comp Setup.
Initial Configuration for Jobs and Job Assignments
Initial configuration in Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments involves creating job families, job
functions, position terms, and employment indicators.
Create Job Families
In the Job Families tab of Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments, you can create values that are
used to group a set of similar jobs in the Jobs and Job Assignments tab and for reporting
purposes. For example, you can create the Retail job family for the Clerk, Receiving, and Cashier
jobs. Creating job families is optional but useful for managing a large number of jobs.
To add a job family:
1. Go to Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments and click the Job Families tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description.
4. Enter a value in the Reference Code field. Reference codes are used to export data to other
applications. These codes must be unique and must not contain special characters.
5. Click Save.
Create Job Functions
In the Job Functions tab of Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments, you can create values that
are used to broadly describe the purpose of a job, such as Administrative or Customer Service.
Creating job functions is useful for tracking and reporting on jobs.
Note: Configuring one or more job functions is required if your organization uses, or plans to use,
the eQuest external job board integration for Recruiting.
To create a job function:
1. Go to Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments and click the Job Functions tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description in the corresponding fields.
4. Enter a value in the Reference Code field. Reference codes are used to export data to other
applications. These codes must be unique and must not contain special characters.
5. Click Save.
Create Position Terms

-- 456 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 457 of 0
In the Position Term tab of Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments, you can create values that
are used to track the intended duration of a position such as Episodic or Fixed. Dayforce comes
with the system Regular position term and you can create additional ones as needed. Creating
position terms is optional but useful for tracking and reporting on positions.
You can also import position terms instead of manually adding them. See Org Setup Import and
Export Configuration.
To create a position term:
1. Go to Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments and click the Position Term tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description in the corresponding fields.
4. Enter a value in the Reference Code field. Reference codes are used to export data to other
applications. These codes must be unique and must not contain special characters.
5. Click Save.
Create Employment Indicators
In the Employment Indicator tab of Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments, you can create
values that are used to categorize employees into different groups that track the type of work
associated with a job assignment. For example, the job assignment could be an apprenticeship or
internship depending on how your organization structures it.
Dayforce comes with the system Seasonal employment indicator and you can create additional
ones as needed. Creating employment indicators is optional but useful for tracking and reporting
on job assignments.
You can also import employment indicators instead of manually adding them. See Org Setup
Import and Export Configuration.
To create an employment indicator:
1. Go to Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments and click the Employment Indicator tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a name and, optionally, a description.
4. Enter a value in the Reference Code field. Reference codes are used to export data to other
applications. These codes must be unique and must not contain special characters.
5. In the Country drop-down list, select one or more countries that the employment indicator is
available for. If you leave this drop-down list cleared, the employment indicator is available
regardless of country. See Configure Countries for Employment Indicators.
6. Click Save.
Configure Countries for Employment Indicators

-- 457 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 458 of 0
You can configure employment indicators to be available based on the country that employees
operate in. This is configured by selecting one or more countries in the Country column of the
Employment Indicator tab in Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments. This column is cleared by
default. If you leave this column cleared, the employment indicator is available regardless of
country.
This functionality is enforced in the following areas:
In the job assignment details of the Jobs and Job Assignments tab in Org Setup > Jobs and
Job Assignments. If an option is selected in the Pay Group drop-down list of the job
assignment details, the Employment Indicator drop-down list shows employment indicators
that are assigned the same country as the selected pay group and employment indicators
that don’t have a country assigned. Employment indicators that are assigned a country that
doesn’t match the employee’s assigned pay group aren’t shown.
In the following areas where employee details can be updated:
The Work > Work Assignments screen in People.
Self-service forms, including the Job Assignment and Compensation Change and Job
Assignment Change forms.
The Edit wizard opened from the People List screen of People.
In each area, the Employment Indicator drop-down list shows employment indicators that
are assigned the same country as the employee's assigned pay group and employment
indicators that don’t have a country assigned. Employment indicators that are assigned a
country that doesn’t match the employee’s assigned pay group aren’t shown.
Note: Country assignment for employment indicators isn’t enforced in the HR Import or HR Data
Config import.
If a job assignment or employee isn’t assigned a pay group, the Employment Indicator drop-down
list in each area shows only employment indicators that don’t have countries configured.
Also, Dayforce shows a validation error message if you change the pay group assigned to the job
assignment or employee to one where the employment indicator that has already been selected
isn’t configured.
Jobs and Job Assignments Tab Overview
In the Jobs and Job Assignments tab of Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments, you can add or
import jobs and job assignments. The left sidebar shows a tree of job families, jobs, job
assignments, and departments. When you select a job or job assignment, Dayforce shows its
details in the remainder of the screen:

-- 458 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 459 of 0
At the highest level of the tree are job families, which you can create in the Job Families tab of Org
Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments. Dayforce shows the number of jobs that each job family
contains next to each job family name. Jobs that don’t have a job family assigned are listed under
the system No Job Family entry.
You can click a job family to view its jobs. Each job shows the number of job assignments that it
contains. When you click a job, each of its job assignments are shown along with their associated
departments:
Items in each level of the tree are listed alphabetically.
In the search field at the top of the sidebar, you can enter all or part of a job or job assignment
name and press Enter to filter the list. The search returns results for job families, jobs, job
assignments, and the department assigned to job assignments.

-- 459 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 460 of 0
If a search result is returned for a job assignment or department, the job and job family above it
are also shown, even if they don’t match your search results. This is because job assignments are
never shown without their parent job and job family (or the No Job Family entry if a job isn’t
assigned to a job family).
In this example, if you search "deli," the job and job family of the Deli Clerk job assignment are
also shown, even though they don’t contain the word "deli":
Conversely, if your search matches a job but not any job assignments under it, only the jobs are
shown.
Other notes:
Only active jobs and job assignments are shown in the sidebar by default, but you can click
All at the top of the list to include end-dated or future-dated ones as well.
You can click the collapse icon ( ) at the top-right of the sidebar to hide it from the screen.
At the top of the details for a selected job or job assignment, Dayforce shows information
about when the record was created and last modified and by whom.

You can create jobs in the Jobs and Job Assignments tab of Org Setup > Jobs and Job
Assignments.
You can also import jobs instead of manually adding them. See Org Setup Import and Export
Configuration.
To create a job:
1. Go to Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments and click the Jobs and Job Assignments
tab.
2. In the left sidebar, select the job family that you want to add the job to and click Add > Add
Job. If you don’t have job families configured, the job is added under the No Job Family
entry.

Job settings
Setting 	Description
General
Name 	The job name.
Reference Code
The cross-reference code for the job. Reference codes are used to
export data to other applications. These codes must be unique and
must not contain special characters.
Effective From
The date that the job is available in Dayforce. This field can’t be edited
after you save the job. Job assignments added under this job must
have effective dates on or after this date.
Effective To
The date that the job is no longer available in Dayforce. The Effective
To field of a job is only enabled if there are no job assignments under a
job or all of the job assignments are already end-dated. In these
cases, the Effective To field is read-only. You can't add job
assignments to a job that has an end date.
Ledger Code
The ledger code for the job. This functionality is applicable only for
organizations that use the Payroll module. Dayforce can associate the
pay amounts for each job with the appropriate general ledger account
and this information can be exported with the Payroll GL Export
background job.

Clock Code
The numerical code that represents the job assignment on clocks. Depending
on configuration, the hardware clocks that employees use to clock in and out
for work can be used to enter job transfers, which are when an employee
spends time working outside of their primary job assignment. The clock code is
the number that an employee enters on the clock's number pad when
transferring to that job assignment.

skills, as needed. You can also refresh the populated skills by clicking Refresh skills in the

Headcount
Allocations
Required subsection that includes a list for creating headcount allocations,

allocations as well.
Location
The org unit. When you select an org unit, the job assignment can be worked
at that location and all locations below it in the organizational hierarchy. For
example, you can select the location at the top of your organizational hierarchy
to make the job assignment available at all of your organization's locations.
Note: For a job assignment to be worked at an org unit, the org unit and job
assignment must have the same department defined. Job assignments are
assigned a department in the Department drop-down list.
Effective
From

Compensation Details

A default pay type that is populated when users select this job assignment in

Job Assignment -
Job Description
The job description for the job assignment. For example, you can

Delete Jobs and Job Assignments
In the Jobs and Job Assignments tab of Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments, you can delete
jobs that don’t have any job assignments under them. You can also delete job assignments that
aren’t associated with a work assignment. When you delete a job assignment and click Save,
Dayforce checks if the job assignment is assigned to an active or historical work assignment. If it
is, Dayforce shows an error message indicating that the job assignment is in use and prevents the
save from completing. You can delete a job assignment if you remove it from all work assignments
or delete all of the work assignments that it’s assigned to.
Copy Jobs and Job Assignments
In the Jobs and Job Assignments tab of Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments, you can copy
jobs and job assignments.
When you select a job and click Copy, Dayforce adds a copy of that job under the same job
family. The job assignments under the original job aren’t carried over to the copied job.
When you select a job assignment and click Copy, Dayforce adds a copy of that job assignment
under the same job.
You can’t copy job families in the Jobs and Job Assignments tab.
Workers Comp Setup
In the Workers Comp tab of Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments, you can add workers’ comp
classification codes and assign them to the appropriate jobs. When you do this, these codes are
shown in the read-only Workers Comp section of a job's details in the Jobs and Job Assignments
tab.
The Workers Comp tab is divided into two areas. At the top of the screen, you can add records for
individual classification codes. At the bottom of the screen, there is an area where you can search
for and assign jobs to the code that is selected at the top of the screen.
Configure Workers Comp Codes

-- 469 of 472 --

Dayforce Implementation Guide
Copyright © 2026 Dayforce, Inc. All Rights Reserved 	Page 470 of 0
To add workers’ comp classification codes and assign them to jobs:
1. Go to Org Setup > Jobs and Job Assignments and click the Workers Comp tab.
2. Click Add.
3. Enter a value in the Workers Comp Class Code field.
4. Enter a name and, optionally, a description.
5. Select an option in the State/Province drop-down list.
6. In the Eligible Job(s) section at the bottom of the screen, use the search field to filter the
Available column, then select the jobs that you want to make the code applicable for.
Note: You can press and hold the Ctrl key and select multiple jobs from the list.
7. Click the right arrow icon to move one or more selected jobs to the Selected list.
8. Click Save.

Position Management Configuration
Position Management Overview
You can use Position Management to model and manage your organization hierarchy for business
and workforce planning. You can get accurate, historical, and current views of your employees
and the overall organizational structure. This approach can help you to plan for future talent
needs, find current talent gaps, and budget effectively to meet your business needs.
The first step in setting up Position Management is to create the functional structure of your
organization in Organization Designer. First, you create business units in Organization Designer
> Business Units. Business units form the functional structure of the organization that keeps track
of filled and vacant positions. The business unit hierarchy represents a functional structure that is
separate from actual locations. All of the positions in your organization are associated with a
business unit.
After you have the business unit framework of your organization in place, you can add positions in
Organization Designer > Positions. Each position represents a seat in your organization. Positions
can be filled or vacant, and they drive the organizational structure of your business, including the
management hierarchy and the overall headcount.
The tasks involved with Position Management are:
Create business units and set up the functional (business unit) org structure. See Add
Business Units.
Create positions and set up a position-based management hierarchy. See Add Positions.
Manage the positions in your organization with tasks such as updating position information,
transferring employees between positions, and terminating employees. See Manage
Positions.
Use the Recruiting module together with Position Management to recruit and hire
candidates. See Recruiting with Position Management.
Position Management and Personal Data Management
When an employee's personal information is removed from Dayforce, their name isn’t shown in
any of the Position Management features. The following list shows some of the places in the
Organization Designer > Positions feature where their information is purged or masked:
In the Audit tab of positions.
In the position details when the as of date is set to a time in the past when the employee
occupied a position.
On the Last Modified section of position details.

See Personal Data Management Administration.
Position Management Key Terms
The following terms are important to understand as you use Position Management:
Business Unit
Business units form the functional structure of the organization that keeps track of filled and
vacant positions. The business unit hierarchy represents a functional structure that is separate
from actual locations. All of the positions in your organization are associated with a business unit.
Department
A department is a generic area that can exist across your organization, like Finance, Marketing,
Sales, and HR. Departments are set up in Org Setup > Organization, in the Departments tab.
Job
A job is a general set of duties that employees can perform, such as Analyst, Director,
Coordinator, and Manager. Jobs are grouped based on responsibilities and can usually be
applied to multiple departments. Jobs are assigned a pay grade and are configured in Org Setup
> Jobs and Job Assignments.
Job Assignment
A job assignment is an instance of a job in a specific department. A job assignment combines a
department and a job, and it can be linked to work assignments. Job assignments also have
locations for which they apply. For example, if a Sales Associate job assignment is valid only in the
US, and it’s in the Sales department, then the job assignment applies to any location in the US that
contains a Sales department. Job assignments are configured in Org Setup > Jobs and Job
Assignments.
Location
Locations, also known as sites, represent the places where people are employed. A location can
be a physical building, a collection of buildings, a town, a city, a province or state, or it can be
virtual. Locations are defined in a hierarchy structure and are used to group workers for
scheduling or other purposes. Locations are set up in Org Setup > Organization, in the
Organization tab.
Position
A position is a unique approved headcount (by business unit and job) in the organization.
Positions usually have one employee A position can usually have only one employee occupying it,
